Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Definition of Hajj: Visitation or Intention?
Defines Hajj linguistically and technically, and engages with objections to the definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Hajj, identify its three components, and explain why intention is not part of the definition.

Core Idea
Hajj is visitation of the Kaaba and Arafat at prescribed times; intention is a condition, not a part of the definition.

The chapter on Hajj in Kanz al-Daqaiq opens with a concise definition: 'visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions.' This definition, however, sparked a subtle debate among Hanafi scholars. While some argued that the linguistic meaning of 'hajj' (intending a great one) should be reflected in the technical definition, the matn deliberately omitted intention. In this lesson, we will unpack the definition, examine the linguistic roots, and understand the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the definition verbatim
Recall the exact words from Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'هو زيارة مكان مخصوص في زمان مخصوص بفعل مخصوص' (It is the visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions).
Memorize this phrase; it is the core of the Hanafi definition.
2
Deconstruct the three components
Identify the 'specific place' (the Kaaba and Arafat), the 'specific time' (for tawaf: from dawn on 10th Dhul Hijjah to end of life; for wuquf: from noon on 9th to dawn on 10th), and the 'specific actions' (tawaf and wuquf).
By 'visitation' the author means these two acts.
3
Understand the linguistic meaning
The Arabic root ح-ج-ج means 'to intend a great one,' not absolute intention. The text refutes the idea that hajj is simply 'qasd khas' (specific intention).
The linguistic evolution from 'intending a great one' to 'visitation' for pilgrimage is important.
4
Examine the dispute over intention
Some scholars (e.g., al-Fath) preferred defining Hajj as 'specific intention with added description.' The Hanafi response: the matn omitted intention because it is a condition (shart) of ihram, not part of the definition's focus on visible acts.
The dispute is conceptual with no practical difference.

Source Text

كتاب الحج
لما كان مركباً من المال والبدن وكان واجباً في العمر مرة أخره ولمراعاة ترتيب حديث
(
الصحيحين بني الإسلام على خمس وختم بالحج وفي رواية ختم بالصوم وعليها اعتمد البخاري في تقديم الحج على الصوم وهو في اللغة - بفتح الحاء وكسرها وبهما قرئ في التنزيل - القصد إلى معظم لا مطلق القصد كما ظنه الشارح وجعله كالتيمم وفي الفقه ما ذكره بقوله قوله : (هو زيارة مكان مخصوص في زمان مخصوص بفعل مخصوص) والمراد بالزيارة الطواف ،والوقوف والمراد بالمكان المخصوص البيت الشريف والجبل المسمى بعرفات، والمراد بالزمان المخصوص في الطواف من طلوع الفجر يوم النحر إلى آخر العمر، وفي الوقوف زوال الشمس يوم عرفة إلى طلوع الفجر يوم النحر . وبهذا التقرير ظهر أن الحج اسم لأفعال مخصوصة من الطواف الفرض والوقوف في وقتهما محرماً بنية الحج سابقاً كما سيأتي أن الإحرام شرط واندفع به ما قرره الشارح من فهم كلام المصنف على أنه في الشريعة جعل لقصد خاص مع زيادة وصف فإن المصنف لم يتعرض للقصد وإنما عرفه بالزيارة وهي فعل
كتاب الحج
قوله : (لما كان مركباً الخ) قال الرملي : فيه نظر بل هو عبادة بدنية محضة والمال إنما هو شرط في وجوبه لا أنه مفهومه وأخره عن الصوم لأنه منع النفس شهواتها والحج قد يكون مشتهى لاشتماله على السفر وفيه تفريج الهموم ارجع إلى النهر قوله : (لا) مطلق القصد الخ) قال في من اللغة. وقيده في الفتح بكونه إلى معظم لا مطلقه
النهر : هو مستشهداً بقوله :
لغة القصد كذا
في غير كتاب
وأشهد من عوف حؤولاً كثيرة يحجون سب الزبرقان المزعفرا
أي يقصدونه معظمين إياه. قال ابن السكيت : هذا معناه الأصلي ثم تعورف استعماله في القصد إلى مكة للنسك تقول حججت البيت أحجه حجاً فأنا حاج ا.هـ. قلت: حيث أطلقه أهل اللغة فتقييده بما في الفتح لا بد له من نقل وما استشهد به من البيت لا يدل على أنه لا يستعمل في مطلق القصد لأن غاية ما أفاد أنه استعمل في بعض مدلولاته تأمل قوله : (وبهذا التقرير ظهر أن الحج اسم الخ) هذا ما استظهره في الفتح في تعريفه عادلاً عن تعريفهم إياه بالقصد الخاص لما سيأتي
The Book of Hajj: It is the visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions, obligatory once in a lifetime. The Book of Hajj: Because it is composed of wealth and body, and was obligatory once in a lifetime, it was delayed, and for observing the order of the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Islam is built on five, and it concluded with Hajj'; in another narration it concluded with fasting, and al-Bukhari relied on that in giving precedence to Hajj over fasting. In language – with fatha or kasra on the ha, and both are recited in the Quran – it means intending a great one, not absolute intention as the commentator supposed and made it like tayammum. In fiqh it is what he mentioned: his saying: (It is the visitation of a specific place at a specific time with a specific action). By 'visitation' is meant tawaf and standing (wuquf). By 'specific place' is meant the Noble House (Kaaba) and the mountain called Arafat. By 'specific time' for tawaf is from dawn on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) to the end of one's life; for wuquf, from noon on the day of Arafah to dawn on the day of Nahr. And by this explanation, it is clear that Hajj is a name for specific actions: the obligatory tawaf and standing in their proper times while in ihram with the intention of Hajj beforehand, as will come that ihram is a condition. And thereby is refuted what the commentator concluded from his understanding of the author's words that in Sharia it is made for a specific intention with an added description. For the author did not address intention; rather he defined it by visitation, which is an action. The Book of Hajj: His saying: (Because it is composed, etc.) Al-Ramli said: There is consideration in that; rather it is a purely physical worship, and wealth is only a condition for its obligation, not part of its concept. And he delayed it after fasting because fasting restrains the soul from its desires, while Hajj may be desired because it involves travel and relief from worries – refer to al-Nahr. His saying: (No, not absolute intention, etc.) He said in [explanation of?] the language: And al-Fath restricted it to intending a great one, not absolute. Al-Nahr: he cited as evidence his saying: 'In language, intention is like...' in another book: 'I witness from Awf many substitutes; they perform Hajj to the tribe of Zibriqan al-Muzafir.' i.e., they intend him, magnifying him. Ibn al-Sikkit said: This is its original meaning; then it was customarily used for intending Mecca for pilgrimage. You say: Hajajtu al-bayt ahujjuhu hajjan, so I am a hajj. End quote. I say: Since the language scholars used it unrestrictedly, restricting it to what is in al-Fath must have a transmitted report. And his citing the verse does not prove that it is not used for absolute intention, because the most it shows is that it was used for some of its meanings. Consider his saying: (And by this explanation, it is clear that Hajj is a name, etc.) This is what al-Fath preferred in its definition, departing from their definition of it as 'specific intention' for what will come.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage is the introduction to the chapter on Hajj in al-Bahr al-Raiq. It provides a technical definition of Hajj as 'visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions,' which is obligatory once in a lifetime. The author discusses the linguistic meaning of 'hajj' – it is derived from the root meaning 'to intend a great one,' not just any intention. The commentary then addresses an objection by al-Ramli that Hajj is purely a physical worship and wealth is only a condition for its obligation, not part of its essence. The author defends the definition given by the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) that Hajj is a composite act involving both wealth and body. The passage also refutes the claim that the definition should include a specific intention (qasd khas), arguing that the matn defines it via visitation (ziyarah), not intention. Finally, the author mentions that al-Fath preferred a different definition (specific intention), but the author suggests that the given definition is adequate.

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): Visitation of the Kaaba and Arafat at specified times with specified actions, obligatory once in a lifetime.
الزيارة (al-ziyarah): Here it means tawaf and wuquf (standing at Arafat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the definition of Hajj in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Intending the Kaaba with specific actions.
B) Visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions.
C) Traveling to Mecca for worship.
D) Performing tawaf only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of Hajj as 'visitation of a specific place at a specific time with specific actions' intentionally omits intention, which is treated as a condition rather than part of the definition.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Definition of Hajj: Actions over Intention
Defines Hajj linguistically and technically, emphasizing action-based definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the technical Hanafi definition of Hajj and explain why it is defined by specific actions (Tawaf and Wuquf) rather than by intention.

Core Idea
Hajj is defined by specific actions (Tawaf and Wuquf) at specific times and places, not by a mere intention to go.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author unpacks the technical definition of Hajj. He clarifies that Hajj is not simply 'heading to Makkah with intention' but a composite worship defined by two specific physical acts: Tawaf and standing at Arafah. This action-based definition aligns with how the Hanafi school defines other pillars of Islam (prayer, fasting, zakat) — each is a name for specific actions, not for an intention alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
The passage begins by stating that Hajj is 'fard once.' Hukm level: fard_ayn. This is the foundation — the act is obligatory on every mukallaf who has the means, once in a lifetime.
Fard_ayn means individual obligation; omission without excuse is sinful.
2
Break down the definition components
The author defines Hajj as 'visitation of a specific place at a specific time with a specific action.' Identify each component: place = Ka'bah and Arafah; time = from dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah to end of life for Tawaf, and from noon of 9th to dawn of 10th for Wuquf; action = Tawaf and Wuquf.
Ziyarah here is a technical term for these two acts, not just any visit.
3
Understand the linguistic vs. technical meaning
Linguistically, 'hajj' means heading to a venerated place, not any heading. The commentator's error of equating it to Tayammum is corrected. Technically, it is restricted to the specific acts.
The linguistic meaning includes veneration, which is preserved in the technical definition.
4
Appreciate the Hanafi method of defining ibadaat
The passage compares Hajj to prayer, fasting, and zakat: each is defined by its actions (standing, bowing; abstention; giving). The Hanafis insist that Hajj too must be defined by actions, not by qasd (intention), which is only a condition.
This methodological consistency refutes definitions based on 'specific purpose.'
5
Address the objection about death after Wuquf
If a pilgrim dies after Wuquf but before Tawaf, the Hajj is considered valid. The objection is that both pillars were not performed, so it should not suffice. The Hanafi response: the pilgrim did what was possible; the House is attributed to the act, and death completes the obligation by necessity.
This exception does not change the definition; it is a concession for death.

Source Text

كتاب الحج
هو زيارة مكان مخصوص في زمان مخصوص بفعل مخصوص فرض مرة على
كتاب الحج
لما كان مركباً من المال والبدن وكان واجباً في العمر مرة أخره ولمراعاة ترتيب حديث
(
الصحيحين بني الإسلام على خمس وختم بالحج وفي رواية ختم بالصوم وعليها اعتمد البخاري في تقديم الحج على الصوم وهو في اللغة - بفتح الحاء وكسرها وبهما قرئ في التنزيل - القصد إلى معظم لا مطلق القصد كما ظنه الشارح وجعله كالتيمم وفي الفقه ما ذكره بقوله قوله : (هو زيارة مكان مخصوص في زمان مخصوص بفعل مخصوص) والمراد بالزيارة الطواف ،والوقوف والمراد بالمكان المخصوص البيت الشريف والجبل المسمى بعرفات، والمراد بالزمان المخصوص في الطواف من طلوع الفجر يوم النحر إلى آخر العمر، وفي الوقوف زوال الشمس يوم عرفة إلى طلوع الفجر يوم النحر . وبهذا التقرير ظهر أن الحج اسم لأفعال مخصوصة من الطواف الفرض والوقوف في وقتهما محرماً بنية الحج سابقاً كما سيأتي أن الإحرام شرط واندفع به ما قرره الشارح من فهم كلام المصنف على أنه في الشريعة جعل لقصد خاص مع زيادة وصف فإن المصنف لم يتعرض للقصد وإنما عرفه بالزيارة وهي فعل
كتاب الحج
قوله : (لما كان مركباً الخ) قال الرملي : فيه نظر بل هو عبادة بدنية محضة والمال إنما هو شرط في وجوبه لا أنه مفهومه وأخره عن الصوم لأنه منع النفس شهواتها والحج قد يكون مشتهى لاشتماله على السفر وفيه تفريج الهموم ارجع إلى النهر قوله : (لا) مطلق القصد الخ) قال في من اللغة. وقيده في الفتح بكونه إلى معظم لا مطلقه
النهر : هو مستشهداً بقوله :
لغة القصد كذا
في غير كتاب
وأشهد من عوف حؤولاً كثيرة يحجون سب الزبرقان المزعفرا
أي يقصدونه معظمين إياه. قال ابن السكيت : هذا معناه الأصلي ثم تعورف استعماله في القصد إلى مكة للنسك تقول حججت البيت أحجه حجاً فأنا حاج ا.هـ. قلت: حيث أطلقه أهل اللغة فتقييده بما في الفتح لا بد له من نقل وما استشهد به من البيت لا يدل على أنه لا يستعمل في مطلق القصد لأن غاية ما أفاد أنه استعمل في بعض مدلولاته تأمل قوله : (وبهذا التقرير ظهر أن الحج اسم الخ) هذا ما استظهره في الفتح في تعريفه عادلاً عن تعريفهم إياه بالقصد الخاص لما سيأتي

لا قصد بدليل ما في عمدة الفتاوى : إذا حلف ليزورن فلاناً غداً فذهب ولم يؤذن له يحنث ولو لم يستأذن ورجع يحنث ا.هـ. فلا بد من الذهاب مع الاستئذان، وسلم من بحث المحقق ابن الهمام على المشايخ من أن التعريف بالقصد الخاص تعريف له بشرطه وليوافق تعريف بقية العبادات فإن الصلاة اسم لأفعال مخصوصة هي القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود، والصوم اسم للإمساك الخاص، والزكاة اسم للإيتاء المخصوص فليكن الحج اسماً لأفعال مخصوصة. ولا يراد بالزيارة زيارة البيت فقط فإنه حينئذ يصير الحج اسماً للطواف فقط وليس كذلك فإن ركنه شيئان : الطواف بالبيت والوقوف بعرفة بالشرط السابق ويشكل عليه ما قالوا: إن المأمور بالحج إذا مات بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل طواف الزيارة فإنه يكون مجزئاً بخلاف ما إذا رجع قبله فإنه لا وجود للحج إلا بوجود ركنيه ولم يوجدا فينبغي أن لا يجزئ الأمر، سواء مات المأمور أو رجع، وسببه البيت لأنه يضاف إليه ولهذا لم يتكرر الحج عن وشرائطه ثلاثة : شرائط وجوب وشرائط وجوب أداء ، وشرائط صحة، فالأولى ثمانية على
Book of Hajj. Hajj is the visitation of a specific place at a specific time with a specific action, obligatory once upon the legally responsible person. Since it is composed of wealth and body and is obligatory once in a lifetime, it was delayed [in the order of the pillars of Islam] and to observe the order of the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'Islam is built on five' and it ends with Hajj, and in another narration it ends with fasting, and al-Bukhari relied on this in placing Hajj before fasting. Linguistically (with fatha on the ح or kasra, both readings in the Quran) it means heading towards a venerated place, not absolute heading as the commentator thought and made it like Tayammum. In fiqh it is what he mentioned: 'It is the visitation of a specific place at a specific time with a specific action.' By visitation is meant Tawaf and Wuquf; by the specific place is meant the Noble House and the mountain called Arafat; by the specific time for Tawaf is from dawn of the Day of Sacrifice until the end of one's life, and for Wuquf is from noon of the Day of Arafah until dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. With this rendering it becomes clear that Hajj is a name for specific actions: the obligatory Tawaf and Wuquf in their times while in Ihram with the intention of Hajj previously, as will come that Ihram is a condition, and it repels what the commentator understood from the author's words that in the Shariah it is made for a specific purpose with an added description, for the author did not mention purpose but defined it by visitation, which is an action. His saying: (Since it is composed etc.) al-Ramli said: there is consideration rather it is a purely physical worship, and wealth is only a condition for its obligation, not part of its meaning, and he placed it after fasting because fasting restrains the soul's desires while Hajj may be desired due to travel and includes relief from worries. Refer to al-Nahr. His saying: (not absolute heading etc.) He said in language: and al-Kamal ibn al-Humam restricted it to heading towards a venerated place, not absolute. In al-Nahr: he adduces as evidence the verse: 'And I call to witness the numerous clans of Awf / who perform Hajj to the home of al-Zibriqan al-Muzaf'ar', i.e. they head towards him venerating him. Ibn al-Sikkit said: this is its original meaning, then it became conventionally used for heading to Makkah for rites; you say Hajajtu al-bayta ahujju hajjan, so I am a Hajj. End. I say: since the lexicographers use it unrestrictedly, its restriction as in al-Fath requires transmission, and the verse cited does not prove it is not used for absolute heading because the most it shows is that it is used for some of its meanings. Consider. His saying: (With this rendering it appears that Hajj is a name etc.) This is what was preferred in al-Fath in its definition, deviating from their definition as 'specific purpose' due to what will come. There is no purpose based on the evidence in Umdat al-Fatawa: if one swears to visit so-and-so tomorrow and goes without permission, he breaks his oath; if he does not seek permission and returns, he breaks his oath. End. So going with permission is necessary. And it is safe from the investigation of al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam on the teachers that the definition by specific purpose defines it by its condition, so that it agrees with the definition of other acts of worship: for prayer is a name for specific actions (standing, recitation, bowing, prostration), fasting is a name for specific abstention, Zakat is a name for specific giving, so let Hajj be a name for specific actions. And by visitation is not meant only visiting the House, for then Hajj would become a name only for Tawaf, but that is not the case because its pillars are two: Tawaf of the House and standing at Arafah with the previous condition. And it is objected to by what they said: if the one commanded to perform Hajj dies after standing at Arafah before the Tawaf of Ziyarah, it suffices, unlike if he returns before it, for there is no existence of Hajj without the existence of its two pillars, and they were not both found, so it should not suffice in either case, whether the commanded one dies or returns. The reason is the House because it is ascribed to it, and because of this, Hajj is not repeated on behalf of... And its conditions are three: conditions of obligation, conditions of obligation of performance, and conditions of validity. The first are eight upon the legally responsible person.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of Hajj from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by stating the technical definition: Hajj is the visitation (ziyarah) of a specific place (the Ka'bah and Arafat) at a specific time (the days of Hajj) with specific actions (Tawaf and Wuquf). This is a fard (obligatory) act once in a lifetime upon the mukallaf. The commentary then addresses the linguistic meaning: the word 'hajj' (with variation in vowelization) in Arabic means 'to head towards a venerated place', not just any heading. The commentator al-Sharh is criticized for equating it to tayammum. The commentary then unpacks the definition, explaining that 'visitation' here means Tawaf and Wuquf, and the specific times for each. This interpretation shows that Hajj is a name for specific actions, not a specific purpose (qasd). The commentary defends this by comparing with other acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat) which are defined by actions. It also addresses a potential objection: if someone dies after Wuquf but before Tawaf, why is it valid? The response is that the pilgrim has done what he could. The passage ends by introducing the three categories of conditions (obligation, performance, validity) and begins listing the first category (eight conditions).

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): Visitation of specific places (Ka'bah and Arafat) at specific times with specific actions (Tawaf and Wuquf), obligatory once in a lifetime.
زيارة (ziyarah): In this context, it means the specific actions of Tawaf and Wuquf, not merely visiting the House.
القصد الخاص (al-qasd al-khas): The specific intention or purpose to perform Hajj, which some scholars included in the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what does 'ziyarah' (visitation) in the definition of Hajj refer to?
A) Simply going to the Ka'bah
B) Tawaf and standing at Arafah
C) Visiting the Prophet's Mosque in Madinah
D) Circumambulating the Ka'bah only

Key Takeaway
Hajj is defined by its constituent actions (Tawaf and Wuquf) at specified times and places, obligatory once in a lifetime.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

The Three Categories of Conditions for Hajj
Introduces the three categories of conditions for Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of conditions for Hajj in the Hanafi school and explain the difference between conditions of obligation, conditions of obligation of performance, and conditions of validity.

Core Idea
Hajj has three types of conditions: obligation, performance, and validity — each with distinct legal consequences.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author structures the discussion around three distinct categories of conditions for Hajj. Recognizing this classification is essential because it determines when Hajj becomes obligatory, when it must be performed, and when it is valid. The first category, conditions of obligation, is noted to include eight specific conditions, which will be detailed later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Locate the sentence: 'وشرائطه ثلاثة : شرائط وجوب وشرائط وجوب أداء ، وشرائط صحة'. Note the three types: conditions of obligation, conditions of obligation of performance, and conditions of validity.
These categories are sequential: first, conditions that make Hajj wajib (obligatory) at all; second, conditions that make the performance of that obligation immediate; third, conditions that make the performed Hajj valid.
2
Define each category
For 'شرائط وجوب': these are prerequisites that make Hajj fard on a person (e.g., being Muslim, sane, adult, free, able). For 'شرائط وجوب أداء': additional prerequisites for the obligation to be due immediately (e.g., no barrier like illness or inability). For 'شرائط صحة': prerequisites for the Hajj itself to be acceptable (e.g., proper Ihram, correct rituals).
Hanafis differentiate between obligation (wujoob) and performance (ada') - e.g., a child may be able to perform Hajj but it is not obligatory until puberty.
3
Note the count for the first category
The author states 'فالأولى ثمانية' (the first are eight). This refers to the well-known eight conditions that must exist for Hajj to be obligatory. Although they are not explicitly listed here, later scholars have enumerated them.
The eight conditions are: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, health, sufficient provision, safe route, and the availability of a mahram for women (according to some).
4
Recognize the fourth category added by later scholars
The passage mentions that Allamah al-Sindi added a fourth type: conditions for Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj (shurut wuqoo' al-Hajj an al-fard). These include nine conditions such as continuance of Islam until death, not intending supererogatory, not committing invalidating acts, etc.
This fourth category overlaps with the first but focuses on the validity of the performed Hajj as fulfilling the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرائطه ثلاثة : شرائط وجوب وشرائط وجوب أداء ، وشرائط صحة، فالأولى ثمانية على
المكلف،
من البحث والموافقته تعريف بقية العبادات، لكن قال في النهر : تخريج كلام المصنف عليه فيه بحث إذ بتقدير يكون قوله بفعل مخصوص حشواً إذ المراد به كما قالوا هو الطواف والوقوف على أن الجار والمجرور متعلق بزيارة وإذا فسرت بالفعل آل المعنى إلى أنه فعل بفعل وفساده لا يخفى. ويمكن أن يقال : المراد به الإحرام وبه يصير الثاني غير الأول وفسروا الزمان المخصوص بأشهر الحج وهو الذي ينبغي إذ الوقوف الذي هو أقوى أركانه مقيد به قوله : ( على أنه في الشريعة) أي حاملاً له أي لكلام المصنف على أنه الخ. قوله : (وليوافق) كأنه عطف على معنى ما تقدم أي قررت كلام المصنف بكذا لما وليوافق مر قوله: (فليكن الحج الخ) أقول : قد يقال إن المشايخ ذكروا لفظ القصد الخاص وقالوا مع زيادة وصف لأن الحج في اللغة القصد ولا بد في الغالب أن يكون المعنى اللغوي موجوداً في المعاني الاصطلاحية، والاصطلاحي أخص فلذا ذكروا اللفظ اللغوي وقيدوه بالشروط الشرعية ليكون أخص وليس غيره من العبادات المذكورة مأخوذاً في معناه النية أو القصد، ولذا عرفوا التيمم بأنه القصد إلى صعيد مطهر فتأمل قوله : ويشكل عليه ما قالوا الخ يمكن الجواب بأن الموت من قبل من له الحق وقد أتى بوسعه من ركن أو ركنين أن عد الإحرام ركناً وقد ورد «الحج عرفة» بخلاف من رجع . في شرح المقدسي قوله : (وشرائطه ثلاثة الخ) زاد العلامة السندي تلميذ العلامة ابن الهمام في منسكه المتوسط المسمى الباب المناسك قسماً رابعاً وهو شرائط وقوع الحج عن الفرض وهي تسعة: الإسلام وبقاؤه إلى الموت والعقل والحرية والبلوغ والأداء بنفسه إن قدر، وعدم نية النفل وعدم الإفساد وعدم النية عن الغير فلا يقع حج الكافر عن الفرض ولا عن النفل إذا أسلم ولا المسلم إذا ارتد بعد الحج وإن تاب ولا المجنون والصبي والعبد وإن أفاق وبلغ وعتق بعده، ولا بأداء الغير قبل العذر ولا بنية الفل أو عن الغير أو مع الفساد فهؤلاء لو حجوا ولو بعد
كذا
And its conditions are three: conditions of obligation, conditions of obligation of performance, and conditions of validity. The first are eight upon the legally responsible person... from research and agreeing with the definition of other acts of worship. But in al-Nahr it is said: deriving the author's words upon it has consideration, for if it is considered, his phrase 'with a specific action' would be redundant because as they said the intended meaning is Tawaf and Wuquf, while the prepositional phrase is attached to 'visitation', and if it is interpreted as action, the meaning becomes 'he does an action with an action' and its corruption is obvious. And it can be said: what is intended by it is Ihram, and thereby the second becomes different from the first, and they interpret the specific time as the months of Hajj, which is appropriate since Wuquf, which is the strongest of its pillars, is tied to it. His saying: 'That in the Shariah' meaning carrying his words i.e. the author's words to the effect that... His saying: 'And to agree' it is as if coordinated with the meaning of what preceded, i.e. I rendered the author's words in such a way to agree with... His saying: 'So let Hajj be...' I say: it may be said that the teachers mentioned the term 'specific purpose' and said with an added description because Hajj in language is purpose, and necessarily the linguistic meaning is usually present in technical meanings, and the technical is more specific, so they mentioned the linguistic term and restricted it with Shar'i conditions to make it more specific, and unlike the other acts of worship mentioned which include intention or purpose in their meaning; therefore they defined Tayammum as 'heading towards pure earth'. So consider. His saying: 'And it is objected by what they said...' The answer can be that death is from the One who has the right, and he has performed what he could of one or two pillars, if Ihram is considered a pillar, and it has been reported 'Hajj is Arafah', unlike the one who returns. In Sharh al-Maqdisi: His saying: 'And its conditions are three...' Allamah al-Sindi, the student of Allamah Ibn al-Humam, added in his medium-sized manasik called Bab al-Manask a fourth type: conditions for Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj, which are nine: Islam, remaining in it until death, intellect, freedom, puberty, performing it oneself if able, not intending supererogatory, not invalidating it, and not intending it on behalf of another. Thus the Hajj of a disbeliever does not count as obligatory nor as supererogatory if he becomes Muslim; nor of a Muslim who apostatizes after Hajj even if he repents; nor of an insane person, a boy, or a slave even if they become sane, reach puberty, or become free afterwards; nor by the performance of another without an excuse; nor with the intention of the obligatory? or on behalf of another, or with invalidation. So these, if they perform Hajj, even after... such.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the definition of Hajj and then lists the conditions. The author states that Hajj has three types of conditions: (1) conditions for obligation (shurut wujoob) – these are eight things that must exist for Hajj to be obligatory; (2) conditions for obligation of performance (shurut wujoob ada’) – additional conditions for the obligation to actually perform it; (3) conditions for validity (shurut sihha) – conditions for Hajj to be valid. The text notes that a fourth category has been added by later scholars: conditions for Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj (i.e. to fulfill the fard obligation), which include Islam, remaining Muslim until death, sanity, freedom, puberty, performing it oneself if able, not intending supererogatory, not invalidating it, and not performing it on behalf of another. Thus, the Hajj of a disbeliever does not fulfill the obligation, nor does the Hajj of a Muslim who apostatizes even if he later repents, nor of an insane person, a child, or a slave, even if they later become sane, reach puberty, or become free. Also, if someone performs Hajj on behalf of another without a valid excuse, or performs Hajj with the intention of supererogatory when obligated, or invalidates it, the Hajj does not count. The passage ends abruptly, indicating more detail to follow.

Key Terms
شرائط وجوب (shurut wujoob): Conditions that make Hajj obligatory upon a person, such as being Muslim, sane, adult, free, and able.
شرائط وجوب أداء (shurut wujoob ada'): Conditions that make the performance of Hajj immediately obligatory, such as physical and financial ability and safety of route.
شرائط صحة (shurut sihha): Conditions for the validity of Hajj, such as being in Ihram with proper intention, performing rituals correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many categories of conditions for Hajj are mentioned at the beginning of the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Hajj has three primary categories of conditions: obligation, performance, and validity, with a fourth later category for counting as the obligatory Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

8 min
Conditions for Hajj to Count as Obligatory (Shurut al-Wujoob and the Fourth Category)
Lists the conditions for Hajj to be obligatory and the added fourth category for it to count as obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions of obligation for Hajj and the nine conditions for Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj, and apply them to identify when a performed Hajj fulfills the fard.

Core Idea
For Hajj to fulfill the Islamic obligation, it must be performed under conditions that ensure it counts, not just that it is valid.

While the earlier classification introduced three categories, the text delves into the first category (conditions of obligation) and adds a crucial fourth category: conditions for the performed Hajj to actually count as the obligatory Hajj. This lesson unpacks these conditions, including the list from Allamah al-Sindi, and clarifies why some acts of Hajj, though valid, do not discharge the one-time obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight conditions of obligation
Although the passage does not list them explicitly, standard Hanafi sources state the eight conditions: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, health, sufficient provision, safe route, and (for women) availability of a mahram. The text refers to 'الأولى ثمانية' (the first are eight).
These conditions must exist at the time of obligation; if any is missing, Hajj is not fard.
2
Recognize the fourth category from al-Sindi
Allamah al-Sindi added a fourth category: 'شرائط وقوع الحج عن الفرض' (conditions for Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj). He lists nine conditions: Islam and remaining Muslim until death, intellect, freedom, puberty, performing oneself if able, not intending supererogatory, not invalidating it, not performing on behalf of another without excuse.
These overlap with the first category but emphasize the continuity of the conditions throughout the Hajj act.
3
Apply to specific cases
The text gives examples: the Hajj of a disbeliever does not count even if he later becomes Muslim; the Hajj of a Muslim who apostatizes after Hajj does not count; the Hajj of an insane person, child, or slave does not count even if they later become sane, adult, or free.
This shows that the conditions must be present at the time of performance and that the person must remain eligible until completion.
4
Distinguish from conditions of validity
Validity conditions (e.g., proper Ihram, correct sequence) are about the act itself. The fourth category is about the legal status of the act as fulfilling the obligation. A valid Hajj may still not count as the obligatory Hajj if, e.g., the person intended supererogatory while obligated.
Thus, a person who performs a valid Hajj but with the intention of nafl while being obligated will not fulfill the fard.

Key Terms
شرائط وقوع الحج عن الفرض (shurut wuqoo' al-hajj 'an al-fard): Conditions for the Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj (fulfilling the fard).
عدم نية النفل ('adam niyyat al-nafl): Not intending the supererogatory (i.e., one must intend the obligatory Hajj specifically).
الأولى ثمانية (al-ula thamaniyah): The first category (conditions of obligation) consists of eight conditions.

Definition of Hajj: Why Intention Is Not Part of the Definition
Critique and defense of the definition of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Hajj and explain why the term 'specific intention' (al-qasd al-khas) is not part of the definition.

Core Idea
Hajj is a name for specific actions, not for intention.

In this passage, the commentator defends the definition of Hajj as 'visiting the House' against the criticism that it lacks the condition of intention. He argues that intention is a condition, not part of the essential definition, and that Hajj, like other acts of worship, is defined by its specific actions: tawaf and wuquf. We will work through the critique and the response to understand the precise Hanafi definition.

Guided Path
1
State the debated definition
Identify the original definition of Hajj as 'ziyarah al-bayt' and the proposed addition of 'qasd al-khas' by some scholars.
2
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's critique
Explain why using 'specific intention' defines Hajj by its condition rather than its essence. The condition is separate from what is defined.
3
Compare to other ibadat
Show that prayer, fasting, and zakat are defined by specific actions, so Hajj should be similarly defined by its pillars: tawaf and wuquf.
4
Address the objection about death after wuquf
Resolve the apparent inconsistency: a pilgrim who dies after wuquf but before tawaf is valid because the hadith 'Hajj is Arafah' establishes wuquf as the primary pillar, and the deceased is excused.
The hadith is evidence that wuquf is the essence of Hajj.
5
Conclude the refined definition
State the correct Hanafi definition: Hajj is the performance of specific actions (tawaf and wuquf) with the proper conditions, not merely an intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وليوافق) كأنه عطف على معنى ما تقدم أي قررت كلام المصنف بكذا لما وليوافق مر قوله: (فليكن الحج الخ) أقول : قد يقال إن المشايخ ذكروا لفظ القصد الخاص وقالوا مع زيادة وصف لأن الحج في اللغة القصد ولا بد في الغالب أن يكون المعنى اللغوي موجوداً في المعاني الاصطلاحية، والاصطلاحي أخص فلذا ذكروا اللفظ اللغوي وقيدوه بالشروط الشرعية ليكون أخص وليس غيره من العبادات المذكورة مأخوذاً في معناه النية أو القصد، ولذا عرفوا التيمم بأنه القصد إلى صعيد مطهر فتأمل قوله : ويشكل عليه ما قالوا الخ يمكن الجواب بأن الموت من قبل من له الحق وقد أتى بوسعه من ركن أو ركنين أن عد الإحرام ركناً وقد ورد «الحج عرفة» بخلاف من رجع . في شرح المقدسي
The book of Hajj: No intention (qasd) is needed, as evidenced by what is in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If someone swore to visit so-and-so tomorrow and went without permission, he breaks his oath; and if he did not seek permission and returned, he also breaks his oath. Thus, going with permission is necessary. Ibn al-Humam refuted the earlier scholars' objection that the definition of Hajj with 'specific intention' defines it by its condition, and to match the definitions of other acts of worship, for prayer is a name for specific actions: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration; fasting is a name for specific abstinence; zakat is a name for specific giving; so Hajj should be a name for specific actions. The intended meaning of 'visitation' is not merely visiting the House, for then Hajj would be a name for tawaf only, which is not the case, as its pillars are two: tawaf of the House and standing at Arafah, with the previous condition. There is an objection: if the one commanded to perform Hajj dies after standing at Arafah but before tawaf al-ziyarah, his Hajj is valid, unlike if he returns before it, for Hajj only exists with both pillars; if they are not present, it should not be valid whether the person dies or returns. Its cause is the House, because it is attributed to it; for this reason, Hajj is not repeated for one who owes it. Its conditions are three: conditions of obligation, conditions of obligation of performance, and conditions of validity. The first type is eight according to... (the passage continues with the critique of the definition from al-Nahr and the response).
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a definition and critique of the definition of Hajj. The commentator begins by critiquing the matn's (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) definition of Hajj as 'ziyarah al-bayt' (visiting the House) with a condition of 'qasd' (intention). He defends the author by explaining that the definition must imply specific actions (tawaf and wuquf) to parallel definitions of other ibadat. He addresses an objection about a pilgrim who dies after wuquf but before tawaf: the Hajj is valid because the right is with Allah, and the person did their best; the hadith 'Hajj is Arafah' supports this. The passage also discusses the interpretation of the author's wording and concludes that the preferred definition includes the pillars.

Key Terms
زيارة البيت (ziyarah al-bayt): Visiting the Sacred House in Mecca, the literal definition of Hajj.
القصد الخاص (al-qasd al-khas): Specific intention, used by some scholars to define Hajj but criticized here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, how does the definition of Hajj compare to other acts of worship like prayer and fasting?
A) Hajj is defined by intention, unlike prayer.
B) Hajj, like prayer and fasting, is a name for specific actions.
C) Hajj is unique in that it requires no specific actions.
D) The definition of Hajj is purely linguistic, not legal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of Hajj focuses on the specific actions of tawaf and wuquf, not on intention.

The Eight Conditions for Hajj Obligation
Enumeration and explanation of eight conditions for Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight shurut al-wujub of Hajj and explain why the author of Kanz omitted Islam and knowledge, and how knowledge is established for Muslims in Dar al-Islam and Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
Hajj becomes obligatory only when eight conditions are met; the first (Islam) and last (knowledge) are inherent in every worship.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists the eight conditions that must be present for Hajj to become obligatory. The author of Kanz omitted two (Islam and knowledge) because they are general conditions for all acts of worship. The commentator defends this omission and clarifies how knowledge of the obligation is presumed for Muslims in Dar al-Islam but requires testimony in Dar al-Harb. Understanding these conditions helps us determine when Hajj becomes a personal duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight conditions
Read the text carefully and list the eight conditions mentioned in the most correct view. Notice that the author of Kanz mentioned only six, omitting Islam and knowledge.
The eight are: Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time, ability for provisions, ability for a mount, and knowledge that Hajj is obligatory.
2
Understand the omission of Islam and knowledge
The commentator explains that Islam and knowledge are conditions for every act of worship, so the author of Kanz omitted them as a general rule. Recognize that their omission is not an error but a methodological choice.
3
Analyze how knowledge is established
For a person in Dar al-Islam, knowledge is presumed (constructive knowledge) simply by being present, regardless of actual awareness. For a person in Dar al-Harb, knowledge is established by testimony: the report of two men, or one man and two women (even if of unknown reliability), or one just person. Note the difference of opinion (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not require 'adalah).
This shows how the school handles evidence for knowledge in different territories.
4
Note the scope of conditions
The conditions of puberty and freedom are not unique to Hajj; they apply to other obligations as well, such as the five daily prayers (in terms of puberty) and other acts. The text mentions 'its five similar cases'—referring to other pillars of Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصح : الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد والقدرة على الراحلة والعلم بكون الحج فرضاً، وقد ذكر المصنف منها ستة وترك الأول والأخير والعذر له كغيره أنهما شرطان لكل عبادة، وقد يقال كذلك العقل والبلوغ والعلم المذكور يثبت لمن في دار الإسلام بمجرد الوجود فيها سواء علم بالفرضية أو لم يعلم ولا فرق في ذلك أن بين يكون نشأ على الإسلام فيها أو لا فيكون ذلك علماً حكيماً، ولمن في دار الحرب بإخبار رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين ولو مستورين أو واحد ،عدل وعندهما لا تشترط العدالة والبلوغ والحرية فيه وفي نظائره الخمسة كما عرف أصولاً وفروعاً
The most correct view: Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time, ability to obtain provisions, ability to obtain a mount, and knowledge that Hajj is obligatory. The author (of Kanz) mentioned six of them and omitted the first and the last, and his excuse is that these two are conditions for every act of worship. It may also be said that intellect and puberty are likewise. The mentioned knowledge is established for one who is in Dar al-Islam simply by being present there, whether he knows of the obligation or not; it makes no difference whether he was raised in Islam there or not, for that counts as constructive knowledge. For one in Dar al-Harb, it is established by the report of two men or one man and two women, even if of unknown reliability, or one just person. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), justice is not required. Puberty and freedom are conditions in this and its five similar cases, as known in principles and branches.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage lists the eight conditions for Hajj to be obligatory (shurut al-wujub). The correct view includes Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time (the months of Hajj or departure time), ability to obtain provisions, ability to obtain a mount, and knowledge that Hajj is an obligation. The author of Kanz omitted Islam and knowledge, but the commentator defends him because these are general conditions for all ibadat. The commentator then discusses how knowledge is presumed for Muslims in Dar al-Islam but requires testimony in Dar al-Harb. The conditions of puberty and freedom are also discussed in similar contexts.

Key Terms
شرائط الوجوب (shurut al-wujub): Conditions that must be present for Hajj to become obligatory.
دار الإسلام (Dar al-Islam): Territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law is applied.
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory not under Muslim rule, considered hostile.
علم حكمي (ilm hukmi): Constructive knowledge: a legal presumption of knowledge based on circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) are listed in the most correct view?
A) Six
B) Seven
C) Eight
D) Nine

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Hajj depends on eight conditions; two are general to all worship, and knowledge can be constructive in Dar al-Islam.

The Time Condition in Hajj: Obligation or Performance
Enumerating conditions and dissecting the time condition dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on whether time is a condition for wujub or ada' of Hajj, identify the proponents, and apply the practical difference regarding the obligation of making a will.

Core Idea
Time is a condition for obligation, not just performance — the obligation arises only when the Hajj months enter.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about the nature of time as a condition for Hajj. The passage first enumerates the conditions for performance and validity, then focuses on the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Zufar on the other. The practical consequence concerns whether a person who becomes capable before the Hajj time must make a will if death seems imminent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of conditions
The passage lists five conditions for obligation of performance (shurut wujub al-ada') and four conditions for validity (shurut al-sihha). Note that time appears in both lists according to the relied-upon view.
The five for wujub al-ada' are: sound body, removal of obstacles, safe route, no 'iddah, mahram. The four for validity are: ihram, time, place, Islam.
2
Locate the disputed point
The debate centers on whether 'time' (the months of Hajj) is a condition for the very obligation of Hajj becoming due, or only for its valid performance once the obligation exists.
The disagreement is between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (time as condition for wujub) and Zufar (time as condition for ada').
3
Examine the proof for the Hanafi position
If a person owns the provision and mount before the time, he may spend them elsewhere. If he owns them during the time, he must reserve them for Hajj. This shows the obligation is tied to the arrival of time.
The proof is based on the permissible use of wealth before the time.
4
Understand Zufar's counterproof
Zufar argues that if a person fears death before the time, some scholars say he must make a will for Hajj, indicating the obligation was already established before the time.
The Hanafi response is that such a will is valid not because the obligation was due, but because the person is 'ahl al-wujub' (a potential obligee).
5
Apply the tarjih
Ibn al-Humam preferred the view that time is a condition for wujub, making this the mufta bihi position. The practical fruit (thamarah) is the obligation of a will: according to the relied view, no will is obligatory before the time.
The will's validity (if made) is accepted by all, but obligation differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانية خمسة على الأصح : صحة البدن وزوال الموانع الحسية عن الذهاب إلى الحج وأمن الطريق وعدم قيام العدة في حق المرأة وخروج الزوج أو المحرم معها . والثالثة أعني شرائط الصحة أربعة : الإحرام بالحج والوقت المخصوص والمكان المخصوص والإسلام ومنهم من ذكر بدل الإحرام النية ، وهذا أولى لاستلزامه النية وغيرها . وواجباته أعني التي يلزم بترك واحد منها دم إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات. ومد الوقوف بعرفة
أو
الاستطاعة لا يسقط عنهم الفرض ويجب عليهم ثانياً إذا استطاعوا ا هـ قوله : (والوقت) قال الرملي : سيذكره أيضاً في شرائط الصحة، ولا شك أن من لم يدرك وقت الحج لم يجب عليه وأنه لا يصح إلا في وقته المخصوص فكان شرطاً للوجوب وشرطاً للصحة تأمل ا هـ . وفي «لباب المناسك»: السابع الوقت وهو أشهر الحج أو وقت خروج أهل بلده إن كانوا يخرجون قبلها فلا يجب إلا على القادر فيها أو في وقت خروجهم فإن ملكه أي المال قبل الوقت فله صرفه حيث شاء ولا حج عليه، وإن ملكه فيه فليس له صرفه إلى غير الحج فلو صرف رفه لم يسقط الوجوب عنه، ولو أسلم كافراً وبلغ صبي أفاق مجنون أو عتق عبد قبل الوقت فخافوا الموت وهم موسرون ؛ قيل ليس عليهم الإيصاء بالحج. وقيل يجب، فإن أوصوا به فعلى الأولى لا يصح، وصح على الثاني، والخلاف مبني على أن الوقت شرط الوجوب أو الأداء قولان ا.هـ. قال شارحه ملا علي : هما روايتان عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وزفر، ورجح ابن الهمام القول بأنه شرط الوجوب، ونسب صاحب المجمع صحة الإيصاء إلى الإمام وصاحبه وخلافها إلى زفر معللاً بأنهم كانوا أهل الوجوب وقت الوصية فيصح إيصاؤهم بأن يحج عنهم في وقته لعجزهم عنه، ويؤيده ما في الخانية : لو بلغ الصبي فحضره الوفاة وأوصى بأن يحج عنه حجة الإسلام جازت وصيته عندنا ويحج فجعل المذهب الجواز وهو لا ينافي جعل الوقت من شرائط الوجوب على المشهور المرجح خلاف ما فهم المصنف وبنى عليه صحة الإيصاء وعدمها ا هـ . قلت: فعلى هذا فثمرة الخلاف في أن الوقت شرط للوجوب أو للأداء لا تظهر في صحة الوصية وعدمها وإنما تظهر في وجوب الإيصاء أو الإحجاج عنه وعدم ذلك فلا يجب على المشهور ويجب على خلافه تأمل قوله : (وقد يقال كذلك العقل والبلوغ أي أنهما شرطان لكل عبادة قوله : (وخروج الزوج والمحرم معها قال الرملي وفي البدائع والأصح أنه أي المحرم شرط الوجوب ا هـ . فقد
The second type is five conditions according to the most correct view: soundness of body, removal of physical obstacles to travel to Hajj, safety of the road, absence of the waiting period ('iddah) for a woman, and the exit of the husband or mahram with her. The third type, meaning conditions of validity, are four: assumption of ihram for Hajj, the specific time (months of Hajj), the specific place (Mecca and Arafat), and Islam. Some mention intention instead of ihram, and this is better because it necessitates intention and other things. Its obligations (wajibat) are those for which omission of any one requires a dam (blood sacrifice): initiating ihram from the miqat, and [prolonged] standing at Arafah. (The text continues with the quote from Lubab al-Manasik about time and the dispute). He said: (And time) al-Ramli said: He will also mention it in conditions of validity. There is no doubt that whoever does not reach the time of Hajj is not obligated, and it is valid only in its specific time, so it is both a condition for obligation and for validity. In Lubab al-Manasik: The seventh [condition] is time, which is the months of Hajj or the time of his people's departure if they depart before them. If one owns the wealth before the time, he may spend it as he wishes; if he owns it within the time, he may not spend it on other than Hajj. If a non-Muslim converts to Islam, a boy reaches puberty, a madman regains sanity, or a slave is freed before the time, and they fear death while being able, there is a saying that they are not required to make a will; another saying says they must. If they do make a will, according to the first view it is not valid; according to the second it is valid. The dispute is based on whether time is a condition for obligation or for performance. The commentator Mulla Ali says: These are two narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar. Ibn al-Humam preferred the view that it is a condition for obligation. The author of al-Majma' attributed the validity of the will to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his two companions, and its invalidity to Zufar. This is supported by what is in al-Khaniyya: If a boy reaches puberty and is at death's door and makes a will that Hajj al-Islam be performed for him, his will is valid according to us, and Hajj is performed. Thus the madhhab is validity, which does not contradict making time a condition for obligation according to the preferred popular view, contrary to what the author understood and built upon regarding the validity of the will. I (the author of al-Bahr) say: The fruit of the dispute is not in the validity of the will but in the obligation of making a will or having Hajj performed for him. According to the popular view, it is not obligatory; according to the other view, it is. Consider.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage covers the remaining two types of conditions: conditions for obligation of performance (shurut wujub al-ada') and conditions for validity (shurut al-sihha). The five conditions for performance are: sound body, removal of physical obstacles, safe route, no 'iddah for women, and presence of a husband or mahram. The four conditions for validity are: ihram, specific time (months of Hajj), specific place (Mecca/Arafat), and Islam. Then the passage dives into an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether time is a condition for obligation (wujub) or for performance (ada'). This dispute affects the ruling on making a will (wasiyya) for Hajj. According to the relied-upon view (time as condition for obligation), a person who becomes capable before the time is not immediately obligated. The commentator analyzes the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar, and concludes that the practical difference is whether one must make a will to have Hajj performed after death if they die before performing it.

Key Terms
شرائط وجوب الأداء (shurut wujub al-ada'): Conditions that must be present for the performance of Hajj to be obligatory once the basic obligation is established.
شرائط الصحة (shurut al-sihha): Conditions that must be present for Hajj to be valid.
الوقت (al-waqt): The specific time for Hajj, i.e., the months of Shawwal, Dhul-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, or the departure time of one's people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory.
C) It is not required; the will, if made, is valid.
D) It is invalid to make such a will.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon view holds time as a condition for obligation, meaning no will for Hajj is required before the Hajj months.

The Three Categories of Conditions for Hajj
Enumerates the three categories of conditions for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of conditions for Hajj and identify which conditions belong to each category according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Hajj's obligation, performance, and validity each depend on distinct sets of conditions.

The Hanafi school classifies the conditions of Hajj into three categories: conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub), conditions of performance (shurut al-ada'), and conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha). This lesson unpacks each category based on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, clarifying key intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The text explicitly names shurut al-wujub, shurut al-ada', and shurut al-sihha. Note the number of conditions in each: 8 (correct position), 5, and 4 respectively.
The author of Kanz omitted Islam and knowledge from the first category because they are common to all acts of worship.
2
Analyse shurut al-wujub
List the eight conditions: Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time (Hajj months), ability (zad and rahila), and knowledge of obligation. Understand how knowledge is established for a Muslim in Dar al-Islam versus a non-Muslim in Dar al-Harb.
For Dar al-Harb, testimony of two men or one man and two women suffices; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not require the witnesses to be just ('adl).
3
Analyse shurut al-ada'
These five conditions enable actual performance: physical health, removal of physical obstacles, safety of the road, no 'idda for women, and presence of husband or mahram.
These ensure the person can physically and legally undertake the journey.
4
Analyse shurut al-sihha
The four conditions for validity: ihram (or intention), specific time (Dhul-Hijjah), specific place (the Haram), and Islam. Note that some scholars prefer 'intention' over 'ihram' because it inherently includes intention and other elements.
Intention (niyyah) is central to all acts of worship.
5
Review the intra-Hanafi variant
Note that for the condition of knowledge in Dar al-Harb, Imam Abu Hanifa requires a single just witness, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept even obscure witnesses without requiring justice.
This is a minor ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصح : الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد والقدرة على الراحلة والعلم بكون الحج فرضاً، وقد ذكر المصنف منها ستة وترك الأول والأخير والعذر له كغيره أنهما شرطان لكل عبادة، وقد يقال كذلك العقل والبلوغ والعلم المذكور يثبت لمن في دار الإسلام بمجرد الوجود فيها سواء علم بالفرضية أو لم يعلم ولا فرق في ذلك أن بين يكون نشأ على الإسلام فيها أو لا فيكون ذلك علماً حكيماً، ولمن في دار الحرب بإخبار رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين ولو مستورين أو واحد ،عدل وعندهما لا تشترط العدالة والبلوغ والحرية فيه وفي نظائره الخمسة كما عرف أصولاً وفروعاً، والثانية خمسة على الأصح : صحة البدن وزوال الموانع الحسية عن الذهاب إلى الحج وأمن الطريق وعدم قيام العدة في حق المرأة وخروج الزوج أو المحرم معها . والثالثة أعني شرائط الصحة أربعة : الإحرام بالحج والوقت المخصوص والمكان المخصوص والإسلام ومنهم من ذكر بدل الإحرام النية ، وهذا أولى لاستلزامه النية وغيرها.
The correct position: Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time, ability to provision, ability to mount (means of transport), and knowledge that Hajj is an obligation. The author mentioned six of these and omitted the first and last, due to the excuse that they are conditions for every act of worship. It may also be said similarly for intellect and puberty. The mentioned knowledge is established for one in Dar al-Islam by mere existence therein, whether he knows the obligation or not, and there is no difference whether he grew up in Islam therein or not, so that constitutes effective knowledge. For one in Dar al-Harb, knowledge is established by the report of two men, or one man and two women, even if they are obscure, or one just person, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) justice is not required. Puberty and freedom are in that and its five analogues as known in principles and branches. The second category: five according to the correct position: physical health, removal of physical obstacles to going to Hajj, safety of the road, absence of waiting period ('idda) for women, and the husband or mahram accompanying her. The third category, i.e. conditions of validity, are four: entering ihram for Hajj, the specific time, the specific place, and Islam. Some mention intention instead of ihram, and this is better because it necessitates intention and other things.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the conditions of Hajj as per the Hanafi school. It lists three categories: conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub), conditions of performance (shurut al-ada'), and conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha). The first category includes eight items as per al-Asahh: Islam, intellect, puberty, freedom, time, ability to provision, ability to mount, and knowledge of the obligation. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq omitted the first and last because they are common to all acts of worship. Knowledge of Hajj being fard is established for a Muslim in Dar al-Islam just by living there, but for a non-Muslim in Dar al-Harb, it requires testimony of two men or one man and two women. The second category (shurut al-ada') includes five: physical health, removal of obstacles, safe road, no 'idda for women, and presence of husband or mahram. The third category (shurut al-sihha) includes: ihram, specific time, specific place, and Islam, with intention recommended as a substitute for ihram. This reflects the Hanafi systematic approach to classifying acts of worship.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istitā‘ah): Ability to perform Hajj: having provisions (zad) and a mount (rahila) beyond one's basic needs.
محرم (maḥram): A male relative whom a woman cannot marry, e.g., father, brother, son.
عدة (‘idda): Waiting period after divorce or death of husband during which a woman cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many conditions of performance (shurut al-ada') are listed?
A) 4
B) 5
C) 6
D) 8

Key Takeaway
Hajj has three distinct sets of conditions: obligation (shurut al-wujub), performance (shurut al-ada'), and validity (shurut al-sihha); each set must be satisfied for the act to be required, possible, and accepted.

Time as a Condition for Hajj: Obligation or Performance?
Analyzes whether time is a condition for obligation or performance of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on whether time is a condition for the obligation or performance of Hajj and apply the practical consequence regarding bequest.

Core Idea
Within the Hanafi school, time's role in Hajj—condition for obligation or performance—affects the obligation to bequeath Hajj.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: is the specific time of Hajj a condition for the obligation to perform Hajj or merely a condition for its valid performance? The answer has practical implications, especially for those who become able just before the season ends and fear death. Understanding this distinction deepens your grasp of how conditions shape obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position(s)
Identify the two views within the Hanafi school: time as a condition for obligation (wujub) vs. time as a condition for performance (ada'). Note that both are attributed to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar.
Ibn al-Humam preferred the wujub view.
2
Identify the key scenario
Consider the case: a person becomes able (Muslim, adult, sane, free) just before the Hajj time ends and fears death. What are the rulings on bequest?
This scenario tests the difference.
3
Analyze the thamarah
Determine the practical consequence of each view. According to the source, the fruit of the difference is not the validity of the bequest, but whether the bequest is obligatory.
Text says: 'ثمرة الخلاف لا تظهر في صحة الوصية وإنما في وجوب الإيصاء'.
4
Understand the basis
Explain why each view leads to a different ruling on bequest obligation. If time is condition for wujub, the person was never obligated, so no need to bequeath. If for ada', obligation is triggered, so bequest becomes obligatory upon inability.
This is a classic usul-furu' connection.
5
Recognize the tarjih
Identify which view is relied upon (mufta bihi). The passage mentions that Ibn al-Humam preferred the wujub view, and it is the famous (mashhur) position.
This tarjih affects fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو الاستطاعة لا يسقط عنهم الفرض ويجب عليهم ثانياً إذا استطاعوا ا هـ قوله : (والوقت) قال الرملي : سيذكره أيضاً في شرائط الصحة، ولا شك أن من لم يدرك وقت الحج لم يجب عليه وأنه لا يصح إلا في وقته المخصوص فكان شرطاً للوجوب وشرطاً للصحة تأمل ا هـ . وفي «لباب المناسك»: السابع الوقت وهو أشهر الحج أو وقت خروج أهل بلده إن كانوا يخرجون قبلها فلا يجب إلا على القادر فيها أو في وقت خروجهم فإن ملكه أي المال قبل الوقت فله صرفه حيث شاء ولا حج عليه، وإن ملكه فيه فليس له صرفه إلى غير الحج فلو صرف رفه لم يسقط الوجوب عنه، ولو أسلم كافراً وبلغ صبي أفاق مجنون أو عتق عبد قبل الوقت فخافوا الموت وهم موسرون ؛ قيل ليس عليهم الإيصاء بالحج. وقيل يجب، فإن أوصوا به فعلى الأولى لا يصح، وصح على الثاني، والخلاف مبني على أن الوقت شرط الوجوب أو الأداء قولان ا.هـ. قال شارحه ملا علي : هما روايتان عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وزفر، ورجح ابن الهمام القول بأنه شرط الوجوب، ونسب صاحب المجمع صحة الإيصاء إلى الإمام وصاحبه وخلافها إلى زفر معللاً بأنهم كانوا أهل الوجوب وقت الوصية فيصح إيصاؤهم بأن يحج عنهم في وقته لعجزهم عنه، ويؤيده ما في الخانية : لو بلغ الصبي فحضره الوفاة وأوصى بأن يحج عنه حجة الإسلام جازت وصيته عندنا ويحج فجعل المذهب الجواز وهو لا ينافي جعل الوقت من شرائط الوجوب على المشهور المرجح خلاف ما فهم المصنف وبنى عليه صحة الإيصاء وعدمها ا هـ . قلت: فعلى هذا فثمرة الخلاف في أن الوقت شرط للوجوب أو للأداء لا تظهر في صحة الوصية وعدمها وإنما تظهر في وجوب الإيصاء أو الإحجاج عنه وعدم ذلك فلا يجب على المشهور ويجب على خلافه تأمل قوله : (وقد يقال كذلك العقل والبلوغ أي أنهما شرطان لكل عبادة قوله : (وخروج الزوج والمحرم معها قال الرملي وفي البدائع والأصح أنه أي المحرم شرط الوجوب ا هـ. فقد
Or ability (for those who become able later) does not remove the obligation from them and it becomes incumbent upon them again if they are able. End quote. His statement: (time). Al-Ramli said: he will also mention it among conditions of validity, and no doubt that whoever does not reach the time of Hajj is not obligated, and that it is valid only in its specific time, so it is a condition for obligation and a condition for validity. Reflect. End quote. In Lubab al-Manasik: the seventh is time, which is the months of Hajj or the time of departure of his countrymen if they leave before that, so it is only obligatory on the one who is able during it or at their departure time. If he possesses the wealth before time, he may spend it as he wishes and no Hajj is due on him. If he possesses it within the time, he may not spend it on other than Hajj, and if he spends it, the obligation does not fall from him. If a disbeliever becomes Muslim, a boy reaches puberty, an insane person regains sanity, or a slave is freed before the time, and they fear death while being well-off, it is said that bequest of Hajj is not upon them; and it is said that it is obligatory. If they bequeath it, according to the first it is not valid, but valid according to the second. The difference is based on whether time is a condition for obligation or performance, two opinions. End quote. Its commentator Mulla 'Ali said: they are two narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar. Ibn al-Humam preferred the opinion that it is a condition for obligation. The author of al-Majma' attributed validity of bequest to the Imam and his two companions, and opposition to Zufar, explaining that they were people of obligation at the time of bequest, so their bequest that someone perform Hajj for them at its time due to their inability is valid. Supported by what is in al-Khaniyya: if a boy reaches puberty and faces his death and bequeaths that Hajj al-Islam be performed for him, his bequest is valid according to us and Hajj is performed. Thus the relied-upon madhhab is permissibility, which does not contradict making time a condition for obligation according to the preferred famous view, contrary to what the author understood and built upon of validity or non-validity. End quote. I say: accordingly, the fruit of the difference whether time is a condition for obligation or performance does not appear in the validity of the bequest, but rather appears in the obligation of bequest or having someone perform Hajj for him. So according to the famous view it is not obligatory, but according to the other view it is obligatory. Reflect. His statement: (and it may be said similarly for intellect and puberty, meaning that they are conditions for every act of worship). His statement: (and the husband or mahram with her). Al-Ramli said: and in al-Bada'i', the correct position is that the mahram is a condition for obligation. End quote. So...
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether time (the specific days of Hajj) is a condition for the obligation (wujub) or for the performance (ada') of Hajj. The text opens by quoting al-Ramli who says time is both a condition for obligation and validity. Then it cites Lubab al-Manasik on the practical rules: if one owns the means before the time, he may spend it freely; if within the time, he must spend it on Hajj. A key scenario: if a person becomes obligated (by conversion, puberty, sanity, or freedom) just before the time ends and fears death, is it obligatory to bequeath Hajj? There are two positions. The commentator Mulla 'Ali explains that Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar have two narrations. Ibn al-Humam preferred that time is a condition for obligation, while the author of al-Majma' attributed the validity of bequest (i.e., that one can bequeath Hajj) to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, with Zufar opposing. The text then says that the practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is not about the validity of the bequest, but about whether the bequest itself is obligatory. According to the famous view (time condition for wujub), bequest is not obligatory; according to the other view, it is. This is a refined legal analysis showing how difference in usul affects furu'.

Key Terms
شرط الوجوب (sharṭ al-wujūb): A condition without which the act is not obligatory at all, e.g., time of Hajj is needed for the obligation to be triggered.
الإيصاء (al-īṣā’): Bequest: a dying person's instruction for someone to perform Hajj on their behalf after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute whether time is a condition for wujub or ada'?
A) Whether the bequest of Hajj is valid
B) Whether the bequest is obligatory
C) Whether the person is considered able
D) Whether the Hajj must be performed in the current year

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the dispute over whether time is a condition for obligation or performance of Hajj does not affect the validity of a bequest, only its obligation.

The Wajibat of Hajj and Their Consequence
Lists the wajibat of Hajj whose omission requires a dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and state the consequence of omitting any one of them.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the wajibat of Hajj are acts whose omission requires a blood sacrifice (dam), but the Hajj remains valid.

The Hajj consists of different categories of acts: arkan (pillars), wajibat (obligations), and sunan (recommended practices). This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq enumerates the wajibat as defined by the Hanafi school. Understanding the list is crucial because each has a specific compensatory mechanism: if a wajib is left out, a dam (sacrifice) becomes necessary, but the Hajj itself is not invalidated.

Guided Path
1
Define 'wajib' in the context of Hajj
Understand that a wajib is an obligatory act that is less than a rukn (pillar) but more than a sunnah. In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a wajib intentionally or through forgetfulness requires a dam (sacrifice) but does not invalidate the Hajj.
This is a key distinction from the Shafi'i school where many of these acts are considered sunnah.
2
Memorize the list of wajibat
Review the extensive list from the text. Group them into categories: Miqat (ihram), Arafah, Muzdalifah, Halq/Taqsir, Sa'y, Ramy, Tawaf-related (beginning from Hajar Aswad, right side, walking, purity, covering awrah), and others (sacrifice for qarin/mutamatti, prayer after tawaf, Tawaf al-Sadr, order, timing of halq, Tawaf al-Ifada).
Memorization anchors like this are essential for quick recall in fatwa and teaching.
3
Identify the consequence of omission
For each wajib, the consequence is the same: a dam (sacrifice of a sheep or equivalent) must be performed. This is stated directly in the passage: 'which for leaving one of them a dam is required'.
There is no distinction based on which wajib is omitted; the rule is uniform.
4
Distinguish between arkan and wajib
Pillars (arkan) such as standing at Arafah, tawaf al-ifada, and sa'y are essential; omitting them invalidates the Hajj. The wajibat listed here are obligatory but not pillars; omission requires compensation (dam) but the Hajj is still valid.
This is a critical point for beginners to avoid confusing the two categories.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a pilgrim who intentionally does not perform the sa'y. According to Hanafi fiqh, the Hajj is valid but a dam is required. This practical application solidifies the concept.
Real-life examples help internalize the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وواجباته أعني التي يلزم بترك واحد منها دم إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات. ومد الوقوف بعرفة أو إلى الغروب، والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بين طلوع فجر يوم النحر إلى طلوع الشمس، والحلق أو التقصير، والسعي بين الصفا والمروة سبعة أشواط وكونه بعد طواف معتد به، ورمي الجمار، وبداية الطواف من الحجر الأسود والتيامن فيه والمشي فيه لمن ليس له عذر يمنعه منه، والطهارة فيه من الحدث الأصغر والأكبر، وستر العورة وأقل الأشواط السبعة وهي ثلاثة، وبداية السعي بين الصفا والمروة من الصفا والمشي فيه لمن ليس له عذر، وذبح الشاة للقارن أو المتمتع وصلاة ركعتين لكل أسبوع، وطواف الصدر، والترتيب بين الرمي والحلق والذبح يوم النحر، وتوقيت الحلق بالمكان وتوقيته بالزمان وفعل طواف الإفاضة في أيام النحر، وما عدا هذه المذكورات مما سيأتي بيانه مفصلاً سنن وآداب.
And its wajibat: those things for which leaving one of them necessitates a dam. Beginning ihram from the miqat. Extending the stay at 'Arafah until sunset. Staying at Muzdalifah between dawn of the Day of Sacrifice and sunrise. Shaving or trimming. Sa'y between Safa and Marwah seven circuits, and it being after a credible tawaf. Stoning the jamarat. Beginning the tawaf from the Black Stone, and keeping it to the right in it, and walking in it for one without an excuse preventing him. Ritual purity in it from minor and major hadath. Covering the 'awrah. The minimum of the seven circuits is three. Beginning sa'y between Safa and Marwah from Safa, and walking in it for one without an excuse. Slaughtering a sheep for the qarin or mutamatti'. Praying two rak'ahs for each cycle (seven tawafs?). Tawaf al-Sadr. Order between stoning, shaving, and slaughtering on the Day of Sacrifice. Timing of shaving to place and time. Performing Tawaf al-Ifada during the days of sacrifice. Other than these mentioned things that will be detailed later are sunan and adab.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the wajibat (obligatory elements) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The author explicitly defines them as acts whose intentional omission requires a dam (blood sacrifice) to compensate. This is a key concept in Hanafi fiqh: between arkan (pillars, which invalidate the act if omitted without excuse) and sunan (recommended acts, whose omission does not require compensation) lies the category of wajib. Listed wajibat include: 1) starting ihram from the miqat, 2) staying at Arafah until sunset, 3) staying at Muzdalifah between Fajr and sunrise of Yawm al-Nahr, 4) shaving or trimming the hair, 5) sa'y after a valid tawaf, 6) stoning the jamarat, 7) starting tawaf from Hajr Aswad, 8) performing tawaf on the right (performance of tawaf positively), 9) walking in tawaf for those able, 10) purification from hadath in tawaf, 11) covering ‘awrah in tawaf, 12) the minimum of sa'y is three circuits, 13) starting sa'y from Safa, 14) walking in sa'y if able, 15) sacrifice for qarin or mutamatti’, 16) praying two rak'ahs after each tawaf (except perhaps Tawaf al-Qudum?), 17) Tawaf al-Sadr, 18) ordering of rituals on Yawm al-Nahr, 19) timing of halq, 20) performing Tawaf al-Ifada in the days of sacrifice. The text concludes that anything beyond these is sunan or adab which will be explained later.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (e.g., sheep) required to compensate for omission of a wajib in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the wajibat of Hajj are clearly enumerated, and omitting any one of them necessitates a dam, but the Hajj itself remains valid.
