Prohibitions of Ihram (Muharramat)
Categorizes and lists actions prohibited during Ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of prohibitions during ihram and list the specific acts prohibited in each category.

Core Idea
A muhrim must avoid two kinds of prohibitions: acts upon himself and acts affecting others.

In this lesson, we examine the muharramat (prohibitions) of ihram. The Hanafi school divides these prohibitions into two types: those that the muhrim does to his own person, and those he does to others or to the environment. Understanding this classification helps memorize the prohibitions and recognize their legal significance.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the two main categories
Prohibitions are either self-directed (touching one's own body) or other-directed (touching others or the environment).
2
List the self-directed prohibitions
These include sexual intercourse, removing hair, trimming nails, applying perfume, covering the head and face, and wearing sewn garments (for men).
Women may wear stitched clothes, but still must avoid perfume and covering face (in some views).
3
List the other-directed prohibitions
These include shaving someone else's head and hunting or causing the death of game animals (in or out of the Haram).
Hunting refers to land game; fish are excluded.
4
Note the exception: cutting trees of the Haram
Cutting trees of the Haram is not counted among ihram prohibitions, as per al-Nihaya; its prohibition is general, not specific to ihram.
Some scholars (like in Fath al-Qadir) consider it analogous to hunting, but the relied-upon position excludes it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما محظوراته فنوعان ما يفعله في نفسه وهو الجماع وإزالة الشعر وقلم الأظفار والتطيب وتغطية الرأس والوجه ولبس المخيط، وما يفعله في غيره وهو حلق رأس الغير والتعرض للصيد في الحل والحرم، وأما قطع شجر الحرم فلا ينبغي عده مما نحن فيه كما في النهاية، فإن حرمته لا تتعلق بالحج ولا بالإحرام. كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال : إنه كصيد الحرم وقد عده من محظوراته فلا بدع في أن يكون حراماً بجهتين كما لا يخفى.
As for its prohibitions, they are two types: what one does to himself, which is sexual intercourse, removing hair, trimming nails, applying perfume, covering the head and face, and wearing sewn garments; and what one does to others, which is shaving another's head and pursuing game in the halal and haram. As for cutting trees of the Haram, it should not be counted among that which concerns us here, as in al-Nihaya, because its prohibition is not connected to Hajj or ihram. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said: it is like game of the Haram, and he counted it among its prohibitions, so it is not surprising that it is prohibited from two aspects, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage enumerates the prohibitions (muharramat) of the state of ihram. It divides them into two categories: (1) those that affect the person himself, such as sexual intercourse, hair removal, nail cutting, perfume, covering head/face, and wearing stitched clothes; (2) those that affect others, such as shaving someone else's head and hunting in the Haram (both within and outside the Haram). The text then notes a point of ihtilaf: cutting the trees of the Haram is not considered a prohibition of ihram according to al-Nihaya, as its prohibition is general and not specific to ihram. However, Fath al-Qadir suggests it may be analogous to hunting and thus a prohibition from two perspectives. This is a refined point showing that the same act may be prohibited for different reasons.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makhīṭ): Garments that are sewn or tailored, prohibited for men in ihram.
الصيد (al-ṣayd): Hunting or causing the killing of game animals, prohibited in the Haram and also for the muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is not included among ihram prohibitions according to al-Nihaya
C) It is allowed if needed
D) It requires dam

Key Takeaway
The muharramat of ihram are divided into self-directed acts and acts affecting others; cutting trees of the Haram is a separate prohibition, not part of ihram.

Important Preliminaries for Hajj: Repentance, Restitution, and Permission
Advises on repentance, rights restitution, and parental consent before Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the important preliminaries for Hajj according to the Hanafi school and apply the rulings on parental and spousal permission to different scenarios.

Core Idea
For obligatory Hajj, permission is recommendatory; for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents is absolute.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition outlines the moral and legal preparations one should undertake before embarking on Hajj. It covers repentance, restitution of rights, and the critical issue of obtaining permission from parents, spouse, and creditors. The rulings vary between obligatory and voluntary Hajj, and depend on the dependency of the family members.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preliminaries
Locate the list of important matters at the beginning of the passage: repentance with its conditions, returning injustices, making up missed acts, regret, resolve, seeking forgiveness, and obtaining consent of those who dislike his departure.
These are moral and spiritual preparations recommended before Hajj.
2
Distinguish fard vs nafl Hajj
Notice the final sentence: 'All this is in obligatory Hajj; as for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents takes precedence absolutely.' This distinguishes the weight of permission.
This is a key principle: for nafl, parents' wishes override.
3
Analyze parental permission scenarios
Work through the cases: (1) Father not needy – no harm; (2) Father needy – disliked; (3) Mother same; (4) Beardless son – father may prevent; (5) Dangerous road – do not go. Also grandparents like parents if absent.
The ruling is not a blanket yes/no; it depends on the circumstances.
4
Examine spouse and creditor situations
For spouse: if the traveler supports her, her dislike matters; if she is self-sufficient, no harm. For debtor: disliked to go unless creditor permits; if there is a guarantor, both must agree except when guarantor was unauthorized.
These rulings protect the rights of dependents and creditors.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: for fard Hajj, permission is not a condition but highly recommended to avoid causing pain; for nafl, parental obedience is absolute.
Consult a person of opinion when there is difference of views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمن أراد الحج مهمات ينبغي الاعتناء بها وهي: البداية بالتوبة بشروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما فعله قصر في من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه في ذلك، والعزم على عدم العود إلى مثل ذلك، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات، وتحصيل رضا من يكره السفر بغير رضاه. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى العيون : إذا أراد الابن أن يخرج إلى الحج وأبوه كاره لذلك إن كان الأب مستغنياً عن خدمته فلا بأس به، وإن كان محتاجاً يكره، وكذا الأم. وفي السير الكبير : إذا لم يخف عليه الضعف فلا بأس به، وكذا إن كرهت خروجه زوجته ومن عليه نفقته، وإن لم يكن عليه نفقته فلا بأس به مطلقاً. وفي النوازل : إن كان الابن أمرد الوجه للأب أن يمنعه عن الخروج حتى يلتحي، وإن كان الطريق مخوفاً لا يخرج صبيح وإن لم يكن أمرد ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما، ويكره الخروج للغزو والحج لمديون وإن لم يكن له مال يقضي به إلا أن يأذن الغريم فإن كان بالدين كفيل بإذنه لا يخرج إلا بإذنهما وإن بغير أذنه فبإذن الطالب وحده ا.هـ. وهذا كله في حج الفرض، أما في حج النفل فطاعة الوالدين أولى مطلقاً كما صرح به في الملتقط ويشاور ذا رأي في اختلف التصحيح كما ترى
For whoever intends Hajj, there are important matters that should be attended to: beginning with repentance with its conditions: returning injustices to their owners when possible, making up for shortcomings in acts of worship, regret for his negligence in that, resolve not to return to the like, seeking forgiveness from those with disputes and transactions, and obtaining the consent of one who dislikes travel without his pleasure. In al-Khulasa, citing al-'Uyun: if the son wants to go out for Hajj while his father disapproves, if the father is not in need of his service, then there is no harm; if he is needy, it is disliked. The same applies to the mother. In al-Siyar al-Kabir: if he does not fear weakness (in the father?), there is no harm; similarly if his wife and those he supports dislike his going out, but if he does not pay their expenses, there is absolutely no harm. In al-Nawazil: if the son is beardless, the father may prevent him from going out until he grows a beard, and if the road is dangerous, he should not go out [صبيح] whether beardless or not. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: grandfathers and grandmothers are like parents in their absence. It is disliked for a debtor to go out for jihad or Hajj if he has no wealth to repay the debt, unless the creditor permits. If the debt has a guarantor, he cannot go out except with the permission of both; if without his permission (the guarantor's?), only the creditor's permission alone suffices. End quote. All this is in obligatory Hajj; as for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents takes precedence absolutely, as stated in al-Multaqat. He should consult a person of opinion when the correction differs, as you see.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage provides important preliminary recommendations for someone intending Hajj. It begins with moral and spiritual preparations: sincere repentance with its conditions (returning wrongfully taken property, making up missed worship, regret, resolve, seeking forgiveness from others, and obtaining consent of those who dislike being traveled away). Then it cites several Hanafi sources on the issue of parental and spousal permission for Hajj. Al-Khulasa states that if a father does not need his son's service, the son may go; if the father depends on him, it is disliked. Similar for the mother. Al-Siyar al-Kabir adds that if there is no fear of weakness, there is no harm; also the wife's dislike matters only if he supports her; if she supports herself, he may go. Al-Nawazil discusses a beardless boy: the father may prevent travel until he grows a beard, and if the road is dangerous, travel is forbidden. Fath al-Qadir extends the parent ruling to grandparents. It is also disliked for a debtor to travel unless the creditor permits, with special rules for guarantors. Finally, all these restrictions apply only to obligatory Hajj (fard); for nafl Hajj, obedience to parents is always prioritized.

Key Terms
تحصيل رضا (taḥṣīl riḍā): Obtaining the consent of a person who dislikes the traveler's departure, such as parents or spouse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which type of Hajj does obedience to parents take absolute precedence over performing the Hajj?
A) Obligatory Hajj (fard)
B) Voluntary Hajj (nafl)
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
For obligatory Hajj, parental permission is not a condition but recommended to avoid harm; for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents takes absolute precedence.

Repentance and Permission Before Hajj
Advising on repentance, permission, and consultation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of repentance for Hajj and identify when permission from parents, spouse, and creditors is required or waived.

Core Idea
Sincere repentance and obtaining consent from those whose rights are affected are prerequisites for a valid Hajj.

This lesson covers the initial preparations for Hajj: sincere repentance, making amends, and securing permission from parents, spouse, and creditors. These steps ensure that the pilgrim sets out with a clear conscience and without violating others' rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of repentance
What are the four conditions of tawbah mentioned? List them.
Includes returning injustices and making up missed worship.
2
Seeking permission from parents
Distinguish between obligatory and voluntary Hajj regarding parental obedience.
For obligatory Hajj, if parent is in need of service, it is makruh to go without permission.
3
Rulings for wife and dependents
When is the wife's permission needed? And those he supports?
If he supports them, their dislike matters; if not, no harm.
4
Creditors and debt
What is the ruling for a debtor? When is it permissible to go?
Makruh without creditor permission unless debt is guaranteed with permission.
5
Consultation and istikharah
What advice is given about consulting others and istikharah?
Consult about timing, not about performing Hajj itself.

ولمن أراد الحج مهمات ينبغي الاعتناء بها وهي: البداية بالتوبة بشروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما فعله قصر في من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه في ذلك، والعزم على عدم العود إلى مثل ذلك، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات، وتحصيل رضا من يكره السفر بغير رضاه. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى العيون : إذا أراد الابن أن يخرج إلى الحج وأبوه كاره لذلك إن كان الأب مستغنياً عن خدمته فلا بأس به، وإن كان محتاجاً يكره، وكذا الأم. وفي السير الكبير : إذا لم يخف عليه الضعف فلا بأس به، وكذا إن كرهت خروجه زوجته ومن عليه نفقته، وإن لم يكن عليه نفقته فلا بأس به مطلقاً. وفي النوازل : إن كان الابن أمرد الوجه للأب أن يمنعه عن الخروج حتى يلتحي، وإن كان الطريق مخوفاً لا يخرج صبيح وإن لم يكن أمرد ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما، ويكره الخروج للغزو والحج لمديون وإن لم يكن له مال يقضي به إلا أن يأذن الغريم فإن كان بالدين كفيل بإذنه لا يخرج إلا بإذنهما وإن بغير أذنه فبإذن الطالب وحده ا.هـ. وهذا كله في حج الفرض، أما في حج النفل فطاعة الوالدين أولى مطلقاً كما صرح به في الملتقط ويشاور ذا رأي في سفره في ذلك الوقت لا في نفس الحج فإنه خير، وكذا يستخير الله في ذلك. ويجتهد في تحصيل نفقة حلال فإنه لا يقبل بالنفقة الحرام كما ورد في الحديث مع أنه يسقط الفرض عنه معها وإن كانت مغصوبة، ولا تنافي بين سقوطه وعدم قبوله فلا يثاب لعدم القبول، ولا يعاقب في الآخرة عقاب تارك الحج. ولا بد له من رفيق صالح يذكره إذا نسي ويصبره إذا جزع ويعينه إذا عجز، وكونه من الأجانب أولى من الأقارب عند بعض الصالحين تبعداً من ساحة القطعية. ويرى المكاري ما يحمله ولا يحمل أكثر منه إلا بإذنه، وقد ذكر عن بعض السلف ويقال إنه الشافعي وقيل ابن المبارك، وقيل ابن القاسم صاحب الإمام مالك أنه دفع إليه مطالعة ليحملها إلى إنسان فامتنع من حملها بدون إذن المكاري لكونه لم يشارطه على ذلك ورعاً من فاعله وكذا يحترز من تحميلها فوق ما تطيق ومن تقليل علفها المعتاد بلا ضرورة ولو مملوكه له وفي إجارة الخلاصة : حمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً، وحمل الحمار مائة وخمسون مناً. قالوا ولا يشارك في الزاد واجتماع الرفقة كل يوم على طعام أحدهم أحل. وينبغي أن يستثنى ما إذا علمت المسامحة بينهما فله المشاركة وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاه مخلص. وتجريد السفر عن التجارة أحسن، ولو اتجر لا ينقص ثوابه كالغازي إذا اتجر كما ذكره الشارح في السير. وأما عن الرياء والسمعة والفخر ظاهراً أو باطناً ففرض وخلط التجارة بهذا القسم كما في فتح القدير مما ينبغي . وأما الركوب في المحمل فكرهه بعضهم خوفاً مما ذكرنا، ولم يكرهه بعضهم إذا د عن ذلك ففي التحقيق لا اختلاف وركوب الجمل أفضل، ويكره الحج على الحمار والظاهر أنها تنزيهية بدليل أفضلية ما ،قابله والمشي أفضل من الركوب لمن يطيقه ولا
And for whoever intends Hajj, there are important matters that should be attended to: beginning with repentance with its conditions, namely returning injustices to their owners when possible, making up what he neglected of acts of worship, regretting his negligence in that, resolving not to return to the like of that, seeking forgiveness from those with whom he had disputes and transactions, and obtaining the satisfaction of one who dislikes travel without his consent. In al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Uyun: If a son wants to go out for Hajj and his father dislikes that, if the father is not in need of his service, then there is no harm; if he is in need, it is disliked; similarly for the mother. In al-Siyar al-Kabir: If one does not fear weakness for him, then there is no harm; similarly if his wife and those he supports dislike his departure, but if he does not support them, then there is no harm absolutely. In al-Nawazil: If the son is beardless, the father may prevent him from going out until he grows a beard; if the road is dangerous, he does not go out... and if he is not beardless... In Fath al-Qadir: Grandfathers and grandmothers are like the parents when they are absent. It is disliked for a debtor to go out for warfare or Hajj even if he has no money to repay, unless the creditor permits. If the debt has a guarantor with his permission, he does not go out except with permission from both; if without his permission, then with the permission of the claimant alone. This all is for obligatory Hajj; as for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents is absolutely preferred as stated in al-Multaqat. He should consult a person of opinion regarding his travel at that time, not regarding the Hajj itself, as that is good; likewise he should seek good from Allah. He should strive to obtain lawful expenditure, for it is not accepted with unlawful expenditure as has come in the hadith, even though the obligation falls from him with it even if it was usurped; there is no contradiction between its falling and its non-acceptance, so he is not rewarded due to non-acceptance, but he is not punished in the Hereafter with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. He must have a righteous companion who reminds him when he forgets, patiently endures when he becomes impatient, and helps him when he is unable; having an unrelated companion is better than a relative according to some righteous, to keep away from the field of cutting off. The beast driver should see what he loads and not load more than that except with his permission. It has been mentioned from some predecessors – it is said to be al-Shafi'i, some say Ibn al-Mubarak, some say Ibn al-Qasim the companion of Imam Malik – that he gave a letter to carry to a person, but he refused to carry it without the permission of the beast driver because he had not stipulated that, out of scrupulousness. Likewise he should be cautious of loading them beyond what they can bear and reducing their usual fodder without necessity, even if owned by him. In Ijara al-Khulasa: The load of a camel is two hundred and forty mans, and the load of a donkey is one hundred and fifty mans. They said: He should not share in provisions, and the gathering of companions every day on the food of one of them is permitted. It should be excepted when mutual leniency is known, then he may share; otherwise if he shares, seeking forgiveness from the partners is a way out. Stripping the journey from trade is better; if he trades, his reward is not diminished, like the warrior if he trades, as the commentator mentioned in al-Siyar. As for riya', fame, and pride, whether outwardly or inwardly, it is obligatory to avoid, and mixing trade with this category is something to be avoided, as in Fath al-Qadir. As for riding in a howdah, some disliked it out of fear of what we mentioned; some did not dislike it if protected from that; in reality there is no disagreement. Riding a camel is better; riding a donkey for Hajj is disliked, and apparently it is tanzihi (disliked), as evidenced by the superiority of the opposite; and walking is better than riding for one who is able to do it.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This lengthy passage outlines the important preparations (muhimmat) for one intending to perform Hajj. It begins with repentance, including returning wrongs, making up missed worship, and seeking forgiveness. It then addresses the issue of seeking permission from parents, spouse, and creditors, with detailed rulings: for obligatory Hajj, if a parent is in need of the child's service, it is disliked to go without permission; similar rules apply for a wife and dependent relatives. A debtor should not go without creditor's permission. For voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents takes precedence absolutely. The pilgrim is advised to consult a wise person and perform istikharah. He must strive for halal expenditure; Hajj with haram money fulfills the obligation but brings no reward. He needs a righteous companion, preferably unrelated to avoid conflicts. He must not overload his mount or underfeed it; specific loads are mentioned. He should avoid sharing provisions unless mutual leniency is known. Stripping travel from trade is better, but trade does not reduce reward as long as it is free from riya'. Riding a camel is better than a donkey; walking is superior for those able.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance with its conditions: return injustices, make up worship, regret, resolve.
الاستحلال (al-istihlal): Seeking forgiveness from those one has wronged.
حج الفرض (Hajj al-fard): Obligatory Hajj (once in a lifetime).
حج النفل (Hajj al-nafl): Voluntary Hajj (supererogatory).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a son performing obligatory Hajj when his mother is not in need of his service?
A) It is haram without permission.
B) It is makruh tanzihi.
C) There is no harm.
D) It is wajib to go.

Key Takeaway
Sincere repentance and obtaining consent from those whose rights are affected are prerequisites for a valid and accepted Hajj.

Halal Expenditure and the Righteous Companion
Advising on lawful expenditure and companionship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hajj with unlawful money fulfills the obligation but is not rewarded, and state the qualities of a righteous travel companion.

Core Idea
Hajj with haram money fulfills the duty but earns no reward; a righteous companion is essential for spiritual and practical support.

This lesson focuses on two critical aspects of Hajj preparation: ensuring that one's expenses are from lawful earnings and choosing a righteous traveling companion. The passage explains the Hanafi distinction between the obligation being fulfilled and the acceptance of the deed, and it provides guidelines for selecting a companion who will aid in religious observance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on halal expenditure
What does the hadith say about Hajj with unlawful money? How do we reconcile the obligation falling and non-acceptance?
The obligation is fulfilled (sqt) but no reward (thawab) due to non-acceptance.
2
Distinguish between fulfillment and acceptance
Explain why there is no contradiction. The pilgrim is not punished for abandoning Hajj, but also not rewarded.
3
Identify qualities of a righteous companion
What three roles does the companion fulfill? Why is a non-relative preferable?
Reminds, endures, helps. Non-relative avoids cutting ties.
4
Consider the beast driver's responsibility
What must the beast driver do regarding loading and permission?
He must not load more than agreed or without permission.

And for whoever intends Hajj, there are important matters that should be attended to: beginning with repentance with its conditions, namely returning injustices to their owners when possible, making up what he neglected of acts of worship, regretting his negligence in that, resolving not to return to the like of that, seeking forgiveness from those with whom he had disputes and transactions, and obtaining the satisfaction of one who dislikes travel without his consent. In al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Uyun: If a son wants to go out for Hajj and his father dislikes that, if the father is not in need of his service, then there is no harm; if he is in need, it is disliked; similarly for the mother. In al-Siyar al-Kabir: If one does not fear weakness for him, then there is no harm; similarly if his wife and those he supports dislike his departure, but if he does not support them, then there is no harm absolutely. In al-Nawazil: If the son is beardless, the father may prevent him from going out until he grows a beard; if the road is dangerous, he does not go out... and if he is not beardless... In Fath al-Qadir: Grandfathers and grandmothers are like the parents when they are absent. It is disliked for a debtor to go out for warfare or Hajj even if he has no money to repay, unless the creditor permits. If the debt has a guarantor with his permission, he does not go out except with permission from both; if without his permission, then with the permission of the claimant alone. This all is for obligatory Hajj; as for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents is absolutely preferred as stated in al-Multaqat. He should consult a person of opinion regarding his travel at that time, not regarding the Hajj itself, as that is good; likewise he should seek good from Allah. He should strive to obtain lawful expenditure, for it is not accepted with unlawful expenditure as has come in the hadith, even though the obligation falls from him with it even if it was usurped; there is no contradiction between its falling and its non-acceptance, so he is not rewarded due to non-acceptance, but he is not punished in the Hereafter with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. He must have a righteous companion who reminds him when he forgets, patiently endures when he becomes impatient, and helps him when he is unable; having an unrelated companion is better than a relative according to some righteous, to keep away from the field of cutting off. The beast driver should see what he loads and not load more than that except with his permission. It has been mentioned from some predecessors – it is said to be al-Shafi'i, some say Ibn al-Mubarak, some say Ibn al-Qasim the companion of Imam Malik – that he gave a letter to carry to a person, but he refused to carry it without the permission of the beast driver because he had not stipulated that, out of scrupulousness. Likewise he should be cautious of loading them beyond what they can bear and reducing their usual fodder without necessity, even if owned by him. In Ijara al-Khulasa: The load of a camel is two hundred and forty mans, and the load of a donkey is one hundred and fifty mans. They said: He should not share in provisions, and the gathering of companions every day on the food of one of them is permitted. It should be excepted when mutual leniency is known, then he may share; otherwise if he shares, seeking forgiveness from the partners is a way out. Stripping the journey from trade is better; if he trades, his reward is not diminished, like the warrior if he trades, as the commentator mentioned in al-Siyar. As for riya', fame, and pride, whether outwardly or inwardly, it is obligatory to avoid, and mixing trade with this category is something to be avoided, as in Fath al-Qadir. As for riding in a howdah, some disliked it out of fear of what we mentioned; some did not dislike it if protected from that; in reality there is no disagreement. Riding a camel is better; riding a donkey for Hajj is disliked, and apparently it is tanzihi (disliked), as evidenced by the superiority of the opposite; and walking is better than riding for one who is able to do it.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This lengthy passage outlines the important preparations (muhimmat) for one intending to perform Hajj. It begins with repentance, including returning wrongs, making up missed worship, and seeking forgiveness. It then addresses the issue of seeking permission from parents, spouse, and creditors, with detailed rulings: for obligatory Hajj, if a parent is in need of the child's service, it is disliked to go without permission; similar rules apply for a wife and dependent relatives. A debtor should not go without creditor's permission. For voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents takes precedence absolutely. The pilgrim is advised to consult a wise person and perform istikharah. He must strive for halal expenditure; Hajj with haram money fulfills the obligation but brings no reward. He needs a righteous companion, preferably unrelated to avoid conflicts. He must not overload his mount or underfeed it; specific loads are mentioned. He should avoid sharing provisions unless mutual leniency is known. Stripping travel from trade is better, but trade does not reduce reward as long as it is free from riya'. Riding a camel is better than a donkey; walking is superior for those able.

Key Terms
النفقة الحلال (al-nafaqah al-halal): Lawful expenditure; used for Hajj, it ensures reward.
الرفيق الصالح (al-rafiq al-salih): Righteous companion who helps in spiritual and practical matters.
سقوط الفرض (suqut al-fard): Fulfillment of the obligation; the duty no longer rests on the person.
عدم القبول (adam al-qubul): Non-acceptance; the deed is not rewarded by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of Hajj performed with usurped (ghasb) money?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The obligation is fulfilled but no reward is given.
C) The Hajj is valid and rewarded if the person repents.
D) The Hajj is not valid until the money is returned.

Key Takeaway
Hajj with haram money fulfills the duty but yields no reward; a righteous companion is indispensable for a successful and spiritually fruitful journey.

Conduct During the Journey: Trade, Riding, and Provisions
Advising on trade, riding, and provisions during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on trade during Hajj, riding preferences, and sharing provisions.

Core Idea
Trade during Hajj is permitted without reward diminishment if free from riya; walking is superior to riding, and sharing provisions is generally avoided unless mutual leniency exists.

This lesson addresses practical conduct during the Hajj journey: engaging in trade, avoiding ostentation, the etiquette of riding animals, and the ruling on sharing provisions. The goal is to maintain the spiritual focus while fulfilling worldly needs lawfully.

Guided Path
1
Evaluate the ruling on trade during Hajj
Is trade permissible during Hajj? Does it diminish the reward? What is the condition?
Trade is allowed and does not reduce reward if free from riya' and pride.
2
Understand the prohibition of riya' and pride
What does the text say about riya', sama', and fakhr?
Avoiding them is fard (obligatory).
3
Identify the preferred mode of travel
What is the ruling on riding a howdah, camel, donkey, and walking?
Camel riding is best; donkey disliked (tanzihi); walking superior for those able.
4
Apply the ruling on sharing provisions
When is sharing provisions allowed? When is it better to avoid?
Generally do not share unless mutual leniency; if shared, seek forgiveness.

ولمن أراد الحج مهمات ينبغي الاعتناء بها وهي: البداية بالتوبة بشروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما فعله قصر في من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه في ذلك، والعزم على عدم العود إلى مثل ذلك، عند بعض الصالحين تبعداً من ساحة القطعية. ويرى المكاري ما يحمله ولا يحمل أكثر منه إلا بإذنه، وقد ذكر عن بعض السلف ويقال إنه الشافعي وقيل ابن المبارك، وقيل ابن القاسم صاحب الإمام مالك أنه دفع إليه And for whoever intends Hajj, there are important matters that should be attended to: beginning with repentance with its conditions, namely returning injustices to their owners when possible, making up what he neglected of acts of worship, regretting his negligence in that, resolving not to return to the like of that, seeking forgiveness from those with whom he had disputes and transactions, and obtaining the satisfaction of one who dislikes travel without his consent. In al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Uyun: If a son wants to go out for Hajj and his father dislikes that, if the father is not in need of his service, then there is no harm; if he is in need, it is disliked; similarly for the mother. In al-Siyar al-Kabir: If one does not fear weakness for him, then there is no harm; similarly if his wife and those he supports dislike his departure, but if he does not support them, then there is no harm absolutely. In al-Nawazil: If the son is beardless, the father may prevent him from going out until he grows a beard; if the road is dangerous, he does not go out... and if he is not beardless... In Fath al-Qadir: Grandfathers and grandmothers are like the parents when they are absent. It is disliked for a debtor to go out for warfare or Hajj even if he has no money to repay, unless the creditor permits. If the debt has a guarantor with his permission, he does not go out except with permission from both; if without his permission, then with the permission of the claimant alone. This all is for obligatory Hajj; as for voluntary Hajj, obedience to parents is absolutely preferred as stated in al-Multaqat. He should consult a person of opinion regarding his travel at that time, not regarding the Hajj itself, as that is good; likewise he should seek good from Allah. He should strive to obtain lawful expenditure, for it is not accepted with unlawful expenditure as has come in the hadith, even though the obligation falls from him with it even if it was usurped; there is no contradiction between its falling and its non-acceptance, so he is not rewarded due to non-acceptance, but he is not punished in the Hereafter with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. Hajj with Unlawful Funds: Fulfillment without Reward
Ruling on Hajj with unlawful spending.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Hajj performed with unlawful funds and explain why the obligation is fulfilled but not rewarded.

Core Idea
Hajj with unlawful funds fulfills the obligation but earns no reward.

The pilgrim is encouraged to earn lawful spending. But if Hajj is performed with unlawful or even usurped funds, the obligation is still discharged. However, the act is not accepted for reward. This nuanced ruling balances textual warnings with practical fulfillment of duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Hajj with unlawful or usurped funds. The ruling is that the obligation (fard) is fulfilled (sāqit al-fard), but the Hajj is not accepted (lā yuqbal) for reward.
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites a hadith that unlawful spending is not accepted. Even with that, the obligation is still met.
Evidence is from Sunnah, but the ruling on fulfillment is based on the principle that the deed itself is valid if the conditions are met.
3
Analyze the consequence
The person is not thābit (rewarded) due to lack of acceptance, but also not punished in the afterlife like those who abandon Hajj entirely.
4
Understand the distinction
There is no contradiction (lā tanāfi) between the obligation being fulfilled and the act not being accepted. This is a key Hanafi legal nuance: validity (sihha) vs. acceptance (qubul) for reward.
This distinction is crucial for understanding how acts with defective means can still meet the minimum requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
سفره في ذلك الوقت لا في نفس الحج فإنه خير، وكذا يستخير الله في ذلك. ويجتهد في تحصيل نفقة حلال فإنه لا يقبل بالنفقة الحرام كما ورد في الحديث مع أنه يسقط الفرض عنه معها وإن كانت مغصوبة، ولا تنافي بين سقوطه وعدم قبوله فلا يثاب لعدم القبول، ولا يعاقب في الآخرة عقاب تارك الحج. ولا بد له من رفيق صالح يذكره إذا نسي ويصبره إذا جزع ويعينه إذا عجز، وكونه من الأجانب أولى من الأقارب عند بعض الصالحين تبعداً من ساحة القطعية. ويرى المكاري ما يحمله ولا يحمل أكثر منه إلا بإذنه، وقد ذكر عن بعض السلف ويقال إنه الشافعي وقيل ابن المبارك، وقيل ابن القاسم صاحب الإمام مالك أنه دفع إليه مطالعة ليحملها إلى إنسان فامتنع من حملها بدون إذن المكاري لكونه لم يشارطه على ذلك ورعاً من فاعله وكذا يحترز من تحميلها فوق ما تطيق ومن تقليل علفها المعتاد بلا ضرورة ولو مملوكه له وفي إجارة الخلاصة : حمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً، وحمل الحمار مائة وخمسون مناً. قالوا ولا يشارك في الزاد واجتماع الرفقة كل يوم على طعام أحدهم أحل. وينبغي أن يستثنى ما إذا علمت المسامحة بينهما فله المشاركة وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاه مخلص. وتجريد السفر عن التجارة أحسن، ولو اتجر لا ينقص ثوابه كالغازي إذا اتجر كما ذكره الشارح في السير. وأما عن الرياء والسمعة والفخر ظاهراً أو باطناً ففرض وخلط التجارة بهذا القسم كما في فتح القدير مما ينبغي . وأما الركوب في المحمل فكرهه بعضهم خوفاً مما ذكرنا، ولم يكرهه بعضهم إذا د عن ذلك ففي التحقيق لا اختلاف وركوب الجمل أفضل، ويكره الحج على الحمار والظاهر أنها تنزيهية بدليل أفضلية ما قابله والمشي أفضل من الركوب لمن يطيقه ولا

قوله: (أنه دفع إليه (مطالعة الذي في النهر : بطاقة وهي الرقعة الصغيرة المربوطة بالثوب التي فيها رقم ثمنه كما في القاموس والمراد بها هنا المكتوب قوله: (وفي إجارة الخلاصة الخ) قال الرملي : نقله فيها عن الفتاوى الصغرى وأقول : لعمري هذا إحجاف على الحمار وإنصاف في حق الجمل فتأمل. وذكر في الجوهرة أن المن ستة وعشرون أوقية والأوقية سبعة مثاقيل وهي عشرة دراهم والمائتان وأربعون مناً . الوسق، فيكون حمل الجمل وسقاً، بالأرطال وهو الرملية تسعة وستون رطلاً وثلث رطل وهو قنطار دمشقي تقريباً على أن الرطل الرملي تسعمائة درهم ويلائم تفسير الوسق بحمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً ولا يلائم التفسير بغيره تأمل.

قوله : (وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاء مخلص) كذا في بعض النسخ، وفي بعضها وإلا فلا يشارك وفي بعضها وإلا لا ولو شارك فالاستحلال مخلص وهي أحسن قوله: (خوفاً مما
His travel at that time, not in Hajj itself, is good, and likewise he seeks guidance from Allah in that. And he strives to acquire lawful spending, for it is not accepted with unlawful spending as related in the hadith, even though the obligation is fulfilled with it even if it is usurped. There is no contradiction between fulfillment and lack of acceptance; he is not rewarded due to lack of acceptance, nor is he punished in the afterlife with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. He must have a righteous companion who reminds him when he forgets, consoles him when he panics, and helps him when he is unable. A companion from non-relatives is preferable to relatives according to some righteous, to distance from the sphere of certainty. And the camel-owner sees what he carries and does not carry more than that except with his permission. It has been mentioned from some predecessors, it is said that it was al-Shafi'i, or Ibn al-Mubarak, or Ibn al-Qasim, companion of Imam Malik, that a note was given to him to carry to a person, and he refrained from carrying it without the permission of the camel-owner because he had not stipulated that, out of piety. Similarly, he avoids loading it beyond its capacity and reducing its customary fodder without necessity, even if it is his own property. In the Ijarah of al-Khulasah: the load of a camel is two hundred and forty mann, and the load of a donkey is one hundred and fifty mann. They said: He should not share in the provisions, and gathering of the group each day for the food of one of them is better. It should be excepted when mutual leniency is known between them, so he may share. Otherwise, if he shares, then seeking permission from the partners is salvation. Stripping travel of trade is better; if he trades, his reward is not decreased, like the warrior if he trades, as the commentator mentioned in al-Siyar. As for avoiding ostentation, fame-seeking, and pride outwardly or inwardly, it is obligatory. Mixing trade with this category, as in Fath al-Qadir, is something to be cautious of. As for riding in the mahmil, some disliked it out of fear of what we mentioned, and some did not dislike it if it is safe from that; in reality there is no difference. Riding a camel is better, and Hajj on a donkey is disliked; it appears to be tanzihi by evidence of the superiority of its opposite. Walking is better than riding for one who can bear it, and not...
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the etiquettes of the Hajj journey. The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents a series of rulings and recommendations for the pilgrim. He begins by advising the pilgrim to seek guidance (istikhara) and to earn lawful spending (nafaqa halal), noting that while Hajj performed with unlawful funds fulfills the obligation, it is not accepted for reward. The pilgrim must seek a righteous companion, preferably unrelated, for mutual support. Regarding hired animals (makari), the author discusses the importance of not overloading or underfeeding them, citing legal references for standard loads. He then addresses sharing provisions among the group, recommending seeking permission to avoid wrongdoing. The passage distinguishes between trade during Hajj (which does not diminish reward) and mixing it with ostentation (which is forbidden). Finally, it discusses modes of travel: riding in a mahmil (litter) is disliked by some, riding a camel is best, riding a donkey is mildly disliked, and walking is superior for those able. The marginal notes clarify the meaning of 'matali'a', the weight measure 'mann', and textual variants on sharing and seeking permission.

Key Terms
سقوط الفرض (suqut al-fard): Fulfillment of the obligation; the legal duty is discharged.
القبول (al-qubul): Acceptance for reward in the afterlife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence of performing Hajj with usurped funds?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The obligation is fulfilled but no reward is given.
C) The person is punished like one who abandons Hajj.
D) The Hajj is valid and reward is given after repentance.

Key Takeaway
Hajj with unlawful funds fulfills the obligation but is not accepted for reward.

Choosing a Righteous Hajj Companion
Recommendation for righteous Hajj companion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended qualities of a Hajj companion and explain why a non-relative is preferred.

Core Idea
A righteous companion who reminds and helps is essential; non-relatives are preferred to avoid family discord.

Traveling for Hajj requires companionship for support and spiritual benefit. The text recommends a righteous companion who will remind, console, and assist. Interestingly, it states that a companion from non-relatives is better than a relative, to distance from potential conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommendation
The text says 'لا بد له من رفيق صالح' – he must have a righteous companion. This indicates necessity (lā budda), but it is not a condition of validity; rather it is a strong recommendation (wājib or sunna).
2
List the qualities
The companion should: remind him when he forgets (yudhakkiruhu idhā nasiya), console him when he panics (yusabbiruhu idhā jazi'a), and help him when he is unable (yu'īnuhu idhā 'ajaza).
3
Understand the preference for non-relatives
Some righteous (ba'd al-sālihīn) considered it better (awlā) to take a companion from non-relatives than relatives, to distance from the sphere of certainty (saḥat al-qaṭ'iyya). Possibly because relatives may lead to arguments or family obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
سفره في ذلك الوقت لا في نفس الحج فإنه خير، وكذا يستخير الله في ذلك. ويجتهد في تحصيل نفقة حلال فإنه لا يقبل بالنفقة الحرام كما ورد في الحديث مع أنه يسقط الفرض عنه معها وإن كانت مغصوبة، ولا تنافي بين سقوطه وعدم قبوله فلا يثاب لعدم القبول، ولا يعاقب في الآخرة عقاب تارك الحج. ولا بد له من رفيق صالح يذكره إذا نسي ويصبره إذا جزع ويعينه إذا عجز، وكونه من الأجانب أولى من الأقارب عند بعض الصالحين تبعداً من ساحة القطعية. ويرى المكاري ما يحمله ولا يحمل أكثر منه إلا بإذنه، وقد ذكر عن بعض السلف ويقال إنه الشافعي وقيل ابن المبارك، وقيل ابن القاسم صاحب الإمام مالك أنه دفع إليه مطالعة ليحملها إلى إنسان فامتنع من حملها بدون إذن المكاري لكونه لم يشارطه على ذلك ورعاً من فاعله وكذا يحترز من تحميلها فوق ما تطيق ومن تقليل علفها المعتاد بلا ضرورة ولو مملوكه له وفي إجارة الخلاصة : حمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً، وحمل الحمار مائة وخمسون مناً. قالوا ولا يشارك في الزاد واجتماع الرفقة كل يوم على طعام أحدهم أحل. وينبغي أن يستثنى ما إذا علمت المسامحة بينهما فله المشاركة وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاه مخلص. وتجريد السفر عن التجارة أحسن، ولو اتجر لا ينقص ثوابه كالغازي إذا اتجر كما ذكره الشارح في السير. وأما عن الرياء والسمعة والفخر ظاهراً أو باطناً ففرض وخلط التجارة بهذا القسم كما في فتح القدير مما ينبغي . وأما الركوب في المحمل فكرهه بعضهم خوفاً مما ذكرنا، ولم يكرهه بعضهم إذا د عن ذلك ففي التحقيق لا اختلاف وركوب الجمل أفضل، ويكره الحج على الحمار والظاهر أنها تنزيهية بدليل أفضلية ما قابله والمشي أفضل من الركوب لمن يطيقه ولا

قوله: (أنه دفع إليه (مطالعة الذي في النهر : بطاقة وهي الرقعة الصغيرة المربوطة بالثوب التي فيها رقم ثمنه كما في القاموس والمراد بها هنا المكتوب قوله: (وفي إجارة الخلاصة الخ) قال الرملي : نقله فيها عن الفتاوى الصغرى وأقول : لعمري هذا إحجاف على الحمار وإنصاف في حق الجمل فتأمل. وذكر في الجوهرة أن المن ستة وعشرون أوقية والأوقية سبعة مثاقيل وهي عشرة دراهم والمائتان وأربعون مناً . الوسق، فيكون حمل الجمل وسقاً، بالأرطال وهو الرملية تسعة وستون رطلاً وثلث رطل وهو قنطار دمشقي تقريباً على أن الرطل الرملي تسعمائة درهم ويلائم تفسير الوسق بحمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً ولا يلائم التفسير بغيره تأمل.

قوله : (وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاء مخلص) كذا في بعض النسخ، وفي بعضها وإلا فلا يشارك وفي بعضها وإلا لا ولو شارك فالاستحلال مخلص وهي أحسن قوله: (خوفاً مما
His travel at that time, not in Hajj itself, is good, and likewise he seeks guidance from Allah in that. And he strives to acquire lawful spending, for it is not accepted with unlawful spending as related in the hadith, even though the obligation is fulfilled with it even if it is usurped. There is no contradiction between fulfillment and lack of acceptance; he is not rewarded due to lack of acceptance, nor is he punished in the afterlife with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. He must have a righteous companion who reminds him when he forgets, consoles him when he panics, and helps him when he is unable. A companion from non-relatives is preferable to relatives according to some righteous, to distance from the sphere of certainty. And the camel-owner sees what he carries and does not carry more than that except with his permission. It has been mentioned from some predecessors, it is said that it was al-Shafi'i, or Ibn al-Mubarak, or Ibn al-Qasim, companion of Imam Malik, that a note was given to him to carry to a person, and he refrained from carrying it without the permission of the camel-owner because he had not stipulated that, out of piety. Similarly, he avoids loading it beyond its capacity and reducing its customary fodder without necessity, even if it is his own property. In the Ijarah of al-Khulasah: the load of a camel is two hundred and forty mann, and the load of a donkey is one hundred and fifty mann. They said: He should not share in the provisions, and gathering of the group each day for the food of one of them is better. It should be excepted when mutual leniency is known between them, so he may share. Otherwise, if he shares, then seeking permission from the partners is salvation. Stripping travel of trade is better; if he trades, his reward is not decreased, like the warrior if he trades, as the commentator mentioned in al-Siyar. As for avoiding ostentation, fame-seeking, and pride outwardly or inwardly, it is obligatory. Mixing trade with this category, as in Fath al-Qadir, is something to be cautious of. As for riding in the mahmil, some disliked it out of fear of what we mentioned, and some did not dislike it if it is safe from that; in reality there is no difference. Riding a camel is better, and Hajj on a donkey is disliked; it appears to be tanzihi by evidence of the superiority of its opposite. Walking is better than riding for one who can bear it, and not...
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the etiquettes of the Hajj journey. The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents a series of rulings and recommendations for the pilgrim. He begins by advising the pilgrim to seek guidance (istikhara) and to earn lawful spending (nafaqa halal), noting that while Hajj performed with unlawful funds fulfills the obligation, it is not accepted for reward. The pilgrim must seek a righteous companion, preferably unrelated, for mutual support. Regarding hired animals (makari), the author discusses the importance of not overloading or underfeeding them, citing legal references for standard loads. He then addresses sharing provisions among the group, recommending seeking permission to avoid wrongdoing. The passage distinguishes between trade during Hajj (which does not diminish reward) and mixing it with ostentation (which is forbidden). Finally, it discusses modes of travel: riding in a mahmil (litter) is disliked by some, riding a camel is best, riding a donkey is mildly disliked, and walking is superior for those able. The marginal notes clarify the meaning of 'matali'a', the weight measure 'mann', and textual variants on sharing and seeking permission.

Key Terms
الرفيق الصالح (al-rafīq al-ṣāliḥ): Righteous companion; one who is religious and supportive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a non-relative companion preferred?
A) Relatives are less righteous.
B) To avoid potential conflict (sāhat al-qaṭ'iyya).
C) Relatives cannot help when in panic.
D) Non-relatives are more knowledgeable.

Key Takeaway
A righteous companion is essential for the Hajj journey, and a non-relative is preferred to avoid familial tension.

Rights of the Makari and Animal Welfare
Rulings on hired mounts and animal treatment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations and etiquettes regarding hired animals in Hajj travel, including load limits and permission for carrying extra items.

Core Idea
The makari's property rights and animal welfare must be respected: no overloading without permission and no underfeeding without necessity.

When hiring a mount (makari) for Hajj, the pilgrim must consider both the owner's rights and the animal's well-being. The text addresses the makari's right to see the load, not to carry more than agreed, and to avoid overloading and reducing fodder. It also gives standard load weights from al-Khulasah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the makari's rights
The makari has the right to see (yarā) what he is carrying and should not carry more than that load without explicit permission.
2
Learn from the story of the predecessors
The author mentions that some early scholars (al-Shafi'i, Ibn al-Mubarak, Ibn al-Qasim) refrained from carrying a note (matali'a) without the makari's permission, showing piety.
3
Understand animal welfare provisions
The pilgrim must avoid loading the animal beyond its capacity (fawq mā tuṭīq) and avoid reducing its customary fodder without necessity, even if the animal is his own property.
4
Note the standard loads
Al-Khulasah states: a camel's load is 240 mann, a donkey's is 150 mann. This provides a practical guideline.
1 mann = 26 awqiya; 240 mann = 1 wasaq.

Source Text

Sharing Provisions and Trade During Hajj
Rulings on sharing provisions and engaging in trade.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the etiquettes of sharing provisions and engaging in trade during Hajj, and identify when permission is required.

Core Idea
Sharing provisions with companions requires mutual leniency or permission; trade is permissible but stripping travel of trade is better.

The passage discusses social and economic aspects of the Hajj journey. Regarding food, it is recommended not to share provisions (zād) but to take turns hosting, unless there is known leniency. If sharing occurs without permission, seeking exoneration is necessary. Regarding trade, it is better to focus solely on Hajj, but if one trades, the reward is not diminished, similar to a warrior. However, mixing trade with ostentation is dangerous.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default ruling on sharing provisions
The text says 'ولا يشارك في الزاد' – he should not share in the provisions. Instead, it is better each day for one of the group to host the meal. But there is an exception: if mutual leniency (musāmaha) is known, then sharing is allowed.
2
Identify the requirement for permission
If one shares without that leniency, then seeking permission (istihlāl) from the partners is salvation (mukhlis). The marginal note clarifies that the correct text says 'وإلا لا يشارك ولو شارك فالاستحلال من الشركاء مخلص'.
3
Analyze the ruling on trade
The text states that stripping travel of trade (tajrīd al-safar 'an al-tijāra) is better (ahsān). However, if one does trade, his reward (thawāb) is not decreased, likened to a warrior who trades.
4
Distinguish between types of trade
There is a critical distinction: trade mixed with ostentation (riyā', sum'a, fakhr) is something to be cautious about (mimmā yanbaghī), whereas permissible trade without those vices does not diminish reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

سفره في ذلك الوقت لا في نفس الحج فإنه خير، وكذا يستخير الله في ذلك. ويجتهد في تحصيل نفقة حلال فإنه لا يقبل بالنفقة الحرام كما ورد في الحديث مع أنه يسقط الفرض عنه معها وإن كانت مغصوبة، ولا تنافي بين سقوطه وعدم قبوله فلا يثاب لعدم القبول، ولا يعاقب في الآخرة عقاب تارك الحج. ولا بد له من رفيق صالح يذكره إذا نسي ويصبره إذا جزع ويعينه إذا عجز، وكونه من الأجانب أولى من الأقارب عند بعض الصالحين تبعداً من ساحة القطعية. ويرى المكاري ما يحمله ولا يحمل أكثر منه إلا بإذنه، وقد ذكر عن بعض السلف ويقال إنه الشافعي وقيل ابن المبارك، وقيل ابن القاسم صاحب الإمام مالك أنه دفع إليه مطالعة ليحملها إلى إنسان فامتنع من حملها بدون إذن المكاري لكونه لم يشارطه على ذلك ورعاً من فاعله وكذا يحترز من تحميلها فوق ما تطيق ومن تقليل علفها المعتاد بلا ضرورة ولو مملوكه له وفي إجارة الخلاصة : حمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً، وحمل الحمار مائة وخمسون مناً. قالوا ولا يشارك في الزاد واجتماع الرفقة كل يوم على طعام أحدهم أحل. وينبغي أن يستثنى ما إذا علمت المسامحة بينهما فله المشاركة وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاه مخلص. وتجريد السفر عن التجارة أحسن، ولو اتجر لا ينقص ثوابه كالغازي إذا اتجر كما ذكره الشارح في السير. وأما عن الرياء والسمعة والفخر ظاهراً أو باطناً ففرض وخلط التجارة بهذا القسم كما في فتح القدير مما ينبغي . وأما الركوب في المحمل فكرهه بعضهم خوفاً مما ذكرنا، ولم يكرهه بعضهم إذا د عن ذلك ففي التحقيق لا اختلاف وركوب الجمل أفضل، ويكره الحج على الحمار والظاهر أنها تنزيهية بدليل أفضلية ما قابله والمشي أفضل من الركوب لمن يطيقه ولا

قوله: (أنه دفع إليه (مطالعة الذي في النهر : بطاقة وهي الرقعة الصغيرة المربوطة بالثوب التي فيها رقم ثمنه كما في القاموس والمراد بها هنا المكتوب قوله: (وفي إجارة الخلاصة الخ) قال الرملي : نقله فيها عن الفتاوى الصغرى وأقول : لعمري هذا إحجاف على الحمار وإنصاف في حق الجمل فتأمل. وذكر في الجوهرة أن المن ستة وعشرون أوقية والأوقية سبعة مثاقيل وهي عشرة دراهم والمائتان وأربعون مناً . الوسق، فيكون حمل الجمل وسقاً، بالأرطال وهو الرملية تسعة وستون رطلاً وثلث رطل وهو قنطار دمشقي تقريباً على أن الرطل الرملي تسعمائة درهم ويلائم تفسير الوسق بحمل البعير مائتان وأربعون مناً ولا يلائم التفسير بغيره تأمل.

قوله : (وإلا وشارك فالاستحلال من الشركاء مخلص) كذا في بعض النسخ، وفي بعضها وإلا فلا يشارك وفي بعضها وإلا لا ولو شارك فالاستحلال مخلص وهي أحسن قوله: (خوفاً مما
His travel at that time, not in Hajj itself, is good, and likewise he seeks guidance from Allah in that. And he strives to acquire lawful spending, for it is not accepted with unlawful spending as related in the hadith, even though the obligation is fulfilled with it even if it is usurped. There is no contradiction between fulfillment and lack of acceptance; he is not rewarded due to lack of acceptance, nor is he punished in the afterlife with the punishment of one who abandons Hajj. He must have a righteous companion who reminds him when he forgets, consoles him when he panics, and helps him when he is unable. A companion from non-relatives is preferable to relatives according to some righteous, to distance from the sphere of certainty. And the camel-owner sees what he carries and does not carry more than that except with his permission. It has been mentioned from some predecessors, it is said that it was al-Shafi'i, or Ibn al-Mubarak, or Ibn al-Qasim, companion of Imam Malik, that a note was given to him to carry to a person, and he refrained from carrying it without the permission of the camel-owner because he had not stipulated that, out of piety. Similarly, he avoids loading it beyond its capacity and reducing its customary fodder without necessity, even if it is his own property. In the Ijarah of al-Khulasah: the load of a camel is two hundred and forty mann, and the load of a donkey is one hundred and fifty mann. They said: He should not share in the provisions, and gathering of the group each day for the food of one of them is better. It should be excepted when mutual leniency is known between them, so he may share. Otherwise, if he shares, then seeking permission from the partners is salvation. Stripping travel of trade is better; if he trades, his reward is not decreased, like the warrior if he trades, as the commentator mentioned in al-Siyar. As for avoiding ostentation, fame-seeking, and pride outwardly or inwardly, it is obligatory. Mixing trade with this category, as in Fath al-Qadir, is something to be cautious of. As for riding in the mahmil, some disliked it out of fear of what we mentioned, and some did not dislike it if it is safe from that; in reality there is no difference. Riding a camel is better, and Hajj on a donkey is disliked; it appears to be tanzihi by evidence of the superiority of its opposite. Walking is better than riding for one who can bear it, and not...
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the etiquettes of the Hajj journey. The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents a series of rulings and recommendations for the pilgrim. He begins by advising the pilgrim to seek guidance (istikhara) and to earn lawful spending (nafaqa halal), noting that while Hajj performed with unlawful funds fulfills the obligation, it is not accepted for reward. The pilgrim must seek a righteous companion, preferably unrelated, for mutual support. Regarding hired animals (makari), the author discusses the importance of not overloading or underfeeding them, citing legal references for standard loads. He then addresses sharing provisions among the group, recommending seeking permission to avoid wrongdoing. The passage distinguishes between trade during Hajj (which does not diminish reward) and mixing it with ostentation (which is forbidden). Finally, it discusses modes of travel: riding in a mahmil (litter) is disliked by some, riding a camel is best, riding a donkey is mildly disliked, and walking is superior for those able. The marginal notes clarify the meaning of 'matali'a', the weight measure 'mann', and textual variants on sharing and seeking permission.

Key Terms
المسامحة (al-musāmaha): Mutual leniency or generosity.
الاستحلال (al-istihlāl): Seeking permission or exoneration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on trade during Hajj travel?
A) It is forbidden and reduces reward.
B) It is permissible and does not reduce reward.
C) It is permissible only if one does not profit.
D) It is recommended as a sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Sharing provisions requires mutual leniency or permission; permissible trade does not diminish Hajj reward.

Avoiding Ostentation and Modes of Travel
Rulings on sincerity and transport preferences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of avoiding ostentation and explain the relative merits of different modes of transport for Hajj.

Core Idea
Avoiding ostentation is obligatory; walking is better than riding, and camel is better than donkey or mahmil.

The passage concludes with important spiritual and practical guidance. First, it emphasizes that avoiding riyā' (show-off), sum'a (reputation-seeking), and fakhr (pride) is farḍ (obligatory). Mixing trade with these is warned against. Then it discusses transport: riding in a mahmil (litter) is disliked by some, but if safe, there is no disagreement. Riding a camel is best, riding a donkey is makruh tanzihi, and walking is superior for those able.

Guided Path
1
Understand the obligatory nature of sincerity
The text states 'أما عن الرياء والسمعة والفخر ظاهراً أو باطناً ففرض' – avoiding these is obligatory (fard). This is a general ruling not limited to Hajj but very relevant.
2
Identify the warning about mixing trade
The text says 'وخلط التجارة بهذا القسم كما في فتح القدير مما ينبغي' – mixing trade with these categories is something to be cautious about. This implies that trade done with ostentation is sinful and can affect the Hajj's reward.
3
Analyze the differences on riding in mahmil
Some disliked it (karihahu ba'duhum) due to fear of ostentation, while others did not dislike it if safe (idhā dufi'a 'an dhālika). The author concludes that in reality there is no difference (lā ikhtilāf), meaning both are acceptable depending on intention.
4
Rank the modes of transport
Riding a camel is better (afḍal). Riding a donkey is disliked (makrūh) but it appears to be tanzīhī (slightly disliked) because its opposite (camel) is better. Walking is better than riding for those who can bear it, but the text adds 'and not' (ولا) possibly meaning 'and not for those who cannot'.
The text is slightly corrupted at the end: 'ولا' may be part of the next sentence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Hajj Obliged Once: Is It Immediate or Can It Be Delayed?
Explains that Hajj is obligatory once and the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether it is immediate or can be delayed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on fawr and tarakhi for Hajj, identify the evidence for each, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once; the Hanafi school's majority holds it must be done immediately, but a minority allows delay, with different consequences for the one who delays.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the Hajj obligation. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that while Hajj is fard once in a lifetime, there is disagreement among the Hanafi imams on whether it must be performed as soon as one is capable or can be delayed. We will explore the evidence on both sides and the practical legal consequences that follow from each position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core ruling: Hajj is obligatory once
The text begins by stating that Hajj is fard (wajib in Hanafi terminology) only once in a lifetime. This is based on the Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:97) and prophetic hadith. Note also the distinction with zakat, which repeats yearly due to its different cause.
The once-only nature is not disputed.
2
Define fawr and tarakhi
Linguistically, fawr means immediate performance, like the boiling of a pot. Tarakhi means permissibility of delay, though haste is better. Understand these terms as they are the subject of the ikhtilaf.
The author provides the lexical origin of fawr.
3
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa (in the more correct narration) and Abu Yusuf hold fawr (immediate). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds tarakhi (delay is permissible, hastening better). There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa agreeing with Muhammad.
label both sides and their proponents.
4
Examine the evidence for each position
Muhammad's evidence: the command (amr) does not indicate time, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed his own Hajj from year nine to year ten. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's evidence: precaution (ihtiyat) due to the risk of death; the Prophet's delay is a special case because he knew he would live.
The Quranic imperative is common to both; the dispute hinges on whether the command implies immediacy.
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
The thamarah: on fawr view, delaying causes sin and fisq (rejected testimony). On tarakhi view, no sin. The mufta bihi is fawr, as it is considered the more correct narration and the view of Abu Yusuf.
This shows that ikhtilaf is not purely academic; it affects real legal status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال: (فرض مرة على الفور) أي فرض الحج في العمرة مرة واحدة في أول سني الإمكان. والفور في اللغة من فور القدر غليانها، وفعل ذلك من فوره أي من وجهه وهو من فور القدر قبل أن تسكن قال الله تعالى من فورهم (هذا) [آل عمران: ١٢٥] ولم يذكر المصنف فرضيته قصداً لأنها من المسائل الاعتقادية فليست من مسائل الفقه لأن مسائله ظنية، وإنما ذكره توطئة لما بعده ودليله القرآني والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبیلا) [آل عمران: ٩٧] والسنة كثيرة. أما كونه لا يتعدد فلأن سببه وهو البيت كذلك، وأما تكرر وجوب الزكاة مع اتحاد المال فلأن سببه هو النامي تقديراً وتقدير النماء دائر مع حولان الحول إذا كان المال معداً للاستنماء في الزمان المستقبل، وتقدير النماء الثابت في هذا الحول غير تقدير النماء في حول آخر، فالمال هذا النماء غير المجموع منه ومن الآخر فيتعدد حكماً كتعدد الوجوب بتعدد النصاب، ولرواية أحمد مرفوعاً «الحج مرة فمن زاد فهو تطوع» (١). وأما كونه على الفور فهو قول أبي يوسف وأصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد يجب على التراخي والتعجيل أفضل. كذا في الخلاصة وتحقيقه أن الأمر إنما هو طلب المأمور به ولا دلالة له على الفور ولا على التراخي فأخذ به محمد وقواه بأنه عليه السلام سنة عشر وفرضية الحج كانت سنة تسع فبعث أبا بكر حج بالناس فيها ولم يحج هو إلى القابلة. وأما أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف فقالا : الاحتياط في تعيين أول الإمكان لأن الحج له وقت معين في السنة والموت في سنة غير نادر فتأخيره بعد التمكن في وقته تعريض له على الفوات فلا يجوز، وبهذا حصل الجواب عن تأخيره عليه الصلاة والسلام إذ لا يتحقق في حقه تعريض الفوات وهو الموجب للفور لأنه كان يعلم أنه يعيش حتى يحج ويعلم الناس مناسكهم تكميلاً للتبليغ . وبهذا التقرير علم أن الفورية ظنية لأن دليل الاحتياط ظني ومقتضاه الوجوب فإذا أخره وأداه بعد ذلك وقع أداء ويأثم بالتأخير لترك الواجب، وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما إذا أخره فعلى الصحيح يأثم ويصير فاسقاً مردود الشهادة، وعلى قول محمد لا يأثم وترد رواية عن أبي حنيفة توافق قول محمد.
Then he said: (Obligatory once, immediately) meaning Hajj is obligatory in a lifetime once in the first years of capability. 'Fawr' linguistically from the boiling of a pot, and doing something 'min fawrihi' means immediately, before the pot settles. Allah said: 'from their fawr' [Al Imran 125]. The author did not mention its being obligatory intentionally because it is a creedal matter, not a legal one, since legal matters are speculative. He only mentioned it as a prelude to what follows. Its Quranic proof is: 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able to find a way' [Al Imran 97], and there are many hadiths. As for it not being repeated, it is because its cause—the House—is likewise [singular]. As for the repetition of zakat obligation despite the unity of wealth, it is because its cause is the wealth that grows by estimation, and the estimation of growth revolves with the passing of the year when the wealth is prepared for growth in future time. The estimation of growth established in this year is different from the estimation of growth in another year, so the wealth of this growth is not the same as the sum of it and the other, so it becomes multiple legally, like the multiplicity of obligation due to multiplicity of nisab. And due to the narration of Ahmad with marfu': 'Hajj is once; whoever does more, it is voluntary.' As for it being immediate, that is the statement of Abu Yusuf and the more correct of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, while according to Muhammad it is obligatory with delay (tarakhi) and hastening is better. This is in al-Khulasah. Its verification: the command is merely a demand for the commanded act and has no indication of immediacy or delay, so Muhammad adopted that and strengthened it by the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Hajj in year ten while the obligation of Hajj was in year nine; he sent Abu Bakr to lead the Hajj in that year and he himself did not perform it until the following year. As for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, they said: precaution requires specifying the first possibility, because Hajj has a specific time in the year and death in a year is not rare; delaying after being able in its time exposes it to being missed, so it is not permissible. With this, the answer to the Prophet's delay is given, for the risk of being missed does not apply to him, as he knew he would live to perform Hajj and teach the people their rites, completing the conveyance. From this exposition, it is known that the immediacy (fawriyyah) is speculative because the proof of precaution is speculative and its requirement is obligation. If he delays and performs it later, it is performance and he sins for the delay due to abandoning the wajib. The practical consequence appears when he delays: according to the correct view, he sins and becomes a transgressor, rejected in testimony. According to Muhammad, he does not sin. And a narration from Abu Hanifa is transmitted that agrees with Muhammad.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two key rulings: (1) Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, and (2) whether it must be performed immediately (fawr) or can be delayed (tarakhi). The author begins by defining 'fawr' linguistically and notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not mention the obligatoriness of Hajj as a legal ruling because it is a matter of belief (i'tiqadi). The Quranic proof (Al Imran 97) and numerous hadiths establish its obligation once, unlike zakat which repeats yearly due to its cause being annually growing wealth. The core of the lesson is the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa (in the more correct narration) and Abu Yusuf hold that Hajj is wajib on the spot (fawr), while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is wajib with delay (tarakhi) but hastening is better. The proof of each side: Muhammad argues that the command (amr) has no indication of time, and the Prophet's delay from year nine to year ten shows permissibility. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that precaution requires performing as soon as possible due to the risk of death; the Prophet's delay is a special case since he knew he would live. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if one delays, on the majority view he sins and becomes a fasiq (rejected testimony); on Muhammad's view he does not sin. A narration from Abu Hanifa also agrees with Muhammad. The preferred (mufta bihi) position is fawr, as indicated by 'asahh al-riwayatayn' and the fact that it is the view of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate performance of Hajj as soon as one is capable, without delay.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): Permissibility to delay Hajj after capability, though hastening is better.
ثمرة الاختلاف (thamarat al-ikhtilaf): The practical consequence of the legal disagreement applied to a real case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute over fawr and tarakhi?
A) If one delays, he must repeat Hajj
B) If one delays, on the correct view he sins and becomes a fasiq whose testimony is rejected
C) If one delays, his Hajj is invalid
D) There is no practical difference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that Hajj must be performed immediately upon capability; delaying without excuse is sinful and harms one's legal integrity.

Hajj is Obligatory Once in a Lifetime
Ruling stated with proof and comparative analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the frequency of Hajj and explain why it is not repeated like zakat.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard 'ayn once, because its cause—the House—is one, not recurring.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a foundational ruling: Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime, and it must be performed at the earliest opportunity. The author explains why this obligation is not repeated annually, contrasting it with zakat, and provides Quranic and hadith proofs. By understanding the cause (sabab) of each obligation, you will grasp the logic behind the frequency of acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State clearly what the passage rules: Hajj is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) once in a lifetime, and it must be done immediately upon ability (fawr).
The Arabic phrase 'فرض مرة على الفور' summarizes the entire ruling.
2
Define the term 'fawr'
Understand the linguistic meaning from boiling pot and its legal implication: prompt performance before any delay. The author quotes Quran 3:125 to illustrate 'from their very rush'.
Fawr contrasts with tarakhi (delay allowed), a separate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 3:97 as the primary evidence. Identify the imperative 'حج' and note that in Hanafi usul, the command form indicates obligation (fard). This dalil is qat'i in both transmission and meaning.
The hadith 'الحج مرة فمن زاد فهو تطوع' is also cited from Ahmad.
4
Analyze the cause theory
The author explains that Hajj is not repeated because its cause (sabab) is the House itself, which is one. For zakat, the cause is the annual growth of wealth, which repeats. This distinction shows how the sabab determines frequency.
The passage uses this comparative analysis to preempt a possible objection: why zakat is repeated but Hajj is not.
5
Apply the distinction
Now apply the principle: any act of worship whose cause is singular (like the House) is obligatory once; any act whose cause is recurrent (like annual growth) is repeated. This is a key Hanafi method for deriving rulings from causes.
This step builds the skill of identifying sabab to understand the hukm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فرض مرة على الفور أي فرض الحج في العمرة مرة واحدة في أول سني الإمكان. والفور في اللغة من فور القدر غليانها، وفعل ذلك من فوره أي من وجهه وهو من فور القدر قبل أن تسكن قال الله تعالى من فورهم (هذا) [آل عمران: ١٢٥] ولم يذكر المصنف فرضيته قصداً لأنها من المسائل الاعتقادية فليست من مسائل الفقه لأن مسائله ظنية، وإنما ذكره توطئة لما بعده ودليله القرآني والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبیلا) [آل عمران: ٩٧] والسنة كثيرة. أما كونه لا يتعدد فلأن سببه وهو البيت كذلك، وأما تكرر وجوب الزكاة مع اتحاد المال فلأن سببه هو النامي تقديراً وتقدير النماء دائر مع حولان الحول إذا كان المال معداً للاستنماء في الزمان المستقبل، وتقدير النماء الثابت في هذا الحول غير تقدير النماء في حول آخر، فالمال هذا النماء غير المجموع منه ومن الآخر فيتعدد حكماً كتعدد الوجوب بتعدد النصاب، ولرواية أحمد مرفوعاً «الحج مرة فمن زاد فهو تطوع» (١).
His saying: (Obligatory once on the immediate basis), meaning the obligation of Hajj in one's lifetime is once at the earliest time of ability. "Al-fawr" in language is from the boiling of a pot, and doing something immediately means from its onset before it settles. Allah said: "from their very rush" [Al-Imran:125]. The author did not mention its obligation deliberately because it is among matters of belief, not fiqh, since fiqh issues are speculative; he only mentioned it as a prelude to what follows. Its proof from the Quran: "And due to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able to find a way" [Al-Imran:97], and the Sunnah is abundant. As for it not being multiple, it is because its cause—the House—is also one. As for the repetition of zakat obligation despite the unity of wealth, it is because its cause is the growth estimation, and the estimation of growth revolves with the passing of the year if the wealth is prepared for growth in the future. The growth established in one year is not the same as growth in another year, so the wealth of this growth is not combined with that of another, thus it becomes multiple legally, like the multiplicity of obligation with multiplicity of nisab. And by the narration of Ahmad raised: "Hajj is once, and whoever does extra, it is voluntary."
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by explaining the matn: Hajj is fard once in a lifetime, and it must be performed at the earliest opportunity (fawr). The author clarifies that Hajj is not repeated like zakat, because the cause of Hajj (the House) is one, while zakat's cause is the annual growth of wealth, which recurs. The proof is from Quran (3:97) and the hadith 'Hajj is once, and what is extra is voluntary.' The passage also notes that the author deliberately omitted the obligation itself from fiqh discussion because it is a belief matter, but mentions it as a foundation.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A legal obligation derived from definitive evidence; neglecting it incurs sin.
فور (fawr): Immediate performance at the earliest possible time.
استطاعة (istita'ah): Ability in terms of health, wealth, and safety to perform Hajj.
سبب (sabab): The cause or occasion that triggers a legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Hajj not repeated every year like zakat?
A) Because the House is one, so its cause is singular.
B) Because Hajj is physically harder than zakat.
C) Because the hadith says 'once' without any reasoning.
D) Because the obligation is only for the wealthy.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard 'ayn once; its cause (the House) is singular, so the obligation is not recurrent.
