The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Whether Hajj is Obligatory Immediately (Fawr) or Delayed (Tarakhi)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fawr vs tarakhi in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the immediacy of Hajj, and evaluate the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
Hajj must be performed at the earliest opportunity — precaution against death dictates immediacy.

This passage examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: is the obligation of Hajj immediate (fawr) or can it be delayed (tarakhi)? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that precaution requires performing Hajj at the first possible time, while Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that the command itself is silent on timing. We will explore the evidence of each side and the practical implications for sin and being a fasiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State who holds fawr (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and who holds tarakhi (Muhammad).
The text says 'قول أبي يوسف وأصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة' for fawr.
2
Understand Muhammad's proof
Muhammad's evidence: the command has no time indication, and the Prophet delayed his Hajj from year 9 to year 10.
Command is silent; the Prophet's action is his proof.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's proof
They argue precaution: Hajj has a specific time, death is possible, so delaying risks missing it.
The Prophet's delay was exceptional due to his knowledge.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
On fawr, delay incurs sin and fasiq; on tarakhi, no sin unless death occurs without performing.
Also, fasiq status requires persistence on fawr view.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is fawr (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), as per the text.
Muhammad's view is a valid alternative but not the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كونه على الفور فهو قول أبي يوسف وأصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد يجب على التراخي والتعجيل أفضل. كذا في الخلاصة وتحقيقه أن الأمر إنما هو طلب المأمور به ولا دلالة له على الفور ولا على التراخي فأخذ به محمد وقواه بأنه عليه السلام سنة عشر وفرضية الحج كانت سنة تسع فبعث أبا بكر حج بالناس فيها ولم يحج هو إلى القابلة. وأما أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف فقالا : الاحتياط في تعيين أول الإمكان لأن الحج له وقت معين في السنة والموت في سنة غير نادر فتأخيره بعد التمكن في وقته تعريض له على الفوات فلا يجوز، وبهذا حصل الجواب عن تأخيره عليه الصلاة والسلام إذ لا يتحقق في حقه تعريض الفوات وهو الموجب للفور لأنه كان يعلم أنه يعيش حتى يحج ويعلم الناس مناسكهم تكميلاً للتبليغ . وبهذا التقرير علم أن الفورية ظنية لأن دليل الاحتياط ظني ومقتضاه الوجوب فإذا أخره وأداه بعد ذلك وقع أداء ويأثم بالتأخير لترك الواجب، وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما إذا أخره فعلى الصحيح يأثم ويصير فاسقاً مردود الشهادة، وعلى قول محمد لا، وينبغي أن لا فاسقاً من أول سنة على المذهب الصحيح بل لا بد أن يتوالى يصير عليه سنون لأن التأخير في هذه الحالة صغيرة لأنه مكروه تحريماً ولا يصير فاسقاً بارتكابها مرة بل لا بد من الإصرار عليها، وإذا حج في آخر عمره ارتفع الإثم اتفاقاً قال الشارح : ولو مات ولم يحج أثم بالإجماع ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن المشايخ اختلفوا على قول محمد؛ فقيل يأثم مطلقاً، وقيل لا يأثم مطلقاً، وقيل: إن خاف الفوات بأن ظهرت له مخائل الموت في قلبه فأخره حتى مات أثم، وإن فجأه الموت لا يأثم وينبغي اعتماد القول الأول وتضعيف القول الثاني لأنه حينئذ يفوت القول بفرضية الحج لأن فائدتها الإثم عند عدم الفعل، سواء كان مضيقاً أو موسعاً اللهم إلا أن يقال : فائدتها على هذا القول وجوب الإيصاء عليه قبيل موته فإذا لم يوص يأثم لترك هذا الواجب لا لترك الحج.
As for it being immediate, it is the saying of Abu Yusuf and the sounder of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, while according to Muhammad it is obligatory with delay and expediting is better. Thus in al-Khulasa and its verification: the command is only a request for the commanded act and has no indication of immediacy or delay, so Muhammad adopted this and strengthened it by that the Prophet (peace be upon him) [performed Hajj] in year ten while the obligation of Hajj was in year nine, so he sent Abu Bakr to lead the people in Hajj that year and did not himself perform Hajj until the next year. As for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, they said: precaution requires determining the earliest possibility because Hajj has a specific time in the year and death in a given year is not rare, so delaying after being able in its time exposes it to being missed and is not permissible. By this the answer to the Prophet's delay is obtained, since in his case there was no risk of missing it, which is what necessitates immediacy, because he knew he would live to perform Hajj and teach people their rituals to complete the conveyance. By this analysis it is known that immediacy is speculative because the evidence of precaution is speculative and its requirement is obligation; if one delays and performs it afterwards, it counts as performance and he sins for the delay for leaving the obligatory. The fruit of the difference appears when he delays: according to the sound view he sins and becomes a fasiq, rejected in testimony, while according to Muhammad no. And it should be that he does not become a fasiq from the first year on the correct madhhab, but rather there must be consecutive years, because the delay in this case is a minor sin since it is makruh tahrimi, and one does not become a fasiq by committing it once, but only by persistence. If he performs Hajj at the end of his life, the sin is removed by agreement. The commentator said: If he dies without performing Hajj, he sins by consensus. This is not hidden, for the mashayikh differed on Muhammad's view: it is said he sins absolutely, it is said he does not sin absolutely, and it is said: if he feared being missed by signs of death in his heart and delayed until death, he sins; if death came suddenly, he does not sin. And the first view should be relied upon and the second weakened, because then the statement that Hajj is fard would be lost, since its benefit is sin when not performed, whether the time is narrow or broad. Unless it is said: its benefit on this view is the obligation to make a bequest before death; if he does not bequest, he sins for leaving this obligation, not for leaving Hajj.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It discusses whether Hajj is wajib immediately (fawr) or can be delayed (tarakhi). Abu Hanifa (the preferred view) and Abu Yusuf hold fawr based on precaution against death. Muhammad holds tarakhi because the command itself has no time specification, and the Prophet delayed his own Hajj by one year after its obligation. The commentator explains the reasoning of each side and the practical consequence: on the fawr view, delaying results in sin and fasiq; on the tarakhi view, no sin unless death occurs. The text also discusses when sin is incurred and when one becomes fasiq.

Key Terms
فورية (fawriyyah): The legal immediacy of an obligation; performance at the earliest opportunity.
تراخي (tarakhi): Permissibility to delay an obligation beyond the first opportunity.
إثم (ithm): Sin incurred by leaving a wajib; in this context, sin for delaying Hajj beyond first ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what happens if one delays Hajj after becoming able and later performs it?
A) No sin, because obligation is on tarakhi
B) He sins for the delay and becomes a fasiq
C) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated
D) He must pay a penalty (dam)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that Hajj is obligatory immediately; delay incurs sin and can make one a fasiq.

The Hanafi Position on Additional Hajj: Nafl, Not Obligatory
Inter-madhhab dispute on classification of additional Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that additional Hajj is nafl, explain the Shafi'i position that it is fard kifayah, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For Hanafis, Hajj is fard once; extra Hajj is nafl—and nafl Hajj is better than voluntary charity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: the legal classification of Hajj performed more than once in a lifetime. While the Hanafi school firmly holds that only the first Hajj is obligatory (fard 'ayn) and any subsequent one is voluntary (nafl), the Shafi'i school considers extra Hajj a communal obligation (fard kifayah). The passage also asserts the Hanafi preference for nafl Hajj over voluntary charity. Understanding this difference clarifies when a Muslim is sinning for not performing extra Hajj and when the community bears collective responsibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: additional Hajj is nafl (voluntary). Note the source phrase 'فرض مرة' (obligatory once) from the base text.
This is the default position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The Shafi'is hold that additional Hajj is fard kifayah: a communal duty to maintain the annual pilgrimage.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi rely on the hadith: 'الحج مرة فمن زاد فهو تطوع' (Hajj is once; whoever adds is doing voluntary). This is a direct textual evidence.
The opposing proof is based on analogy from general obligation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In Hanafi, there is no sin for omitting extra Hajj; in Shafi'i, if no one performs, the whole community sins.
This affects fatwa and communal responsibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi). The passage also asserts that nafl Hajj is better than voluntary charity, reinforcing its merit.
The tarjih is based on explicit text (nas) over qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلم من قوله «فرض مرة» أن ما زاد عليها فهو تطوع ويشهد له الحديث السابق. وعند الشافعية أن الحج لا يوصف بالنفلية بل المرة الأولى فرض عين وما زاد ففرض كفاية لأن من فروض الكفاية أن يحج البيت كل عام ولم أرده لأئمتنا بل صرحوا بالنفلية فقالوا: حج النفل أفضل الصدقة، ولا يخفى أنه إذا من كذا في التبيين. وقال نوح أفندي الظاهر أن مراده بالإثم إثم تفويت الحج لا إثم تأخيره فإنه لا يرتفع عند أبي يوسف كما مر ويدل عليه قوله : ولو مات ولم يحج أثم بالإجماع أي أثم تفويته لأنه بتأخيره عرضه على الفوات ا هـ. وفيما استدل به نظر يدل عليه بحث المؤلف في كلام الزيلعي ونقل الأقوال الثلاثة وما ذاك إلا في التأخير إذ لا شك في إثم تارك فرض قطعي وإلا لم يكن فرضاً ولا واجباً، فالمراد في الموضعين إثم التأخير يدل عليه ما قال في الفتح : ثم على ما أورده المصنف يأثم بالتأخير عن أول سني الإمكان فلو حج بعده ارتفع الإثم ا هـ. وفي القهستاني: فيأثم عند الشيخين بالتأخير إلى غيره بلا عذر إلا إذا أدى ولو في آخر عمره فإنه رافع للإثم بلا خلاف، وحينئذ فهو مخالف لما نقله عن صدر الشريعة من عدم ارتفاع الإثم عند الثاني قوله : (فقيل يأثم مطلقاً) قال في النهر : لم أر عن محمد القول بالإثم مطلقاً إذ بتقديره يرتفع الخلاف، فالظاهر أن هذا سهو، نعم المنقول عنه كما في الفتح أنه على التراخي فلا يأثم إذا حج قبل موته ، فإذا مات بعد الإمكان ولم يحج ظهر أنه أثم. ونقل القولين الآخرين ثم قال : وصحة الأول غنية عن الوجه، وعلى اعتباره قيل يظهر الإثم من السنة الأولى، وقيل من الأخيرة من سنة رأى في نفسه الضعف وقيل يأثم في الجملة غير محكوم بمعين بل علمه إلى الله تعالى ا هـ . ولا يخفى عليك ما فيه فإن ما ادعى عدم رؤيته نقله بيده وتلفظه بفيه وهو قول الفتح : فإذا مات بعد الإمكان ولم يحج ظهر أنه أثم وهو معنى قول المؤلف يأثم مطلقاً» أي سواء فجأة الموت أو لا. وقوله إذ بتقديره يرتفع الخلاف» ممنوع فإنه على قول الإمامين يأثم بالتأخير عن أول سني الإمكان كما مر وعلى قول محمد يظهر بالموت إثمه وكلام لمؤلف فيما إذا مات فالفرق واضح تدبر قوله : (فقالوا حج النفل أفضل من الصدقة) قال الرملي قال المرحوم الشيخ عبد الرحمن العمادي مفتي الشام في مناسكه : وإذا حج حجة الإسلام فصدقة التطوع
And from his saying 'obligatory once' it is understood that what is beyond it is voluntary, and the previous hadith testifies to it. According to the Shafi'is, Hajj is not described as supererogatory; rather, the first time is fard 'ayn and what is extra is fard kifayah, because among the communal obligations is that the House be visited every year. But I have not seen this from our imams; rather they explicitly stated it is supererogatory and said: supererogatory Hajj is better than charity. It is not hidden that... from al-Tabyin. And Nuh Efendi said: the apparent meaning is that by 'sin' he meant the sin of missing Hajj, not the sin of delaying, for it is not removed according to Abu Yusuf as previously indicated, and his saying 'if he dies without Hajj he sins by consensus' proves it, i.e., the sin of missing it because by delaying he exposed it to being lost. But there is consideration in this evidence... and in al-Qahistani: he sins according to the two shaykhs for delaying to another year without excuse, but if he performs it even at the end of his life, it removes the sin without dispute. Thus it contradicts what was quoted from Sadr al-Shari'ah about non-removal of sin according to the second. His saying: (it is said he sins absolutely) – al-Nahr said: I have not seen from Muhammad the statement of sin absolutely, for if so the dispute would be eliminated; so apparently this is a slip. Indeed, what is transmitted from him as in al-Fath is that he holds tarakhi, so he does not sin if he performs Hajj before his death; if he dies after ability without performing, it becomes apparent that he sinned. And he transmitted the other two opinions... And his saying: (they said supererogatory Hajj is better than charity) – al-Ramli said: the late Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Umadi, mufti of Sham, said in his Manasik: if one has performed the Hajj of Islam, then supererogatory charity...
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and a ruling statement. It begins by reiterating that additional Hajj is nafl based on the hadith. Then it contrasts the Shafi'i position: they consider additional Hajj as fard kifayah (communal obligation) to maintain the annual pilgrimage. The Hanafi response is that their imams explicitly say it is nafl, and that nafl Hajj is better than voluntary charity. The remainder of the passage returns to the earlier dispute about sin for delay, discussing various opinions on when sin is incurred and whether it can be removed. The final part restates the Hanafi position that nafl Hajj is superior to sadaqah.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory; performing it earns reward.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): Communal obligation; if some perform it, the rest are absolved.
صدقة تطوع (sadaqah tatawwu'): Voluntary charity given beyond obligatory zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is additional Hajj beyond the first classified?
A) Fard kifayah
B) Wajib
C) Nafl (supererogatory)
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Hajj is obligatory only once; additional pilgrimages are nafl and superior to voluntary charity.

The Sin of Delaying Hajj: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sin of delaying Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on whether delaying Hajj incurs sin and explain why the majority view (sin from first year, removable by performance) is preferred over others.

Core Idea
Delaying Hajj without excuse is sinful, but performance removes the sin; persistence is required to become a fasiq.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into an important intra-Hanafi debate: does delaying the obligatory Hajj after acquiring the means incur sin immediately, only at death, or not at all? The commentators reconcile conflicting transmissions from Imam Muhammad and establish the mufta bihi position. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh divergent riwayat within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal nature
The act under discussion is delaying the performance of Hajj after one becomes capable (istita'a). Hajj is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime. The question is whether delay itself constitutes a sin and when that sin arises.
Distinguish between sin of delay (ithm al-ta'khir) and sin of omission (ithm al-tark).
2
Summarize the three positions
The passage presents three views within the Hanafi school: (a) sin from the first year of ability (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), (b) sin only becomes apparent at death if not performed (Muhammad's transmitted view), (c) sin only if one fears missing Hajj due to signs of death (some mashayikh).
These correspond to different understandings of whether the obligation is immediate (fawr) or permissive (tarakhi).
3
Understand the majority preference
The commentator argues that the first view (sin from first year) is preferred because the very purpose of obligation is to prompt action with a penalty for delay; otherwise the obligation would be undermined. The sin is removed if Hajj is performed later, but the delay itself remains a violation.
This is supported by al-Fath and al-Qahistani.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of alternative interpretations
The passage rebuts the claim that sin is only for missing Hajj (tark) not delay, and also criticizes a claim that no absolute sin is reported from Muhammad. Evidence from al-Fath shows the opposite.
This step shows how later Hanafi authorities (mutakhkhirin) resolve apparent contradictions in the madhhab.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: a person who delays Hajj for many years but eventually performs it is sinful for the delay but the sin is removed; he does not become a fasiq unless persistence. If he dies without performing, he dies with sin. This affects how a mufti advises the delayed person.
Contrast with the Shafi'i view on additional Hajj is mentioned but is a side issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
محمد لا، وينبغي أن لا فاسقاً من أول سنة على المذهب الصحيح بل لا بد أن يتوالى يصير عليه سنون لأن التأخير في هذه الحالة صغيرة لأنه مكروه تحريماً ولا يصير فاسقاً بارتكابها مرة بل لا بد من الإصرار عليها، وإذا حج في آخر عمره ارتفع الإثم اتفاقاً قال الشارح : ولو مات ولم يحج أثم بالإجماع ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن المشايخ اختلفوا على قول محمد؛ فقيل يأثم مطلقاً، وقيل لا يأثم مطلقاً، وقيل: إن خاف الفوات بأن ظهرت له مخائل الموت في قلبه فأخره حتى مات أثم، وإن فجأه الموت لا يأثم وينبغي اعتماد القول الأول وتضعيف القول الثاني لأنه حينئذ يفوت القول بفرضية الحج لأن فائدتها الإثم عند عدم الفعل، سواء كان مضيقاً أو موسعاً اللهم إلا أن يقال : فائدتها على هذا القول وجوب الإيصاء عليه قبيل موته فإذا لم يوص يأثم لترك هذا الواجب لا لترك الحج. وعلم من قوله «فرض مرة» أن ما زاد عليها فهو تطوع ويشهد له الحديث السابق. وعند الشافعية أن الحج لا يوصف بالنفلية بل المرة الأولى فرض عين وما زاد ففرض كفاية لأن من فروض الكفاية أن يحج البيت كل عام ولم أرده لأئمتنا بل صرحوا بالنفلية فقالوا: حج النفل أفضل الصدقة، ولا يخفى أنه إذا
من
كذا في التبيين. وقال نوح أفندي الظاهر أن مراده بالإثم إثم تفويت الحج لا إثم تأخيره فإنه لا يرتفع عند أبي يوسف كما مر ويدل عليه قوله : ولو مات ولم يحج أثم بالإجماع أي أثم تفويته لأنه بتأخيره عرضه على الفوات ا هـ. وفيما استدل به نظر يدل عليه بحث المؤلف في كلام الزيلعي ونقل الأقوال الثلاثة وما ذاك إلا في التأخير إذ لا شك في إثم تارك فرض قطعي وإلا لم يكن فرضاً ولا واجباً، فالمراد في الموضعين إثم التأخير يدل عليه ما قال في الفتح : ثم على ما أورده المصنف يأثم بالتأخير عن أول سني الإمكان فلو حج بعده ارتفع الإثم ا هـ. وفي القهستاني: فيأثم عند الشيخين بالتأخير إلى غيره بلا عذر إلا إذا أدى ولو في آخر عمره فإنه رافع للإثم بلا خلاف، وحينئذ فهو مخالف لما نقله عن صدر الشريعة من عدم ارتفاع الإثم عند الثاني قوله : (فقيل يأثم مطلقاً) قال في النهر : لم أر عن محمد القول بالإثم مطلقاً إذ بتقديره يرتفع الخلاف، فالظاهر أن هذا سهو، نعم المنقول عنه كما في الفتح أنه على التراخي فلا يأثم إذا حج قبل موته ، فإذا مات بعد الإمكان ولم يحج ظهر أنه أثم. ونقل القولين الآخرين ثم قال : وصحة الأول غنية عن الوجه، وعلى اعتباره قيل يظهر الإثم من السنة الأولى، وقيل من الأخيرة من سنة رأى في نفسه الضعف وقيل يأثم في الجملة غير محكوم بمعين بل علمه إلى الله تعالى ا هـ . ولا يخفى عليك ما فيه فإن ما ادعى عدم رؤيته نقله بيده وتلفظه بفيه وهو قول الفتح : فإذا مات بعد الإمكان ولم يحج ظهر أنه أثم وهو معنى قول المؤلف يأثم مطلقاً» أي سواء فجأة الموت أو لا. وقوله إذ بتقديره يرتفع الخلاف» ممنوع فإنه على قول الإمامين يأثم بالتأخير عن أول سني الإمكان كما مر وعلى قول محمد يظهر بالموت إثمه وكلام لمؤلف فيما إذا مات فالفرق واضح تدبر
Book of Hajj. Muhammad said no, and it is appropriate that he does not become a transgressor from the first year according to the correct madhhab, rather he continues performance over years because delay in this case is a minor sin as it is makruh tahrimi, and he does not become a transgressor by committing it once, rather persistence is needed. If he performs Hajj in the last part of his life, the sin is removed by agreement. The commentator said: if he dies without performing Hajj, he sins by consensus, and it is not hidden what is in it; the mashayikh differed on the statement of Muhammad: some said he sins absolutely, some said he does not sin absolutely, and some said: if he feared missing out because signs of death appeared in his heart and he delayed until death, then he sins; if death overtook him suddenly, he does not sin. The first opinion should be adopted and the second weakened because at that point the statement that Hajj is obligatory would be lost, for its benefit is sin when action is not performed, whether it is immediate or extended. Unless it is said: its benefit on this view is that he is obligated to make a will (wasiyya) shortly before his death; if he does not make a will, he sins for leaving this wajib, not for leaving Hajj. It is understood from his statement «it is obligatory once» that what exceeds it is supererogatory, and the previous hadith bears witness to this. According to the Shafi'is, Hajj is not described as supererogatory; rather the first time is fard 'ayn and what exceeds is fard kifaya because it is among communal obligations that the House be visited every year. But I have not seen this from our imams; rather they explicitly stated supererogation and said: supererogatory Hajj is better than charity. And it is not hidden that when... so in al-Tabyin. Nuh Afandi said: the apparent meaning is that by sin he means the sin of missing Hajj, not the sin of delaying it, for it is not removed according to Abu Yusuf as mentioned. This is indicated by his statement: if he died without performing Hajj, he sins by consensus, i.e., the sin of missing it, because by delaying he exposed it to being lost. But there is consideration in what he inferred, as indicated by the author's discussion in the words of al-Zayla'i, and he narrated three opinions, and this is only concerning delay, since there is no doubt about the sin of one who abandons a definitive obligation; otherwise it would not be fard or wajib. So the intent in both places is the sin of delay, as indicated by what al-Fath said: then according to what the author mentioned, he sins by delaying from the first year of feasibility; if he performs Hajj afterward, the sin is removed. In al-Qahistani: according to the two shaykhs, he sins by delaying to another year without excuse, unless he performs it even at the end of his life, then it lifts the sin without dispute. And this contradicts what he narrated from Sadr al-Shari'ah about the sin not being removed according to the second. His statement: (it was said he sins absolutely) – al-Nahr said: I have not seen from Muhammad the opinion of absolute sin, because if so, the dispute would be lifted. The apparent is that this is a slip. Rather, what is transmitted from him, as in al-Fath, is that it is permissive (tarakhi), so he does not sin if he performs Hajj before his death. If he dies after feasibility without performing Hajj, then it becomes clear that he sinned. He narrated the other two opinions and then said: the validity of the first is self-evident, and based on it, it is said the sin appears from the first year, or from the last year when he sees weakness in himself, or he sins in general without specifying, but his knowledge is with Allah. It is not hidden from you what is in it, for what he claimed not to have seen, he himself narrated and uttered with his mouth, i.e., the statement of al-Fath: if he dies after feasibility without performing Hajj, then it becomes clear that he sinned, which is the meaning of the author's statement 'he sins absolutely', i.e., whether death is sudden or not. And his statement 'since if so the dispute would be lifted' is denied, because according to the two imams he sins by delaying from the first year of feasibility, and according to Muhammad his sin appears at death, and the author's speech is about when he dies; the difference is clear. Reflect.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sin of delaying the obligatory Hajj after one becomes capable. The commentator begins by clarifying that delaying Hajj without a valid excuse is considered a minor sin (makruh tahrimi) and does not make one a fasiq unless one persists in delaying. If one performs Hajj later in life, the sin is removed by agreement. However, there is ikhtilaf on the statement of Imam Muhammad: some say the sin occurs only if one fears death and still delays, others say it occurs absolutely, and others say it does not occur if death is sudden. The preferred view is the first, because the very purpose of obligation is to prompt action under penalty of sin; otherwise the obligation loses its force. The passage then transitions to the ruling that Hajj is fard once in a lifetime, and additional Hajj is nafl, contrary to the Shafi'i view that it becomes fard kifaya. This part is a prelude to the main discussion on delay. The commentator then rebuts Nuh Afandi's interpretation that the sin is only for missing Hajj, arguing that the sin is for delay as per the majority view. The text concludes with a critique of a claim that no absolute sin is reported from Muhammad, showing that al-Fath and others confirm it.

Key Terms
إثم التأخير (ithm al-ta'khir): The sin incurred by delaying an obligatory act (Hajj) beyond the first moment of feasibility without a valid excuse.
فرض مرة (fard marrah): The obligation of Hajj is once in a lifetime for those capable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, which statement best describes the ruling on delaying Hajj after becoming capable?
A) Delaying Hajj is not sinful because the obligation is permissive (tarakhi).
B) Delaying Hajj is sinful from the first year of ability, but the sin is removed if Hajj is performed later.
C) Delaying Hajj makes one a fasiq immediately.
D) Delaying Hajj is only sinful if one dies without performing it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that delaying Hajj without excuse is sinful, but the sin is removed by eventual performance; persistence in delay can lead to fasiq.

Virtue of Nafil Hajj vs Voluntary Charity: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the relative virtue of nafil Hajj and voluntary charity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on nafil Hajj vs charity and apply contextual qualifiers to determine the preferred view.

Core Idea
The better act is not fixed; charity outranks nafil Hajj when need is dire, but Hajj's hardship multiplies reward.

After fulfilling the obligatory Hajj, a Muslim may wonder whether to perform an additional supererogatory Hajj or to give voluntary charity. Hanafi scholars differ on which is more virtuous. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq records the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad, and later scholars refine the ruling based on circumstances. Understanding this dispute teaches us that virtue in acts of worship is context-dependent.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify what each of the three founding imams held: Imam Muhammad preferred charity, Abu Yusuf preferred nafil Hajj, and Abu Hanifa initially agreed with Muhammad but later changed to Abu Yusuf's view.
2
Understand the basis
What evidence or reasoning supports each view? Muhammad: charity benefits others directly and avoids sins common in Hajj. Abu Yusuf: hardship in Hajj multiplies reward. Later scholars also note the hadith of spending in Hajj multiplied 700 times.
The hadith is understood to refer to obligatory Hajj, not nafil.
3
Apply the later tarjih
How did later Hanafi scholars (al-Lubab, al-Qari) resolve the dispute? They qualified charity's superiority to cases of extreme need or famine.
Otherwise, nafil Hajj may be superior due to its own spending and hardships.
4
Derive the practical rule
In contemporary times, charity may be better if society suffers from widespread poverty and pilgrims often commit sins during Hajj.
The commentator (al-Ramli) emphasizes this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فقالوا حج النفل أفضل من الصدقة) قال الرملي قال المرحوم الشيخ عبد الرحمن العمادي مفتي الشام في مناسكه : وإذا حج حجة الإسلام فصدقة التطوع بعد ذلك أفضل من حج التطوع عند محمد، والحج أفضل عند أبي يوسف وكان أبو حنيفة رحمه الله يقول بقول محمد فلما ورأى ما فيه من أنواع المشقات الموجبة لتضاعف الحسنات . حج رجع ألى قول أبي يوسف ا هـ. قلت قد يقال إن صدقة التطوع في زماننا أفضل لما يلزم الحاج غالباً من ارتكاب المحظورات ومشاهدته لفواحح المنكرات وشح عامة الناس بالصدقات وتركهم الفقراء والأيتام في حسرات ولا سيما في أيام الغلاء وضيق الأوقات وبتعدي النفع تتضاعف الحسنات، ثم رأيت في متفرقات اللباب الجزم بأن الصدقة أفضل منه وقال شارحه القاري أي على ما هو المختار كما في التجنيس ومنية المفتى وغيرهما ولعل تلك الصدقة محمولة على إعطاء الفقير الموصوف بغاية الفاقة أو في حال المجاعة وإلا فالحج مشتمل على النفقة بل ورد أن الدرهم الذي ينفق في الحج بسبعمائة الخ . قلت : قد يقال ما ورد محمول على الحج الفرض على أنه لا مانع من كون الصدقة للمحتاج أعظم أجراً من سبعمائة
His statement: (They said supererogatory Hajj is better than charity) – al-Ramli said: the late Sheikh Abdul Rahman al-Imadi, Mufti of Sham, said in his Manasik: When one has performed the obligatory Hajj, then voluntary charity after that is better than supererogatory Hajj according to Muhammad. Hajj is better according to Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) used to agree with Muhammad, but when he saw in it the kinds of hardships that necessitate multiplication of good deeds, he performed Hajj and returned to the opinion of Abu Yusuf. I say: It may be said that voluntary charity in our time is better due to what most pilgrims inevitably commit of prohibited acts and witnessing abominable evils, and the stinginess of the general public in charity, leaving the poor and orphans in sorrow, especially in times of high prices and financial hardship, and good deeds are multiplied due to the widespread benefit. Then I saw in the selections of al-Lubab the categorical statement that charity is better than it, and its commentator al-Qari said it is the preferred view as in al-Tajnis, Munyat al-Mufti, and others. Perhaps that charity is understood to refer to giving to the extremely needy or during famine; otherwise, Hajj includes spending, and it has been narrated that the dirham spent in Hajj is multiplied by seven hundred. I say: It may be said that what is narrated is understood to refer to obligatory Hajj, and there is no obstacle to charity for the needy having a greater reward than seven hundred.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute over the relative virtue of supererogatory Hajj (nafl) versus voluntary charity (sadaqah tatawwu') after one has already performed the obligatory Hajj. Three positions are presented: According to Imam Muhammad, voluntary charity is better than nafil Hajj. Abu Yusuf holds that nafil Hajj is better. Abu Hanifa initially agreed with Muhammad but later, after performing Hajj and observing the hardships and spiritual benefits, changed his view to agree with Abu Yusuf. The commentator then offers his own analysis, stating that in contemporary times, charity may be better due to the prevalence of sins during Hajj and the dire needs of the poor. He cites al-Lubab and its commentator al-Qari who affirm the preference of charity in certain contexts. However, this is qualified: the charity must be for the extremely needy or during famine. Otherwise, the reward of spending in Hajj is immense, as a hadith mentions that a dirham spent in Hajj is multiplied seven hundred times. The passage ends by suggesting that such hadith refer to obligatory Hajj, not nafil, so charity might still be superior for nafil.

Key Terms
حج النفل (hajj al-nafl): Supererogatory Hajj performed after the obligatory Hajj.
صدقة التطوع (sadaqat al-tatawwu'): Voluntary charity beyond obligatory zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is voluntary charity considered better than nafil Hajj?
A) Always, because charity benefits others directly.
B) When the charity is given to an extremely needy person or during a famine.
C) When the pilgrim cannot afford the journey.
D) Never, because nafil Hajj is always superior.

Key Takeaway
The relative virtue of nafil Hajj and charity depends on circumstances; charity outranks when need is acute, otherwise Hajj's rewards are immense.

Conditions for Obligation of Hajj
Parsing conditions for Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions for Hajj obligation and identify the three categories of persons exempted.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard 'ayn only for the free, adult, sane, healthy, and financially capable; slaves, children, and insane are never obligated.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq precisely defines the shurut that make Hajj obligatory. Understanding these limits prevents misapplication of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
List the six conditions
From the text: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability (provisions + riding animal), and surplus beyond essential needs.
2
Identify exempted persons
Slaves (even if authorized), children, and insane are not obligated; the text explains why for slaves (lack of ownership and conflict with master's rights).
3
Understand the ability condition
Ability includes financial means (zad, rahila) beyond necessities for self and dependents, and physical safety. Borrowed ability does not create obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يخفى الخ) قال منلا علي في شرح المنسك المتوسط : نعم يفرض لعارض كنذر أو قضاء بعد فساد أو إحصار أو الشروع فيه بمباشرة إحرام الخ.
٥٤٤
كتاب الحج
الفور بشرط حرية وبلوغ وعقل وصحة وقدرة زاد وراحلة فضل عن مسكنه وعما لا
نذر الحج فإنه يصير فرضاً أيضاً. ومن فروعه ما في الخلاصة : رجل قال الله علي مائة حجة لزمته كلها، ولو قال أنا أحج لا حج عليه، ولو قال إذا دخلت الدار فأنا أحج يلزمه عند الشرط، ولو قال المريض إن عافاني الله تعالى من مرضي هذا فعلي حجة فبرئ لزمته حجة وإن لم يقل علي حجة الله لأنه الحجة لا تكون إلا لله، ولو برأ وحج جاز عن حجة الإسلام، ولو نوى غير حجة الإسلام صحت نيته ا هـ . وظاهره أنه ينصرف إلى حجة الإسلام من غير نيته، وينبغي أن ينصرف إلى غير حجة الإسلام بغير نية، إلا أن ينويها، وقد صرح به الشارح الزيلعي في كتاب الأضحية لكن علل المحقق ابن الهمام لما في الخلاصة بأن الغالب أن يريد به المريض الذي فرط في الفرض حتى مرض ، وقد قدمنا أن الحج يتصف بالحرمة إذا كان المال حراماً ويمكن أن يقال : إنه يكون واجباً وهو ما إذا جاوز الميقات بغير إحرام فإنهم قالوا : يجب عليه أحد النسكين إما الحج أو العمرة، فإذا اختار الحج فإنه يتصف بالوجوب وقد قدمنا أنه يتصف بالكراهة وهو حجة بغير إذن أبويه بشرطه أو بغير إذن صاحب الدين، فتحرر من هذا أنه يكون فرضاً وواجباً ونفلاً وحراماً ومكروهاً، والظاهر أنه لا يتصف بالإباحة لأنه عبادة وضعاً ..
قوله : (بشرط حرية وبلوغ وعقل وصحة وقدرة زاد وراحلة فضل عن مسكنه وعما لا بد منه ونفقة ذهابه وإيابه وعياله فلا حج على عبد ولو مدبراً أو أم ولد أو مكاتباً أو مبعضاً أو مأذوناً في الحج ولو كان بمكة لعدم ملكه بخلاف الصوم والصلاة لأن الحج لا يتأتى إلا بالمال غالباً بخلافهما، ولفوات حق المولى في مدة طويلة وحق العبد مقدم بإذن الشرع والمولى، وإن أذنه فقد أعاره منافعه والحج لا يجب بقدرة عارية ولا على صبي ولا مجنون
قد
His statement: (And it is not hidden, etc.) – Mulla Ali said in the commentary of al-Mansak al-Mutawassit: Yes, it becomes obligatory due to an incidental cause like a vow, or making up after corruption, or being restricted, or starting by entering ihram. Page 544 Book of Hajj. Immediacy (fawr) with the condition of freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability regarding provisions and riding animal, surplus to his residence and what is indispensable, and the expenses of going and returning and his dependents. So there is no Hajj upon a slave, even if he is mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, partial slave, or authorized to perform Hajj, even if he is in Makkah, because he does not own property; unlike fasting and prayer, because Hajj cannot be performed without wealth generally, contrary to them, and due to the loss of the master's right over a long period, and the slave's right is given priority by the permission of the Law and the master. If the master gives permission, he has lent his services, and Hajj is not obligatory by borrowed ability. It is not obligatory on a child or an insane person. The vow (nathr) of Hajj makes it also obligatory. Among its branches is in al-Khulasa: A man said: 'By Allah, I owe one hundred Hajjs' – all become obligatory. If he said 'I will perform Hajj' – nothing is required. If he said 'If I enter the house, I will perform Hajj' – it becomes binding upon the condition. If a sick person said 'If Allah cures me from this illness, I owe a Hajj' – then he recovers, a Hajj is binding upon him, even if he did not say 'I owe a Hajj for Allah' because Hajj is only for Allah. If he recovers and performs Hajj, it suffices for the obligatory Islam Hajj. If he intended other than the Islamic Hajj, his intention is valid. Its apparent meaning is that it applies to the Islamic Hajj without his intent, and it should apply to other than the Islamic Hajj without intent, unless he intends it. This has been stated by the commentator al-Zayla'i in the book of Udhiyah, but the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam explained what is in al-Khulasa by saying that usually the sick person intends the obligatory Hajj which he had delayed until illness. We have already said that Hajj is described as prohibited if the wealth is unlawful. It can be said that it becomes wajib, which is the case when one passes the miqat without ihram; they said he must perform one of the two rights: either Hajj or 'umrah. If he chooses Hajj, it becomes wajib. We have already said that it can be described as makruh: it is Hajj without the permission of one's parents, subject to condition, or without the permission of the creditor. From this, it is established that it can be fard, wajib, nafl, haram, and makruh. It is apparent that it is not described as mubah because it is an act of worship by definition. His statement: (with the condition of freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability regarding provisions and riding animal, surplus to his residence and what is indispensable, expenses of going and returning and his dependents. So no Hajj upon a slave, even if mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, partial slave, or authorized to perform Hajj, even if in Makkah, because he does not own property; unlike fasting and prayer because Hajj cannot be performed without wealth generally, contrary to them, and due to the loss of the master's right for a long period. The slave's right is prioritized by permission of the Law and the master. If he gives permission, he has lent his services, and Hajj is not obligatory by borrowed ability. Nor is it obligatory upon a child or an insane person.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq serves as a parsing exercise for the conditions (shurut) that make Hajj obligatory. It begins by noting that Hajj can become obligatory due to incidental causes such as a vow (nathr), making up a corrupted Hajj, being prevented (ihsar), or starting the journey by entering ihram. Then it lists the standard conditions: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, and the ability to secure provisions (zad) and a riding animal (rahila) that are surplus to essential needs like housing and family expenses. The text explains that slaves are not obligated even if they are authorized, because Hajj requires wealth and a long time, and the master's rights are prioritized. Similarly, children and insane persons are not obligated. The passage also includes a detailed examination of vows (nathr) related to Hajj, citing al-Khulasa: if one vows a specific number of Hajjs, they all become binding; conditional vows like 'if I enter the house I will perform Hajj' become binding upon fulfillment of the condition; and a sick person who vows to perform Hajj if cured must perform it, and it counts as the obligatory Hajj unless he intends otherwise. The text then notes that Hajj can take various rulings (fard, wajib, nafl, haram, makruh) depending on circumstances, but never mubah as it is an act of worship.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istita'ah): Ability to perform Hajj, consisting of health, safe passage, and financial means (zad and rahila) surplus to essential needs.
نذر الحج (nathr al-hajj): A vow to perform Hajj, which makes Hajj obligatory upon fulfillment of condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for Hajj obligation according to the passage?
A) Freedom
B) Puberty
C) Being employed
D) Health

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard 'ayn only upon those who are free, adult, sane, healthy, and have surplus means beyond essential needs.

Rulings of Vows (Nathr) for Hajj
Explaining nathr rulings for Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a nathr makes Hajj obligatory and distinguish between unconditional, conditional, and specific nathr expressions.

Core Idea
A vow (nathr) to perform Hajj makes it fard, even if one has already performed Hajj al-Islam, unless the vow explicitly excludes it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the legal effect of a nathr (vow) concerning Hajj. It clarifies how different wordings create binding obligations and whether a nathr Hajj counts toward the obligatory Hajj al-Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nathr expressions
The text lists examples: 'By Allah, I owe 100 Hajjs' (unconditional), 'If I enter the house, I will perform Hajj' (conditional), 'If Allah cures me, I owe a Hajj' (sick person).
2
Determine obligation
Unconditional and conditional nathr make Hajj obligatory upon utterance or condition. The phrase 'I will perform Hajj' alone does not obligate.
3
Understand the default intention
If a sick person vows a Hajj and recovers, the performed Hajj counts as Hajj al-Islam unless he intends otherwise (e.g., nafl). The apparent ruling is that it defaults to Hajj al-Islam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Zayla'i holds it defaults to non-fard; Ibn al-Humam argues it usually refers to the obligatory Hajj the person delayed.

Source Text

Conditions for the Obligation of Hajj
States the conditions for Hajj obligation and the effect of vows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for the obligation of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and apply them to determine who is obligated.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory immediately upon fulfilling six conditions: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability with provisions and mount.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins the chapter on Hajj by specifying the conditions that trigger its obligation. Understanding these conditions is essential to determine who must perform Hajj and when. The text also explains the effect of vows (nadhr) making Hajj obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
List all six conditions mentioned in the text: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability (provisions and mount) surplus to residence and necessities.
The text uses 'bishart hurriya wa bulugh wa aql wa sihha wa qudra zad wa rahila fadl 'an maskanihi wa 'amma la budda minhu'.
2
Understand the condition of freedom
Explain why a slave (including mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, muba'dh) is not obligated, even with permission. The reason: lack of ownership of self and long absence from master's rights.
Note: fasting and prayer are different because they do not require wealth.
3
Understand puberty and sanity
A child or insane person is not obligated; their Hajj is valid but counts as nafl, not the obligatory one.
Hanafi rule: acts of worship require legal capacity (ahliyyah).
4
Understand health and ability (zad wa rahila)
One must be healthy enough to travel and have sufficient provisions and transport, beyond basic needs for family and dependents.
This is the Hanafi definition of istita'ah.
5
Understand the effect of vows (nadhr)
A vow to perform Hajj makes Hajj obligatory even if one would not otherwise be obligated. The passage gives examples from al-Khulasa: a vow of multiple Hajjs binds all; conditional vows become binding upon fulfillment.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi position on vows.

كتاب الحج الفور بشرط حرية وبلوغ وعقل وصحة وقدرة زاد وراحلة فضلت عن مسكنه وعما لا نذر الحج فإنه يصير فرضاً أيضاً. ومن فروعه ما في الخلاصة : رجل قال الله علي مائة حجة لزمته كلها، ولو قال أنا أحج لا حج عليه، ولو قال إذا دخلت الدار فأنا أحج يلزمه عند الشرط، ولو قال المريض إن عافاني الله تعالى من مرضي هذا فعلي حجة فبرئ لزمته حجة وإن لم يقل علي حجة الله لأنه الحجة لا تكون إلا لله، ولو برأ وحج جاز عن حجة الإسلام، ولو نوى غير حجة الإسلام صحت نيته ا هـ . وظاهره أنه ينصرف إلى حجة الإسلام من غير نيته، وينبغي أن ينصرف إلى غير حجة الإسلام بغير نية، إلا أن ينويها، وقد صرح به الشارح الزيلعي في كتاب الأضحية لكن علل المحقق ابن الهمام لما في الخلاصة بأن الغالب أن يريد به المريض الذي فرط في الفرض حتى مرض ، وقد قدمنا أن الحج يتصف بالحرمة إذا كان المال حراماً ويمكن أن يقال : إنه يكون واجباً وهو ما إذا جاوز الميقات بغير إحرام فإنهم قالوا : يجب عليه أحد النسكين إما الحج أو العمرة، فإذا اختار الحج فإنه يتصف بالوجوب وقد قدمنا أنه يتصف بالكراهة وهو حجة بغير إذن أبويه بشرطه أو بغير إذن صاحب الدين، فتحرر من هذا أنه يكون فرضاً وواجباً ونفلاً وحراماً ومكروهاً، والظاهر أنه لا يتصف بالإباحة لأنه عبادة وضعاً ..
قوله : (بشرط حرية وبلوغ وعقل وصحة وقدرة زاد وراحلة فضل عن مسكنه وعما لا بد منه ونفقة ذهابه وإيابه وعياله فلا حج على عبد ولو مدبراً أو أم ولد أو مكاتباً أو مبعضاً أو مأذوناً في الحج ولو كان بمكة لعدم ملكه بخلاف الصوم والصلاة لأن الحج لا يتأتى إلا بالمال غالباً بخلافهما، ولفوات حق المولى في مدة طويلة وحق العبد مقدم بإذن الشرع والمولى، وإن أذنه فقد أعاره منافعه والحج لا يجب بقدرة عارية ولا على صبي ولا مجنون
بعد ذلك أفضل من حج التطوع عند محمد، والحج أفضل عند أبي يوسف وكان أبو حنيفة رحمه الله يقول بقول محمد فلما ورأى ما فيه من أنواع المشقات الموجبة لتضاعف الحسنات . حج رجع ألى قول أبي يوسف ا هـ. قلت قد يقال إن صدقة التطوع في زماننا أفضل لما يلزم الحاج غالباً من ارتكاب المحظورات ومشاهدته لفواحش المنكرات وشح عامة الناس بالصدقات وتركهم الفقراء والأيتام في حسرات ولا سيما في أيام الغلاء وضيق الأوقات وبتعدي النفع تتضاعف الحسنات، ثم رأيت في متفرقات اللباب الجزم بأن الصدقة أفضل منه وقال شارحه القاري أي على ما هو المختار كما في التجنيس ومنية المفتى وغيرهما ولعل تلك الصدقة محمولة على إعطاء الفقير الموصوف بغاية الفاقة أو في حال المجاعة وإلا فالحج مشتمل على النفقة بل ورد أن الدرهم الذي ينفق في الحج بسبعمائة الخ . قلت : قد يقال ما ورد محمول على الحج الفرض على أنه لا مانع من كون الصدقة للمحتاج أعظم أجراً من سبعمائة قوله: (ولا يخفى الخ) قال منلا علي في شرح المنسك المتوسط : نعم يفرض لعارض كنذر أو قضاء بعد فساد أو إحصار أو الشروع فيه بمباشرة إحرام الخ.
The book of Hajj. Immediate obligation, with the condition of freedom, puberty, sanity, health, and ability (provisions and mount) surplus to his residence and what is indispensable. A vow of Hajj makes it obligatory as well. Among its branches: in al-Khulasa: a man said 'Upon me (is the obligation of) one hundred Hajjs'—all are binding; if he said 'I will perform Hajj' nothing is binding; if he said 'when I enter the house I will perform Hajj' it is binding upon the condition; if a sick person said 'if Allah cures me from this illness, then upon me is a Hajj' and he recovers, a Hajj is binding even if he did not say 'upon me is a Hajj of Allah' because Hajj is only for Allah; if he recovered and performed Hajj, it suffices for Hajj al-Islam; if he intended other than Hajj al-Islam his intention is valid. Its apparent meaning is that it is directed to Hajj al-Islam without his intention, and it should be directed to other than Hajj al-Islam without intention unless he intends it; and al-Zayla'i explicitly stated in the book of Udhiyya, but Ibn al-Humam investigated regarding al-Khulasa that the sick person who neglected the obligation until he became ill is the common case. We have mentioned that Hajj is described as forbidden (haram) if the wealth is unlawful; and it can be said that it is obligatory (wajib) when one passes the miqat without ihram, for they said: one of the two rites is obligatory, either Hajj or Umra; if he chooses Hajj it becomes wajib; we have mentioned that it is described as makruh—it is a Hajj without the permission of his parents under its condition or without the permission of the creditor. So it is deduced from this that it can be fard, wajib, nafl, haram, and makruh; apparently it is not described as mubah because it is an act of worship by nature.
His statement: (with the condition of freedom, puberty, sanity, health, ability, provisions, and mount surplus to his residence and what is indispensable, and expenses of going and returning and his dependents; so no Hajj is obligatory upon a slave, even if mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, muba'd, or a ma'dhun for Hajj even if in Makkah, because he does not own [himself], unlike fasting and prayer because Hajj is not accomplished except with wealth generally, unlike them; and due to the loss of the master's right over a long period, and the slave's right is given precedence by permission of the Law and the master; if he permits him, he has lent him his benefits, and Hajj is not obligatory with borrowed ability; nor upon a child nor an insane person.
After that, voluntary charity is better than voluntary Hajj according to Muhammad, and Hajj is better according to Abu Yusuf; Abu Hanifa used to say the saying of Muhammad, but when he saw what it contains of types of hardships that multiply good deeds, he performed Hajj and returned to the saying of Abu Yusuf. I say: it may be said that voluntary charity in our time is better due to what the pilgrim often incurs of committing prohibited things and witnessing abominable evils, and the general stinginess of people with charity, leaving the poor and orphans in regrets, especially in days of high prices and tight times; and by the generality of benefit, good deeds multiply. Then I saw in the Mufarraqat al-Lubab the firm opinion that charity is better than it, and its commentator al-Qari said: i.e., according to the chosen position as in al-Tajnis, Munyat al-Mufti, and others; perhaps that charity is understood as giving to the poor described as extreme need or in a famine; otherwise, Hajj involves spending; indeed it is reported that the dirham spent in Hajj is by seven hundred... I say: it may be said what is reported is understood as obligatory Hajj, and there is no preventing that charity to the needy is greater in reward than seven hundred. His statement: (and it is not hidden...) said Mulla Ali in Sharh al-Mansik al-Mutawassit: yes, it becomes obligatory due to an incident like a vow, or making up after corruption, or confinement (ihsar), or beginning it by directly entering ihram, etc.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the conditions for the obligation of Hajj. The matn states that Hajj is obligatory immediately upon meeting conditions: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, and ability (zad and rahila). The commentary first discusses rulings related to vows (nadhr), explaining that a vow makes Hajj obligatory (fard) as well. It gives examples from al-Khulasa: if one vows a hundred Hajjs, all are binding; if one says 'I will perform Hajj' without a vow, nothing is binding; a conditional vow becomes binding upon fulfillment of the condition. For a sick person who vows a Hajj upon recovery, it becomes binding and suffices for Hajj al-Islam unless he intends otherwise. The commentary then discusses the legal descriptions of Hajj: it can be fard, wajib, nafl, haram (if with unlawful wealth), makruh (if without parents' permission), but not mubah. Then it lists the conditions in detail: freedom (so no obligation on slaves, even if mudabbar, umm walad, etc.), puberty (so no obligation on child), sanity (so no obligation on insane), and health and ability. The passage also includes a discussion on the superiority of voluntary charity over voluntary Hajj, recording the difference between Muhammad (charity better) and Abu Yusuf (Hajj better), with Abu Hanifa initially agreeing with Muhammad then later with Abu Yusuf. The commentator adds that in current times charity may be better due to common violations during Hajj.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate obligation; Hajj must be performed as soon as conditions are met, not delayed.
زاد وراحلة (zad wa rahila): Provisions (food) and mount (transport) sufficient for the journey to and from Makkah.
نذر الحج (nadhr al-hajj): A vow to perform Hajj; it makes Hajj obligatory even if one is not otherwise obligated.
الحرية (al-hurriyya): Freedom; a slave is not obligated for Hajj.
البلوغ (al-bulugh): Puberty; a child is not obligated.
العقل (al-aql): Sanity; an insane person is not obligated.
الصحة (al-sihha): Health; one must be physically able to undertake the journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Hajj?
A) Freedom from slavery
B) Being a male
C) Possessing provisions and mount
D) Being of sound mind

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory immediately upon meeting six conditions: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, and ability (provisions and mount) beyond basic needs; a vow also triggers obligation.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Legal Descriptions of Hajj and the Voluntary Charity Dispute
Discusses legal descriptions of Hajj and intra-Hanafi dispute on charity vs voluntary Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five legal rulings that can describe Hajj and state the mufta bihi position on voluntary charity versus voluntary Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj can be fard, wajib, nafl, haram, or makruh depending on circumstances; voluntary charity is better than voluntary Hajj according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq not only states the conditions for obligation but also explores the various legal descriptions Hajj can assume based on the performer's situation. Additionally, it records an important intra-Hanafi dispute: is voluntary charity better than voluntary Hajj, or vice versa? Understanding this helps prioritize acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five possible rulings for Hajj
List the five rulings mentioned: fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary but not from definitive evidence), nafl (voluntary), haram (forbidden), and makruh (disliked). The text excludes mubah.
Hajj becomes haram if funded by unlawful wealth; makruh if without parents' permission or creditor's permission.
2
Understand when each ruling applies
Explain the conditions that trigger each ruling. For example, fard when obligation conditions are met; wajib when one passes the miqat without ihram and chooses Hajj; nafl when done voluntarily; haram when with unlawful money; makruh when without required permissions.
The text also mentions that Hajj can be wajib due to a vow or after corruption.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on voluntary charity vs voluntary Hajj
Identify the two positions: Muhammad al-Shaybani said voluntary charity is better; Abu Yusuf said voluntary Hajj is better. Abu Hanifa initially agreed with Muhammad, but later changed to Abu Yusuf's view after performing Hajj and witnessing its hardships and multiplied rewards.
The commentator then adds that in his time (due to common violations during Hajj), charity may be better, but this is not the mufta bihi.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is from later texts (al-Lubab, al-Tajnis, Munyat al-Mufti) that voluntary charity is better, especially for the needy or in famine. However, the commentary notes that Hajj involves spending, and a dirham spent in Hajj is rewarded seven hundredfold for obligatory Hajj.
The dispute is legitimate ikhtilaf; both views have merit.

Key Terms
الحج التطوع (al-hajj al-tatawwu'): Voluntary Hajj performed in addition to the obligatory one.

According to the text, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position on voluntary charity versus voluntary Hajj?

The Obligation of Ihjaj: The Hanafi Dispute on Sending a Substitute for Hajj
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ihjaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a physically unable person must hire a substitute for Hajj, and explain the practical consequence of this dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa lifts the obligation entirely; the Sahibayn require hiring a substitute if you have the means.

Hajj is obligatory for those who are able, but what about chronic illness, imprisonment, or disability? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether such individuals must send someone else. This passage clarifies the positions and the underlying proofs, distinguishing between personal ability and financial ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of health and its role
The passage begins by stating that health is a condition for obligation. Note the initial definition as 'soundness of limbs' and later refinement.
The condition of health is one of the shurut al-wujub for Hajj.
2
List the categories of excused individuals
Read the list: quadriplegic, chronically ill, paralyzed, amputee, sick, old man, blind, prisoner, one fearing a tyrannical ruler. Understand that these are all excused from personal performance.
The list includes both permanent and temporary impediments.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position on ihjaj
According to the apparent madhhab of Abu Hanifa, these individuals are not obligated to perform Hajj themselves nor to hire a substitute (ihjaj), even if they have wealth.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
4
State the Sahibayn's position on ihjaj
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the person has the means, they must hire someone to perform Hajj on their behalf. This is also a transmission from them.
The Sahibayn analogize to proxy Hajj for the deceased.
5
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a wealthy paralyzed person who does not hire a substitute commits no sin; under the Sahibayn, they are sinful and must fulfill the obligation by sending someone.
Later fatwa often prefers the Sahibayn's view for precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فلا حج على عبد الخ) أي لا يجب عليه لكنه يصح منه ويقع نفلاً قوله: (ولا على صبي الخ) أي لا يجب
قد
بد له منه ونفقة ذهابه وإيابه وعياله وأمن طريق ومحرم أو زوج لا مرأة في سفر فلو
وفي المعتوه خلاف في الأصول فذهب المصنف تبعاً لفخر الإسلام إلى أنه يوضع عنه الخطاب كالصبي فلا يجب عليه شيء من العبادات، وذهب الدبوسي في التقويم إلى أنه مخاطب بالعبادات احتياطاً. والمراد بالصحة صحة الجوارح فلا يجب أداء الحج على مقعد ولا على زمن ولا مفلوج ولا مقطوع الرجلين ولا على المريض، والشيخ الذي لا يثبت بنفسه على الراحة والأعمى والمحبوس والخائف من السلطان الذي يمنع الناس من الخروج إلى الحج ولا يجب عليهم الحج بأنفسهم ولا الإحجاج عنهم إن قدروا على ذلك هذا ظاهر المذهب عن أبي حنيفة وهو رواية عنهما، وظاهر الرواية عنهما أنه يجب عليهم الإحجاج فإن أحجوا أجزأهم
عليه أيضاً فلو حج وهو مميز بنفسه أو غير مميز بإحرام وليه فهو نفل، وأما غير العاقل فاختلف فيه ففي البدائع لا يجوز أداء الحج من المجنون والصبي الذي لا يعقل كما لا يجب عليهما. وقال ابن أمير حاج : قال مشايخنا وغيرهم بصحة حج الصبي ولو كان غير مميز وكذا بصحة حج المجنون ا هـ . وينبغي الجمع بينهما بحمل الأول على مجنون ليس له قابلية النية في الإحرام كالصبي الذي لا يعقل، والثاني على الذي له بعض الإدراكات الشرعية وعلى صحة حج الصبي الغير المميز إذا ناب عنه وليه في النية كذا في شرح لباب المناسك لمنلا علي القاري. أقول : المتعين حمل ما في البدائع على أداء المجنون والصبي بنفسهما بلا ،ولي وحمل ما نقله ابن أمير حاج على ما إذا أحرم عنهما وليهما فإن المجنون كالصبي في ذلك كما سنذكره قريباً عن الذخيرة والولوالجية وغيرهما قوله : (والمراد بالصحة صحة الجوارح قال في النهر قال بعض المتأخرين : يرد عليه المريض إذا كان صحيح الجوارح فإنه لا يجب عليه الحج أيضاً ومن ثم فسرها بعضهم بصحة البدن ويرد عليه أن الأعمى كذلك بدليل أن تصرفه ينفذ من كل المال أنه لا يجب عليه الحج فالأولى أن يفسر بسلامة البدن من الآفات المانعة مع عن القيام بما لا بد منه في السفر قوله : ( فلا يجب أداء الحج على مقعد الخ الأصوب أن يقول «فلا يجب الحج الخ ويسقط لفظة «أداء» ليوافق قوله بعده لا يجب عليهم الحج بأنفسهم ولا الإحجاج عنهم الخ لأن هذا بناء على أن الصحة من شرائط الوجوب فينافيه التعبير بالأداء تأمل قوله : (ولا مقطوع الرجلين) الظاهر أن مقطوع الرجل الواحدة ومقطوع اليدين كذلك لظهور الحرج عليهما إن وقع التكليف للحج بأنفسهما، ثم رأيت الكرماني نص على مقطوع اليدين أيضاً فمقطوع الرجل الواحدة بالأولى. كذا في شرح اللباب لمنلا علي القاري قوله : (والمحبوس) قال العلامة منلا علي القاري في شرحه على لباب المناسك : نقل عن شمس الإسلام أن السلطان ومن بمعناه من الأمراء ذوي الشأن ملحق بالمحبوس في هذا الحكم فيجب الحج في ماله يعني إذا كان له مال غير مستغرق لحقوق الناس في ذمته دون نفسه لأنه متى خرج من مملكته تخرب البلاد وتقع الفتنة بين العباد وربما يقتل في تلك الحالة وربما لا يمكنه ملك آخر من الدخول في حد مملكته فتقع فتنة عظيمة تفضي إلى مضرة بليغة لعامة المسلمين في أمر الدنيا والدين ا هـ . والظاهر أن هذا بالنسبة إلى من تكون سلطنته ثابتة بالشرائط الشرعية وإلا فيجب عليه خلع نفسه وإقامة من يستحق الخلافة مقامه في أمره إن لم البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ٣٥
His statement: (so no Hajj upon a slave, etc.) meaning it is not obligatory upon him, but it is valid from him and occurs as supererogatory. His statement: (nor upon a child, etc.) meaning it is not obligatory.
Already.
He must have surplus to his residence and expenses of going and returning and his dependents, and safe road, and a mahram or husband for a woman in travel, so if...
And regarding the insane (ma'tuh), there is a difference in principles: the author, following Fakhr al-Islam, holds that the address is removed from him like a child, so nothing of worship is obligatory upon him; al-Dabusi in al-Taqwim holds that he is addressed with worship as a precaution. And the meaning of health is soundness of limbs: so it is not obligatory to perform Hajj on a quadriplegic, nor on a chronically ill person, nor on a paralyzed person, nor on one with both legs amputated, nor on a sick person, nor on an old man who cannot steady himself on the mount, nor on a blind person, nor on a prisoner, nor on one fearing a ruler who prevents people from going out to Hajj. They are not obligated to perform Hajj themselves, nor to hire someone to perform Hajj on their behalf if they are able to do that—this is the apparent madhhab from Abu Hanifa, and it is a transmission from both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The apparent transmission from both is that they must hire someone, and if they hire someone it suffices them.
Also, if he performs Hajj while discerning (mumayyiz) by himself, or non-discerning by the ihram of his guardian, it is supererogatory. As for the non-sane, there is a difference: in al-Bada'i, performing Hajj by a madman and a non-discerning child is not permissible, just as it is not obligatory upon them. And Ibn Amir Haj said: our shaykhs and others said the Hajj of a child is valid even if non-discerning, and similarly the Hajj of a madman. It is necessary to reconcile by carrying the first on a madman who has no capacity for intention in ihram, like a non-discerning child, and the second on one who has some legal perception and on the validity of the Hajj of a non-discerning child if his guardian deputizes for him in intention, as in Sharh Lubab al-Manasik by Mulla Ali al-Qari. I say: the determinate view is to carry what is in al-Bada'i on the performance of Hajj by the madman and child themselves without a guardian, and carry what Ibn Amir Haj narrated on the case where their guardian performs ihram for them, because the madman is like a child in that regard, as we will soon mention from al-Dhakhira and al-Walwalijiyya and others. His statement: (and the meaning of health is soundness of limbs). He said in al-Nahr: some later scholars said: it is objected that the sick person is sound of limbs, yet Hajj is not obligatory upon him also; hence some interpreted it as soundness of the body. It is objected that the blind is also like that, since his transactions are effective in all his wealth, yet Hajj is not obligatory upon him. So the better interpretation is safety of the body from preventing ailments that prevent undertaking what is necessary in travel. His statement: (so it is not obligatory to perform Hajj on a quadriplegic, etc.) The more correct is to say 'so Hajj is not obligatory on...' and drop the word 'ada'' (performance) to agree with his later statement 'they are not obligated to perform Hajj themselves nor to hire someone for them' because this is based on health being a condition of obligation, so the expression of performance contradicts it, reflect. His statement: (nor on one with both legs amputated). Apparently, one with one leg amputated and one with both hands amputated are similar, due to the obvious hardship on them if the obligation to perform Hajj themselves is imposed. Then I saw al-Kirmani explicitly mentioned one with both hands amputated as well, so one with one leg amputated is more deserving. As in Sharh al-Lubab by Mulla Ali al-Qari. His statement: (and the prisoner). Allama Mulla Ali al-Qari said in his commentary on Lubab al-Manasik: it is transmitted from Shams al-Islam that the sultan and those like him from amirs of high status are annexed to the prisoner in this ruling; so Hajj is obligatory on his wealth, meaning if he has wealth not encumbered by rights of people in his liability, but not on his person, because if he leaves his kingdom, the lands will be ruined and fitna will occur among the people and perhaps he will be killed in that situation, and perhaps another king may not be able to enter his kingdom, leading to a great fitna causing severe harm to the general Muslims in worldly and religious matters. Apparently, this applies to one whose sultanate is established with legal conditions; otherwise, he must remove himself and install the one deserving caliphate in his place in his...
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling statement on who is excused from performing Hajj in person and whether they must send a substitute. It begins with comments on the condition of freedom and childhood, then discusses the insane (ma'tuh): the author (following Fakhr al-Islam) says the insane are not addressed like children, so no obligation; al-Dabusi says they are addressed as a precaution. The main focus is on 'health' meaning soundness of limbs, listing those excused: quadriplegic, chronically ill, paralyzed, amputee, sick, old man, blind, prisoner, and one fearing a tyrannical ruler. According to the apparent madhhab of Abu Hanifa, these individuals are not obligated to perform Hajj themselves nor to hire a substitute (ihjaj), even if they have the wealth. However, a transmission from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad says they must hire a substitute, and if they do, it suffices. The passage then discusses the validity of Hajj performed by a child or madman: if they perform it themselves, it is nafl; but if the guardian makes ihram for them, it is valid according to many. The reconciliation is that the madman who has no capacity for intention cannot perform Hajj himself, but if the guardian intends for him, it is valid. The commentator also refines the definition of 'health' by noting that even a healthy-limbed sick person is excused, so the correct interpretation is freedom from ailments that prevent travel. Finally, it extends the ruling of imprisonment to rulers (sultans) who cannot leave without causing fitna; in that case, Hajj is obligatory on their wealth (they must pay someone to go) but not on their person.

Key Terms
إحجاج (ihjaj): Sending someone else to perform Hajj on one's behalf, usually by hiring or asking another person.
صحة الجوارح (sihhat al-jawarih): Soundness of limbs; the text clarifies that this is not the intended meaning of 'health' in the conditions, because a person with sound limbs may still be sick or blind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent madhhab of Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on a wealthy blind person who cannot perform Hajj himself?
A) He must hire someone to perform Hajj on his behalf.
B) He is not obligated to perform Hajj himself nor to hire someone.
C) He must perform Hajj himself even if blind.
D) He must go with a guide.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Hajj is personal; inability removes it completely (Abu Hanifa) or transfers it to wealth (Sahibayn).

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Defining Health and Extending Excuses: The Hanafi List of Those Exempt from Hajj
Expansion of the definition of health and list of excused persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the list of individuals excused from personal Hajj performance and explain why the condition of health is defined as safety from travel-preventing ailments rather than soundness of limbs.

Core Idea
Health for Hajj means ability to travel safely, not just sound limbs.

The passage refines the common understanding of 'health' and extends the excuse to rulers who cannot leave without causing fitna. This lesson unpacks the list of excused persons and the reasoning behind the definition of health, including the annexation of rulers to prisoners.

Guided Path
1
Note the initial definition of health
The passage initially defines health as 'soundness of limbs' (sihhat al-jawarih). Understand that this is the literal meaning.
This is the definition found in some earlier texts.
2
Identify the objection to this definition
The commentator objects: a person with sound limbs can still be sick or blind, yet Hajj is not obligatory on them. So soundness of limbs alone is insufficient.
The objection shows that the definition must be broader.
3
Identify the refined definition
The better interpretation is 'safety of the body from ailments that prevent undertaking what is necessary in travel.' This covers sickness, blindness, and other impediments.
This refined definition is consistent with the list of excused individuals.
4
List the categories of excused individuals
The passage lists: quadriplegic, chronically ill, paralyzed, amputee, sick, old man, blind, prisoner, and one fearing a tyrannical ruler. Note that some categories are explicit and others are analogically extended.
For example, one with one leg amputated is included by qiyas.
5
Note the annexation of rulers to prisoners
Shams al-Islam holds that a ruler who cannot leave without causing fitna is annexed to the prisoner. In that case, Hajj is obligatory on his wealth (he must pay a substitute) but not on his person.
This is an exception: the ruler must still hire someone because he has the means but cannot go.

However, a transmission from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad says they must hire a substitute, and if they do, it suffices. The passage then discusses the validity of Hajj performed by a child or madman: if they perform it themselves, it is nafl; but if the guardian makes ihram for them, it is valid according to many. The reconciliation is that the madman who has no capacity for intention cannot perform Hajj himself, but if the guardian intends for him, it is valid. The commentator also refines the definition of 'health' by noting that even a healthy-limbed sick person is excused, so the correct interpretation is freedom from ailments that prevent travel. Finally, it extends the ruling of imprisonment to rulers (sultans) who cannot leave without causing fitna; in that case, Hajj is obligatory on their wealth (they must pay someone to go) but not on their person.

Key Terms
صحة الجوارح (sihhat al-jawarih): Soundness of limbs; the text clarifies that this is not the intended meaning of 'health' in the conditions, because a person with sound limbs may still be sick or blind.
المحبوس (al-mahbus): Prisoner; included in the list of those excused from personal Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refined definition in the passage, which of the following is the correct interpretation of 'health' for Hajj obligation?
A) Soundness of all limbs
B) Ability to walk without assistance
C) Safety of the body from ailments that prevent travel
D) Absence of any chronic disease

Key Takeaway
The condition for Hajj obligation is the ability to undertake the journey safely, not merely physical soundness; rulers who cannot leave without fitna are annexed to prisoners.
