The Condition of Rahila for Hajj Obligation
Explaining the definition and requirement of rahila for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of rahila for Hajj and explain why sharing a mount (uqbah) does not satisfy it.

Core Idea
Hajj is wajib only if you can ride the entire journey; sharing a mount does not meet the condition.

The obligation of Hajj is not absolute; it depends on the ability to travel, which in classical Hanafi fiqh includes having a suitable riding animal. This passage clarifies what qualifies as a rahila and what does not, highlighting distinctions between different types of mounts and addressing a dispute with the Shafi'i school. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly determining when Hajj becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Define rahila linguistically and legally
Identify that rahila in Arabic refers specifically to a camel mount, male or female. This implies that mere ability to ride another animal (e.g., mule or donkey) does not fulfill the condition—though scholars mention dislike (karaha) rather than explicit prohibition.
The linguistic definition sets the default, but custom may modify it.
2
Identify the core condition: continuous riding throughout the journey
The condition is having a rahila for the entire journey. If one can only arrange shared riding (uqbah), where two people take turns, this does not suffice because continuous personal riding is required.
3
Distinguish between types of mounts based on one's station
For a non-luxurious person, a 'ra's zamila' (pack animal with provisions) suffices. For a luxurious person, a 'shiq mahmil' (half-litter) is needed. This shows that the condition is relative to the person's custom and status.
The Hanafi school considers personal custom; the mount must be appropriate to one's usual mode of travel.
4
Understand why uqbah fails the condition
Uqbah involves hiring an animal jointly and alternating riding and walking. Since the person does not have continuous riding capability, the condition is not met, regardless of ability to walk.
Walking does not substitute for riding; the rahila is a separate condition.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i dispute regarding mu'addil
The Shafi'i school requires another person (mu'addil) to ride the other side of a mahmil if one can only ride a shiq mahmil. The Hanafi school rejects this, arguing that one can place provisions on the other side. The practical consequence: In Hanafi, Hajj is wajib even without a mu'addil; in Shafi'i, it is not.
The author shares a personal experience to illustrate the Hanafi position's practicality despite hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراحلة في اللغة المركب من الإبل ذكراً كان أو أنثى وهي فاعلة بمعنى مفعولة وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لو قدر على غير الراحلة من بغل أو حمار فإنه لا يجب عليه ولم أره صريحاً، وإنما صرحوا بالكراهة. ويعتبر في حق كل إنسان ما يبلغه فمن قدر على رأس زاملة - وهو المسمى في عرفنا راكب مقتب . وأمكنه السفر عليه وجب وإلا بأن كان مترفها فلا بد أن يقدر على شق محمل وهو المسمى في عرفنا محارة أو موهية، وإن أمكنه أن يكتري عقبة لا يجب عليه لأنه غير قادر على الراحلة في جميع الطريق وهو الشرط سواء كان قادراً على المشي أو لا والعقبة أن يكتري اثنان راحلة يتعقبان عليها يركب أحدهما مرحلة والآخر مرحلة وشق المحمل جانبه لأن للمحمل جانبين ويكفي للراكب أحد جانبيه، وقد رأيت في كتب الشافعية أن يركب في الجانب الآخر وهو المسمى بالمعادل، فإن لم يجد لا يجب الحج عليه ولم أره لأئمتنا، ولعلهم إنما لم يذكروه لما أنه ليس بشرط لإمكان أن يضع زاده وقربته وأمتعته في الجانب الآخر، وقد وقع لي ذلك في الحجة الثانية في الرجعة لم أجد معادلاً يصلح لي ففعلت ذلك لكن حصل لي نوع مشقة حين يقل الماء والزاد والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال .
And 'rahila' in language is a riding mount from camels, male or female, and it is a noun in the pattern of 'fa'ilah' meaning 'maf'ulah'. And in this there is an indication that if one is able on other than a rahila, such as a mule or donkey, then it is not obligatory upon him, and I have not seen it explicitly, rather they explicitly mentioned dislike (karaha). And consideration is in respect of every person what reaches him. So whoever is able to ride on a 'ra's zamila' - which is called in our custom 'rakib muqtab' - and it is possible for him to travel on it, it becomes obligatory. Otherwise, if he is a person of luxury, then he must be able to ride on a 'shiq mahmil' which is called in our custom 'muhara' or 'muhiya'. And if he is able to hire a 'uqbah' (alternating riding), it is not obligatory upon him because he is not capable of the rahila for the entire journey, and that is the condition, whether he is able to walk or not. And 'uqbah' is that two people hire a riding animal and take turns, one riding one stage and the other the next. And 'shiq al-mahmil' is its side, because the mahmil has two sides, and one side suffices for the rider. And I have seen in the books of the Shafi'is that one rides on the other side, which is called 'al-mu'addil', and if he does not find one, Hajj is not obligatory upon him. I have not seen this from our Imams, and perhaps they did not mention it because it is not a condition, due to the possibility that he puts his provisions, waterskin, and belongings on the other side. And this happened to me on the second Hajj on the return: I did not find a suitable 'mu'addil', so I did that, but I experienced some hardship when water and provisions became scarce. Allah knows the true state of affairs.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the condition of having a riding animal (rahila) for the obligation of Hajj. It begins by defining rahila linguistically as a camel mount, which implies that if one can afford a mule or donkey, Hajj is not obligatory solely due to that. The author notes he hasn't seen this explicitly, but scholars mention Karaha (dislike) for such. Then it details the requirement: one must have a mount suitable to his condition—if a person can ride on a 'ra's zamila' (a pack animal with provisions) and travel, Hajj is wajib. If one is accustomed to luxury, he must be able to ride a 'shiq mahmil' (half of a litter). Hiring a 'uqbah' (alternating turns) does not satisfy because one lacks continuous riding. The author also compares with Shafi'i school, where if no 'mu'addil' (someone to ride the other side) is found, Hajj is not obligatory. Our Imams didn't require this, as one can put provisions on the empty side, though it may be difficult.

Key Terms
الراحلة (al-rahila): A riding camel, male or female, capable of long-distance travel.
شق المحمل (shiq al-mahmil): One side of a litter (mahmil) used for riding.
العقبة (al-uqbah): A practice where two travelers share one riding animal, alternating riding and walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person is able to hire a 'uqbah' (alternating sharing) for the entire journey?
A) Hajj becomes wajib because he can travel the whole way.
B) Hajj does not become wajib because he is not capable of the rahila continuously.
C) It is makruh to do so, but Hajj is still valid.
D) It depends on whether he can walk the stages he does not ride.

Key Takeaway
The condition of rahila for Hajj requires continuous riding capability on a mount appropriate to one's station; sharing does not fulfill it, and the Hanafi school does not require a companion for a half-litter.

Condition of Ownership for Provisions and Riding Animal
Clarifying that capacity requires ownership or hire, not permission or gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for capacity (qudra) in Hajj regarding provisions and riding animal, and apply it to scenarios of permission, gift, and borrowing.

Core Idea
Ownership or hire establishes capacity for Hajj; permission or borrowing does not.

This passage clarifies a key condition for the obligation of Hajj: the capacity (qudra) must be based on ownership or hire, not on mere permission or borrowing. Even if someone offers to provide these for free, the obligation does not arise unless the individual themselves owns or hires the means. The Hanafi school strictly requires that the provisions and riding animal be owned or hired by the person, and no amount of external generosity creates the duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligation of Hajj. It is wajib only when certain conditions are met, one of which is capacity (qudra).
2
Identify the condition under discussion
The condition is capacity regarding provisions (zad) and riding animal (rahila). These are necessary for the journey.
3
State the Hanafi rule for provisions
Capacity for provisions is established only by ownership (milk), not by permission (ibaha). Even if someone permits you to use their provisions, it does not create the obligation.
Ownership means the provisions belong to you outright.
4
State the Hanafi rule for riding animal
Capacity for riding animal is established only by ownership or hire (ijarah). Borrowing (ariyah) or permission does not suffice. This applies to non-Makkans.
Hire is treated like ownership for the duration of the journey.
5
Apply the rule to the examples and exception
If a son offers obedience and permits his father provisions and riding animal, Hajj is not wajib on the father. Similarly, a gift of money for Hajj does not oblige acceptance. For a Makkan (or those near Makkah), the riding animal condition is waived because they can walk to Arafat without hardship.
The exception is based on ease; if a Makkan cannot walk at all, then a riding animal is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القدرة على الزاد لا تثبت إلا بالملك لا بالإباحة والقدرة على الراحلة لا تثبت إلا بالملك أو الإجارة لا بالعارية والإباحة، فلو بذل الابن لأبيه الطاعة وأباح له الزاد والراحلة لا يجب عليه الحج، وكذا لو وهب له مال ليحج به لا يجب عليه القبول لأن شرائط أصل الوجوب لا يجب عليه تحصيلها عند عدمها. ثم اشتراط القدرة على الزاد عام في حق كل حتى أهل مكة، وأما القدرة على الراحلة فشرط في حق غير المكي وأما هو فلا . ومن حولها كأهلها لأنه لا يلحقهم مشقة فأشبه السعي إلى الجمعة أما إذا كان لا يستطيع المشي أصلاً فلا بد منه في حق الكل. وفي قوله «وما لا بد منه» إشارة إلى أن المسكن لا بد
Then, capacity regarding provisions is only established by ownership, not by permission. And capacity regarding the riding animal is only established by ownership or hire, not by borrowing or permission. So if a son offers obedience to his father and permits him provisions and riding animal, Hajj is not obligatory upon him. Similarly, if someone gives him a gift of money to perform Hajj, he is not obliged to accept, because the conditions of the original obligation are not required to be procured when they are absent. Then, the condition of capacity for provisions is general for everyone, even the people of Makkah. As for capacity for a riding animal, it is a condition for those other than the Makkan, but for the Makkan, it is not. And those around it (Makkah) are like its people, because they do not experience hardship, so it resembles going to Jumu'ah. But if one cannot walk at all, then it is necessary for everyone. And in his statement 'and what is indispensable' (wa ma la budda minhu) there is an indication that the dwelling is indispensable...
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a clear ruling statement regarding the conditions of capacity (qudra) for Hajj. It distinguishes between ownership and mere permission. For provisions (zad), only ownership counts; permission from someone else (ibaha) does not make Hajj wajib. For the riding animal (rahila), one must own it or hire it; borrowing (ariyah) or permission does not suffice. The author gives examples: even if a son offers to provide everything for his father, the father is not obliged to go if he does not himself possess the means. Similarly, a gift of money for Hajj does not oblige acceptance. Then it explains that the condition of provisions applies to everyone, including Makkans, but the condition of a riding animal is only for non-Makkans (those outside the miqat), because Makkans can walk to Arafat easily, like going to Friday prayer. However, if a Makkan cannot walk at all, a riding animal becomes necessary. The phrase 'wa ma la budda minhu' is interpreted as referring to essential needs like housing, not a condition for Hajj.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Capacity/ability consisting of ownership or hire of provisions and riding animal.
المكي (al-makki): A resident of Makkah or within the miqat area; not required to have a riding animal for Hajj unless unable to walk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A resident of Madinah has no riding animal but his friend says, 'You can use my camel for Hajj for free.' Is Hajj wajib on him according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because he has access to a camel.
B) No, because borrowing does not establish capacity for the riding animal.
C) Yes, because the friend's permission is like ownership.
D) No, because he is not a Makkan but he could walk.

Key Takeaway
Capacity for Hajj is established only through ownership of provisions and ownership or hire of a riding animal; mere permission, gift, or borrowing does not oblige Hajj.

The Ruling on Mu'aadil and Required Mount Types for Hajj
Defines required mount types and disputes Shafi'i condition of mu'aadil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a mount in Hajj and explain why a mu'ādil is not required, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Continuous access to a mount is required for Hajj; a mu'ādil is not a condition in the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq clarifies the types of mounts that make Hajj obligatory and addresses a key dispute with the Shafi'is. You will learn what constitutes a sufficient mount in the Hanafi school and why sharing a mount by alternating stages or requiring a companion is not necessary.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on mount types
Identify the three types of mounts mentioned: ra's zāmila (head of a baggage camel) for ordinary persons, shiqq al-maḥmil (one side of a litter) for those accustomed to luxury, and 'uqba (alternating stages) which is insufficient.
Continuous access is the key condition.
2
Identify the Shafi'i condition of mu'ādil
Note that the Shafi'i school requires a companion (mu'ādil) to ride the other side of the litter, without which Hajj is not obligatory.
The author saw this in Shafi'i books.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i basis is that riding without a mu'ādil causes excessive difficulty, making the journey not feasible.
They consider capability (istitā'a) as including ease.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that one can place luggage on the empty side, and difficulty is manageable. The author provides personal experience as evidence.
The author's second Hajj example supports this.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude that in the Hanafi school, Hajj is obligatory on someone who can afford one side of a litter even without a mu'ādil, whereas in the Shafi'i school it is not.
This is a practical difference in making the obligation contingent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حق كل إنسان ما يبلغه فمن قدر على رأس زاملة - وهو المسمى في عرفنا راكب مقتب . وأمكنه السفر عليه وجب وإلا بأن كان مترفها فلا بد أن يقدر على شق محمل وهو المسمى في عرفنا محارة أو موهية، وإن أمكنه أن يكتري عقبة لا يجب عليه لأنه غير قادر على الراحلة في جميع الطريق وهو الشرط سواء كان قادراً على المشي أو لا والعقبة أن يكتري اثنان راحلة يتعقبان عليها يركب أحدهما مرحلة والآخر مرحلة وشق المحمل جانبه لأن للمحمل جانبين ويكفي للراكب أحد جانبيه، وقد رأيت في كتب الشافعية أن يركب في الجانب الآخر وهو المسمى بالمعادل، فإن لم يجد لا يجب الحج عليه ولم أره لأئمتنا، ولعلهم إنما لم يذكروه لما أنه ليس بشرط لإمكان أن يضع زاده وقربته وأمتعته في الجانب الآخر، وقد وقع لي ذلك في الحجة الثانية في الرجعة لم أجد معادلاً يصلح لي ففعلت ذلك لكن حصل لي نوع مشقة حين يقل الماء والزاد والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال . قوله : (على رأس زاملة) قال في السراج : الزاملة البعير يحمل عليه المسافر متاعه وطعامه قوله : (ولم أره لأئمتنا) قال الرملي : بل قواعدنا موافقة لهم وأنت عالم بأن من لم يجد معادلاً غير قادر، وما ذكره من وضع زاده وقربته الخ فاسد إذ المسألة مصورة فيمن يقدر على الشق فقط وحيث قدر على المحمل فلا كلام في الوجوب تأمل
For every person, [the capability] is what reaches him. So the one who is able [to afford] the head of a baggage camel - which in our terminology is called a 'rākib muqtab' - and can travel on it, it is obligatory. Otherwise, if he is accustomed to luxury, then he must be able [to afford] one side of a litter (shiqq al-maḥmil), which in our terminology is called 'maḥāra' or 'mawhiyya'. And if he can rent a mount for alternating stages ('uqba), it is not obligatory because he is not able [to have] the mount for the entire road, which is the condition, whether he is able to walk or not. The 'uqba is that two persons rent a mount, alternating on it: one rides for one stage and the other for the next. And 'shiqq al-maḥmil' is its side, because the litter has two sides, and for the rider one of its sides is sufficient. I have seen in the books of the Shafi'is that he rides on the other side, which is called the 'mu'ādil'. If he does not find [one], Hajj is not obligatory upon him. I have not seen this [opinion] from our imams. Perhaps they did not mention it because it is not a condition, since it is possible for him to place his provisions and water bag and belongings on the other side. And this happened to me on my second Hajj on the return journey: I did not find a mu'ādil suitable for me, so I did that; but I experienced some hardship when water and provisions became scarce. And Allah knows the reality of the matter. His saying: (على رأس زاملة) - al-Siraj said: 'Az-zāmila is the camel on which the traveler carries his belongings and food.' His saying: (ولم أره لأئمتنا) - al-Ramli said: 'Rather our principles agree with them. And you know that one who does not find a mu'ādil is not capable. And what he mentioned about placing his provisions and water bag etc. is invalid because the case is pictured for one who can [only afford] one side. If he can [afford] the litter, then there is no question about obligation. Reflect.'
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq. The author explains the condition of having a suitable mount for Hajj. He defines different types: 'ra's zāmila' is a riding seat on a pack camel, and 'shiqq al-maḥmil' is one side of a litter for a person accustomed to luxury. Sharing a mount by alternating stages ('uqba) is insufficient for obligation because continuous access to the mount is required. The author then highlights a difference with the Shāfi'ī school: they require a 'mu'ādil' - a companion riding on the other side of the litter - and consider its absence an obstacle to obligation. The Hanafī school does not require this, as one can place his luggage on the empty side. The author supports this with a personal experience. The comment from al-Ramlī defends the Hanafī position, arguing that the case where one finds only one side effectively means he cannot afford the full litter, so the obligation is lifted. However, if one can afford the full litter, the issue of mu'ādil does not arise. The passage thus clarifies that the mu'ādil is not a condition in the Hanafī madhhab, and the ruling is based on the general principle of capability.

Key Terms
زاملة (zāmila): A camel that carries the traveler's belongings and food; also used as a mount.
رأس زاملة (ra's zāmila): The front part of a baggage camel where a person rides; a type of mount for Hajj.
شق محمل (shiqq maḥmil): One side of a covered litter (mahmil) that can be ridden; a mount for a person accustomed to luxury.
عقبة ('uqba): An arrangement where two persons rent a mount and ride it alternately stage by stage.
معادل (mu'ādil): A companion who rides the other side of the litter to balance it; required by Shāfi'īs but not by Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following arrangements makes Hajj obligatory?
A) Being able to rent a mount for alternating stages ('uqba).
B) Being able to afford one side of a litter (shiqq al-maḥmil) for the entire journey.
C) Being able to afford a mu'ādil to share the litter.
D) Being able to walk part of the way and ride part of the way.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, continuous access to a mount for the entire Hajj journey is the condition for obligation; sharing by stages or requiring a mu'ādil are not necessary.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

8 min
Conditions for Hajj: Ownership of Provisions and Mount, and Exemption for Makkans
States ownership/rental condition for provisions and mount and exempts Makkans from mount requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Hajj obligation regarding provisions and mount, identify the exemptions for Makkans and those within the mawāqīt, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving gifts and loans.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when provisions are owned and the mount is owned or hired; Makkans need only provisions.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq explains that Hajj becomes obligatory only when a person has true capability (istitā‘a) over provisions and transport. The school distinguishes between ownership or hire—which create an obligation—and mere permission or borrowing, which do not. A special exemption applies to residents of Makka and those within the Mawaqit, who only need provisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling is that Hajj becomes obligatory (fard) only when the conditions of capability are met. The passage specifies the types of capability required.
2
Understand the condition for provisions
Capability for provisions (zād) is established only through ownership (milk), not through permission (ibāḥa) or a gift that is not accepted.
Example: if a son is given permission to use his father's food, Hajj is not obligatory.
3
Understand the condition for the mount
Capability for the mount (rāḥila) is established only through ownership or hiring (ijāra), not through borrowing (ʿāriya) or permission.
A borrowed mount does not create an obligation.
4
Apply the exemption for Makkans
Makkans and those within the mawāqīt (stations of iḥrām) are exempt from needing a mount; they only need provisions. If they cannot walk, a mount becomes necessary for everyone.
5
Analyse the intra-madhhab difference
There is a dispute over who counts as 'like a Makkan.' The first view: all within the mawāqīt. The second view: only those within three days' travel. Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī strengthened the second view.
The first view is more widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الشرائط أن يجد له من ثم القدرة على الزاد لا تثبت إلا بالملك لا بالإباحة والقدرة على الراحلة لا تثبت إلا بالملك أو الإجارة لا بالعارية والإباحة، فلو بذل الابن لأبيه الطاعة وأباح له الزاد والراحلة لا يجب عليه الحج، وكذا لو وهب له مال ليحج به لا يجب عليه القبول لأن شرائط أصل الوجوب لا يجب عليه تحصيلها عند عدمها. ثم اشتراط القدرة على الزاد عام في حق كل حتى أهل مكة، وأما القدرة على الراحلة فشرط في حق غير المكي وأما هو فلا . ومن حولها كأهلها لأنه لا يلحقهم مشقة فأشبه السعي إلى الجمعة أما إذا كان لا يستطيع المشي أصلاً فلا بد منه في حق الكل. وفي قوله «وما لا بد منه» إشارة إلى أن المسكن لا بد أحد ه. أن فسره المؤلف تأمل . ثم رأيت بعض الفضلاء نقل عن الشيخ عبد الله العفيف في شرح منسكه أنه اعترض كلام منلا علي فقال : لا يخفى منابذته لما قرروه من أنه يعتبر في حق كل ما يليق بحاله عادة وعرفاً إذ كثير من المترفهين لا يقدر على الركوب إلا في المحفة لا سيما عند بعد المسافة، فمن كان كذلك ينبغي أن يعتبر في حقه بلا ارتياب وأما لو قدر على غيرها من محمل أو رأس زاملة فلا يعذر ولو كان شريفاً أو وجيهاً أو ذا ثروة ا قوله : (على رأس زاملة) قال في السراج : الزاملة البعير يحمل عليه المسافر متاعه وطعامه قوله : (ولم أره لأئمتنا) قال الرملي : بل قواعدنا موافقة لهم وأنت عالم بأن من لم يجد معادلاً غير قادر، وما ذكره من وضع زاده وقربته الخ فاسد إذ المسألة مصورة فيمن يقدر على الشق فقط وحيث قدر على المحمل فلا كلام في الوجوب تأمل قوله : (ومن حولها كأهلها) قال في المنسك المتوسط المسمى لباب المناسك ومن كان داخل المواقيت فهو كالمكي في عدم اشتراط الراحلة، وقيل بل من كان دون مدة السفر، فمن كان من مكة على ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً فهو كالآفاقي في حق الراحلة وهو اختيار جماعة ا.هـ. وقوى الثاني شارحه منلا علي القاري
Among the conditions is that he finds for himself [the means]. Then capability for provisions is only established by ownership, not by permission (ibāḥa). Capability for the mount is only established by ownership or hiring (ijāra), not by borrowing (ʿāriya) or permission. So if a son offers obedience to his father and permits him provisions and mount, Hajj is not obligatory upon him. Similarly, if someone gives him money as a gift to perform Hajj, he is not obligated to accept it, because the conditions for the origin of obligation are not required to be acquired when they are absent. Then the condition of capability for provisions is general for everyone, even the people of Makkah. As for capability for the mount, it is a condition for the non-Makkan, but for the Makkan it is not. And those around it (Makka) are like its people, because no hardship befalls them, so it resembles going to Friday prayer. However, if he cannot walk at all, then it is necessary for everyone. And in His saying: 'and what is indispensable' there is an indication that housing is indispensable... one of them he interpreted? Reflect. Then I saw some virtuous ones quoting from Shaykh ʿAbd Allāh al-ʿAfīf in his commentary on his manāsik that he objected to the statement of Mullā ʿAlī, saying: 'It is not hidden that it contradicts what they established, that for each person what befits his state customarily and habitually is considered. For many of the luxurious ones cannot ride except in a sedan chair (miḥaffa), especially over a long distance. So whoever is like that should be considered in his case without doubt. But if he is able to [afford] other than it, like a litter or a head of a baggage camel, then he is not excused, even if he is a noble or a dignitary or wealthy.' His saying: (على رأس زاملة) – al-Sirāj said: 'Az-zāmila is the camel on which the traveler carries his belongings and food.' His saying: (ولم أره لأئمتنا) – al-Ramlī said: 'Rather our principles agree with them. And you know that one who does not find a muʿādil is not capable. And what he mentioned about placing his provisions and water bag etc. is invalid because the case is pictured for one who can [only afford] one side. If he can [afford] the litter, then there is no question about obligation. Reflect.' His saying: (ومن حولها كأهلها) – He said in al-Mansak al-Mutawassiṭ called Lubāb al-Manāsik: 'Whoever is within the mawāqīt is like the Makkan in that the mount is not required. And it is said: rather, whoever is less than the travel duration [i.e. within three days]. So whoever is three days or more from Makka is like the non-Makkan regarding the mount, and this is the choice of a group.' End. And the second view was strengthened by its commentator Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof segment from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq. It sets forth two key conditions for the obligation of Hajj: capability (qudra) over provisions must be through ownership, not mere permission; and capability over the mount must be through ownership or hire, not borrowing or permission. Therefore, if a son is granted permission by his father to use provisions and a mount, Hajj is not obligatory because the condition of ownership is not met. Similarly, accepting a gift of money for Hajj is not obligatory. These are conditions of the original obligation; one need not acquire them if absent. Then the passage distinguishes between residents of Makka and others: the condition of having a mount applies only to non-Makkans; Makkans are exempt because they do not face long travel hardship, analogous to the exemption from transport for Friday prayer. However, if a Makkan cannot walk at all, a mount becomes necessary for everyone. The passage also includes a critique of Mullā ʿAlī's view, arguing that capability should be judged according to one's customary state; a person accustomed to luxury may require a sedan chair, but if he can afford a litter or camel, he is not excused. Finally, the text discusses who is considered 'like the Makkan': those within the mawāqīt (stations of iḥrām) are considered like Makkans, while a different view holds that those within three days' travel are like Makkans, and Mullā ʿAlī strengthens this latter view.

Key Terms
زاد (zād): Provisions, food and drink for the journey.
راحلة (rāḥila): A mount (riding animal) suitable for travel; required for Hajj for non-Makkans.
إباحة (ibāḥa): Permissive ownership (e.g., a gift or permission to use) does not establish capability for obligation.
عارية (ʿāriya): A loan of an object for use; does not count as capability for mount.
مكي (Makki): A resident of Makka; exempt from needing a mount for Hajj because of proximity.
مواقيت (mawāqīt): Stations where pilgrims enter iḥrām; those within them are considered like Makkans regarding mount requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A non-Makkan man is offered a free mount for Hajj by a friend. Is Hajj obligatory upon him according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because he has the means to travel.
B) No, because the mount is not owned or hired by him.
C) Yes, but only if he accepts the offer.
D) No, because he must own the mount outright.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is only obligatory when one owns provisions and owns or hires a mount (for non-Makkans); permission or borrowing does not create capability.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Indispensable Needs Exempt from Sale for Hajj
Expansion of the rule on indispensable needs for Hajj capability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the indispensable needs that exempt a person from selling assets for Hajj according to the Hanafi school, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving housing, capital, and timing.

Core Idea
Essential assets (house, servant, tools, capital) are not sold for Hajj; but cash must be used when the time arrives.

This lesson examines the Hanafi concept of 'original needs' (ḥawāʾij aṣliyya) that exempt a person from having to sell assets to fund the Hajj pilgrimage. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq clarifies what counts as indispensable and distinguishes between one who owns essential assets and one who has cash. A key nuance is that if the Hajj time arrives, having cash makes Hajj obligatory even if one lacks a house, because refraining from buying a house does not cause the same hardship as selling an existing one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that one is not required to sell essential assets (house, servant, clothing, necessary belongings) to perform Hajj. Only surplus wealth beyond these needs triggers obligation.
This is based on the phrase 'mā lā budda minhu' (what is indispensable).
2
List the Exempted Assets
From the text, list the following: residence (house used for living), servant, clothing, essential household items, business capital (for merchants), tools of trade (for artisans), and debts. These are 'original needs' (ḥawāʾij aṣliyya).
Capital for trade/farming is exempt; artisan only needs tools, not capital.
3
Analyze the Exception for Cash
If a person has no house or servant but possesses sufficient cash for Hajj and for basic needs during travel, and the time for departure has arrived, then Hajj is obligatory. He cannot spend that cash to buy a house first.
This is the view of Abū Yūsuf, adopted as muftā bihī. The text resolves an apparent conflict with al-Khulāṣa.
4
Understand the Underlying Rationale
The difference is that selling an existing asset (house, servant) causes hardship, whereas refraining from buying a new asset does not. Therefore, the obligation is tied to ownership of surplus cash, not to the ability to sell essential assets.
This is a rational (ʿaqlī) derivation, not based on a specific textual proof.

Source Text

وفي قوله «وما لا بد منه» إشارة إلى أن المسكن لا بد يكون محتاجاً إليه للسكنى فلا تثبت الاستطاعة بدار يسكنها وعبد يستخدمه وثياب يلبسها ومتاع يحتاج إليه، وتثبت الاستطاعة بدار لا يسكنها وعبد لا يستخدمه فعليه أن يبيعه ويحج بخلاف ما إذا كان سكنه وهو كبير يفضل عنه حتى يمكنه بيعه والاكتفاء بما دونه ببعض ثمنه ويحج بالفضل فإنه لا يجب بيعه لذلك كما لا يجب بيع مسكنه والاقتصار على السكني بالإجارة اتفاقاً . يشير إلى اشتراطها فيه أيضاً. وجعل في النهر الإشارة من العدول عن التعبير بالدار إلى المسكن، وما فعله المؤلف أحسن لئلا يرد عليه ما إذا كان ساكناً فيه ويستغنى عنه بسكناه في غيره أيضاً قوله : (بخلاف ما المناسك، وصرح به في اللباب حيث قال : ومن مال يبلغه ولا مسكن له ولا خادم فليس له صرفه إليه إن حضر الوقت بخلاف من له مسكن يسكنه لا يلزمه بيعه . قال منلا علي في شرحه والفرق بينهما ما في البدائع وغيره عن أبي يوسف أنه قال : إذا لم يكن له مسكن ولا خادم وله مال يكفيه لقوت عياله من وقت ذهابه إلى حين إيابه وعنده دراهم تبلغه إلى الحج لا ينبغي أن يجعل ذلك في غير الحج، فإن فعل أثم لأنه مستطيع بملك الدراهم فلا يعذر في الترك ولا يتضرر بترك شراء المسكن والخادم بخلاف بيع المسكن والخادم فإنه يتضرر ببيعهما ا هـ. على أنه قال بعض الفضلاء : إن عبارة الخلاصة خلاف ما نقله المؤلف عنها ونص عبارتها ناقلاً - عن التجريد : إن كان له دار لا يسكنها وعبد لا يستخدمه فعليه أن يبيعه ويحج به، وإن لم يكن له مسكن ولا شيء من ذلك وعنده دراهم يبلغ بها الحج ويبلغ ثمن مسكن وخادم وطعام وثوب فعليه الحج. وإن جعلها في غير الحج أثم ا هـ . فتعين ما قدمناه عن اللباب وبه صرح في التتارخانية أيضاً قوله : (إليه أشار في ذلك الخلاصة أقول : الذي رأيته في الخلاصة خلافه ونصها وإن لم يكن له مسكن ولا شيء من . وعنده دراهم تبلغ به الحج وتبلغ ثمن مسكن وخادم وطعام وقوت عليه الحج وإن جعلها في غيره أثم .. اهـ. بحروفه قوله : (وقد يقال اعتبار الوسط الخ قال الرملي : ليس هذا المقصود بل المقصود اعتبار
And in His saying 'and what is indispensable' there is an indication that housing must be needed for residence, so capability is not established by a house he lives in, a servant he uses, clothes he wears, or belongings he needs. Capability is established by a house he does not live in or a servant he does not use; he must sell them and perform Hajj. Unlike the case when his dwelling is large and there is a surplus beyond his need, such that he can sell it and suffice with something less for part of its price and perform Hajj with the surplus; then he is not required to sell it for that purpose, just as he is not required to sell his home and settle for renting by consensus. Rather, if he sells and buys his need and performs Hajj with the surplus, it is better. And if he has no house or servant and has money that would cover their price but nothing remains after that for Hajj, then Hajj is not obligatory because that wealth is occupied by the original need. He indicated in al-Khulāṣa. And he indicated by His saying 'and what is indispensable' that there must remain for him money equivalent to the capital of trade after Hajj if he is a merchant, and likewise the village head and farmer. As for the artisan, no [such condition]. This is in al-Khulāṣa. And capital varies according to people. And by 'dependents' is meant those whose maintenance is obligatory upon him. The commentator said: 'In his maintenance and the maintenance of his dependents, the moderate level is considered without extravagance.' His servant, tools of his craft, payment of his debts, and housing are similar, because all are original needs. So conditioning need for other than housing indicates its conditioning for it as well. And in al-Nahr, the indication is from the change from the expression 'dār' to 'maskin', and what the author did is better to avoid the objection when he lives in it and can do without it by living elsewhere. His saying: (بخلاف ما إذا كان سكنه) – the pronoun in 'kāna' refers to the house, interpreting 'maskin' or 'place', i.e. unlike when it is his dwelling and it is large etc. So his word 'sakanahu' with the three vowels is the predicate of 'kāna', and it is a noun meaning 'house', not a verb, and his word 'wa huwa kabīr' is a circumstantial clause. His saying: (ولو لم يكن له مسكن الخ) – this is carried on what is before the arrival of the time when the people of his town depart. If the time arrives, performing the ritual becomes incumbent upon him, and he is not allowed to divert it to something else, as Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī mentioned in his commentary on Lubāb al-Manāsik. It is stated explicitly in al-Lubāb: 'Whoever has money that reaches [the cost of Hajj] but has no house or servant, he is not allowed to divert it to something else if the time has arrived, unlike one who has a house he lives in; he is not required to sell it.' Mullā ʿAlī said in his commentary: 'The difference between them is what is in al-Badāʾiʿ and others from Abū Yūsuf: he said: If he has no house or servant but has money sufficient for his dependents' sustenance from the time of his departure until his return, and he has dirhams that will take him to Hajj, he should not spend that on other than Hajj. If he does, he sins because he is capable by owning the dirhams, so he is not excused for leaving it, and he is not harmed by leaving off buying a house and servant, unlike selling the house and servant, for he would be harmed by selling them.' End. However, some virtuous ones said: 'The wording of al-Khulāṣa is contrary to what the author transmitted from it, and its text, quoting from al-Tajrīd, is: If he has a house he does not live in and a servant he does not use, he must sell them and perform Hajj. And if he has no house or anything of that sort and has dirhams that will take him to Hajj and will also cover the price of a house, servant, food, and clothing, then Hajj is obligatory upon him. If he spends them on other than Hajj, he sins.' End. So what we presented from al-Lubāb is established, and it is explicitly stated in al-Tātārkhāniyya as well. His saying: (إليه أشار في ذلك الخلاصة) – I say: What I saw in al-Khulāṣa is contrary to that. Its text: 'And if he has no house or anything . . . and he has dirhams that will take him to Hajj and will cover the price of a house, servant, and food, Hajj is obligatory upon him. If he spends them on other than Hajj, he sins.' End. In his own words. His saying: (وقد يقال اعتبار الوسط الخ) – al-Ramli said: 'This is not the intended meaning; rather the intended meaning is consideration...'
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq explaining the concept of 'what is indispensable' (mā lā budda minhu) in the context of Hajj capability. The author clarifies that essential assets for living are not considered wealth for the purpose of istiṭāʿa (capability). These include: a house one lives in, a servant one uses, clothes one wears, and necessary belongings. If one has a surplus house or servant, he must sell them to fund Hajj. However, if his house is large and he can sell it, buy a smaller one, and use the surplus for Hajj, he is not forced to do so; it is merely better. If he has no house or servant but has enough money to buy them, and no surplus remains for Hajj, Hajj is not obligatory because the money is needed for basic necessities. The passage also expands the exception to business capital: a merchant, farmer, or village head must retain enough capital to continue his trade after Hajj; an artisan does not need such a reserve. The definition of 'dependents' is those whom one must support. The commentator says that one's own maintenance and that of dependents should be at a moderate level without extravagance. The phrase 'what is indispensable' also includes tools of trade, debts, and housing. The text then engages in a discussion about whether a person who has no house but has money must use it for Hajj or may first buy a house. The preferred view (from al-Lubāb and supported by Abū Yūsuf) is that if the time for departure has arrived, he must use the money for Hajj and cannot defer it to buy a house, because he is capable by owning the cash. However, he is not required to sell an existing house. This ruling is clarified by distinguishing between selling an existing asset (harmful) and refraining from buying one (not harmful). The passage ends with a note on the text of al-Khulāṣa and a discussion on the moderate standard for expenditure, though the latter is cut off.

Key Terms
ما لا بد منه (mā lā budda minhu): Indispensable items such as housing, servant, clothing, tools, and business capital that are not sold for Hajj.
رأس المال (raʾs al-māl): Capital for trade or farming that must be preserved for livelihood after Hajj; not to be spent on Hajj.
محترف (muḥtarif): An artisan or craftsman who earns by his labor; he does not need to retain capital, only his tools.
ديون (duyūn): Debts that are due; paying them is an original need before Hajj obligation.
وسط (wasaṭ): Moderate level of expenditure without extravagance or miserliness; used in maintenance calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has $10,000 cash, no house, and no debts. Hajj costs $8,000. According to the Hanafi school, is Hajj obligatory?
A) No, because he needs a house.
B) Yes, because he has surplus cash.
C) No, because he can invest the money.
D) Yes, but only if he sells all his belongings.

Key Takeaway
Essential assets for living are not sold for Hajj, but surplus cash must be used when the time arrives; the key is whether hardship is incurred by selling vs. refraining from buying.

Condition of Safety on the Road and Sea Travel for Hajj Obligation
Explains when fear of enemies or necessity of sea travel precludes Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of safety for Hajj obligation and apply the Hanafi rule on sea travel to determine when Hajj is obligatory.

Core Idea
Hajj is only wajib when the route is safe; sea travel does not automatically exempt if the crossing is generally safe.

In this passage, the author of Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the obligation of Hajj depends on safety from enemies on the road. If fear predominates due to bandits or war, Hajj is not wajib. He then addresses a common question: does the need to travel by sea remove the obligation? The answer depends on the usual safety of that sea route, not on the mere fact of being at sea. A hadith distinguishing rivers from seas supports this balanced approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on road safety
Locate the condition: Hajj is wajib only when safety predominates (ghalabat al-salamah). If fear of enemies dominates, the obligation drops.
This is a condition of obligation (wujub), not just performance.
2
Understand the disagreement on sea travel
Note that some scholars say customary sea travel prevents obligation; al-Kirmani disagrees. The preferred view (al-ashah) is that if the sea route is usually safe, Hajj is wajib; otherwise not.
The decisive factor is the general safety of that particular crossing.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith about Sayhan, Jayhan, Euphrates, and Nile being rivers from Paradise is cited. This is used to argue that large rivers are not dangerous seas.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but used for guidance.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The classification of these waters as rivers indicates they are safe for travel, unlike seas. Therefore, travel on such rivers is treated like land travel for Hajj obligation.
The implication is that the safety of the water body matters, not its mere size.
5
Apply the preferred view
According to al-Kirmani's view (which is the relied-upon position), one must assess the predominance of safety on the sea route. If safe, Hajj is wajib; if not, it is not.
This balances the principle of safety with the necessity of performing Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع غلبة السلامة عدم غلبة الخوف حتى إذا غلب الخوف على القلوب من المحاربين لوقوع النهب والغلبة منهم مراراً وسمعوا أن طائفة تعرضت للطريق ولها شوكة والناس يستضعفون لا يجب. واختلف في سقوطه إذا لم يكن بد من ركوب البحر؛ فقيل البحر العادة يمنع الوجوب وقال الكرماني : إن كان الغالب في البحر السلامة من موضع جرت بركوبه يجب وإلا فلا وهو الأصح وسيحون وجيحون والفرات والنيل أنهار لا بحار كما في الحديث سيحان وجيحان والفرات والنيل كل من أنهار الجنة .
With predominance of safety, not predominance of fear, so if fear dominates hearts from the warriors due to occurrence of plunder and overwhelming from them repeatedly, and they hear that a group has blocked the road and has power, and the people consider them weak, it is not obligatory. And there is disagreement on its dropping if there is no alternative but to ride the sea: it was said that customary sea travel prevents obligation, and al-Kirmani said: if safety is predominant in the sea from a place where sailing is customary, it is obligatory, otherwise not, and that is the most correct. And the Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, and Nile are rivers, not seas, as in the hadith: 'Sayhan, Jayhan, Euphrates, and Nile are all from the rivers of Paradise.'
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining that safety from enemies on the road is a condition for the obligation of Hajj. The author clarifies that if fear of bandits predominates, Hajj is not wajib. Then he addresses the issue of sea travel: there is a difference of opinion whether the need to travel by sea removes the obligation. The preferred view (al-ashah) is that if the sea route is generally safe, Hajj is obligatory; otherwise it is not. He supports this with a hadith classifying certain large bodies of water as rivers, not seas, implying that river travel is easier and safer.

Key Terms
غلبة السلامة (ghalabat al-salamah): Predominance of safety on the road such that fear is not overwhelming.
ركوب البحر (rukuub al-bahr): The act of traveling by sea; if unavoidable, its safety is judged like land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view, when does riding the sea exempt a person from Hajj obligation?
A) Whenever there is any fear of the sea.
B) When the sea is generally unsafe in that particular crossing.
C) Only if the sea is a large ocean like the Atlantic.
D) When the person is a weak swimmer.

Key Takeaway
Safety from enemies and a generally safe sea crossing are conditions for Hajj obligation according to the Hanafi school.

The Condition of Mahram for a Woman's Hajj Journey
Ruling with proof from hadith, refuting analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's requirement of a mahram for Hajj travel, cite the primary hadith evidence, and refute the opposing view based on qiyas ma'a al-nass.

Core Idea
A woman must have a mahram or husband to travel for Hajj; the hadith is explicit and analogy to trustworthy women fails.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that a woman's Hajj journey is conditional upon having a mahram or husband. The author cites multiple hadiths that explicitly prohibit travel without a mahram, and refutes the analogy to trustworthy women traveling together. We will analyze the proof structure and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: A woman must have a mahram or husband to travel for Hajj. Without one, Hajj is not obligatory upon her, and traveling without is haram.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the primary dalil
Locate the hadith evidence: the author cites the Sahihain and Musnad al-Bazzar with explicit prohibitions.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) but the meaning is clear (qati dalala).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the prohibition (nahy) indicates impermissibility, and the command to accompany shows necessity.
The Prophet's order to the man to return and accompany his wife is a strong proof.
4
Evaluate the opposing view
Some scholars argue that a group of trustworthy women suffices. The author rejects this as qiyas ma'a al-nass (analogy against the text).
The analogy to the emigrant woman and captive is invalid because their situation is not travel for worship.
5
Understand the refutation
The emigrant and captive travel to escape fitna, not to a specific destination for worship. Moreover, company may increase fitna, as seclusion with non-mahram is forbidden.
Thus the text takes precedence over analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومحرم أو زوج لامرأة في سفر أي وبشرط محرم إلى آخره لما في الصحيحين «لا تسافر امرأة ثلاثاً إلا ومعها محرم» وزاد مسلم في رواية أو زوج. وروى البزاز «لا تحج امرأة إلا ومعها محرم فقال رجل: يا رسول الله إني كتبت في غزوة وامرأتي حاجة قال : ارجع فحج معها فأفاد هذا كله أن النسوة الثقات لا تكفي قياساً على المهاجرة والمأسورة لأنه قياس مع النص مع وجود الفارق فإن الموجود في المهاجرة والمأسورة ليس سفراً لأنها لا تقصد مكاناً معيناً بل النجاة خوفاً من الفتنة حتى لو وجدت مأمناً كعسكر المسلمين وجب أن تقر، ولأنه يخاف عليها الفتنة وتزاد بانضمام غيرها إليها ولهذا تحرم الخلوة بالأجنبية وإن كان معها غيرها لا يجوز له مناكحتها على التأبيد بقرابة أو رضاع أو مصاهرة.
His saying: (And a mahram or a husband for a woman in travel) meaning: and with the condition of a mahram, etc. Because in the two Sahihs: 'A woman should not travel for three days except with a mahram.' And Muslim added in a narration: 'or a husband.' And al-Bazzar narrated: 'A woman should not perform Hajj except with a mahram.' A man said: O Messenger of Allah, I have enlisted in a military expedition and my wife intends Hajj. He said: Return and perform Hajj with her. All this indicates that trustworthy women (traveling with other women) are not sufficient, by analogy to the emigrant woman and the captive, because that is an analogy against the text, and there is a difference: the case of the emigrant and captive is not travel, as they do not intend a specific place but rather escape out of fear of fitna. So if she finds a safe place like a Muslim army, she must stay. And because fitna is feared for her and is increased by the company of others. Therefore, seclusion with a non-mahram woman is forbidden, and even if another person is with her, it is not permissible for him to marry her on a permanent basis due to lineage, fosterage, or marriage affinity.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from multiple hadiths establishing that a woman must have a mahram or husband to travel for Hajj. The author refutes the analogy to trustworthy women traveling together, citing that the hadiths are explicit and the analogy fails because the situations differ: emigrant women flee fitna, not travel for worship. The condition of mahram is strict; even if a woman is trustworthy, she may not travel alone or with other women.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, fosterage, or affinity.
نسوة ثقات (niswah thiqaat): Trustworthy women traveling together without a mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the analogy of trustworthy women to the emigrant woman (muhajirah) and captive (asirah)?
A) Because trustworthy women are not like captives.
B) Because the emigrant and captive do not intend a specific travel but escape fitna.
C) Because the emigrant woman is more pious than a trustworthy woman.
D) Because the hadith only applies to spouses.

Key Takeaway
A woman must have a mahram or husband to travel for Hajj; the hadith is explicit and qiyas cannot override it.

Defining Mahram and its Conditions for Women's Travel
Definition of mahram with conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mahram for women's travel and identify which persons qualify or are excluded based on conditions of adulthood, sanity, trustworthiness, and religious affiliation.

Core Idea
A mahram for travel must be adult, sane, trustworthy, and not a Magian — the purpose is protection, not mere relation.

The Hanafi school defines a mahram for a woman's travel very specifically: it is the husband or any person permanently forbidden to marry her by blood, fosterage, or affinity. But being a relative is not enough—the mahram must meet certain conditions to ensure he can actually protect her. This lesson parses the definition and the conditions that make or break a mahram's eligibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the opening: 'wal-mahram al-zawj wa man la yajūzu lah munākaḥatuhā 'alā al-ta'bīd...' The mahram is either the husband or anyone permanently forbidden to marry her.
The husband is included even though marriage with him is not prohibited—he is a special case.
2
List the inclusions and exclusions
The text lists who is included (Muslim, dhimmi, free, slave) and explicitly excludes four: the Magian who believes marriage permissible, the untrustworthy relative, the pre-pubescent boy, and the insane.
The purpose of mahram is protection (al-ḥifẓ wa al-ṣiyānah); these four lack the capacity or intent to protect.
3
Analyze the husband's special status
The author notes that while no conditions are usually stipulated for the husband, he must still be trustworthy and capable—otherwise he fails the purpose.
This is an important extension: even a husband can be disqualified if he is untrustworthy, a boy, or insane.
4
Note the exception for young girls
A girl who has not reached the age of desire (shahwah) may travel without a mahram; once she reaches it, she requires one.
This is not simply puberty; it is the age when she becomes an object of desire and needs protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمحرم الزوج ومن لا يجوز له مناكحتها على التأبيد بنسب أو رضاع أو صهرية، ومثله فشمل المسلم والذمي والحر والعبد ولا يرد عليه المجوسي الذي يعتقد إباحة نكاحها والمسلم القريب إذا لم يكن مأموناً والصبي الذي لم يحتلم والمجنون لأن المقصود من المحرم الحفظ والصيانة لها وهو مفقود في هؤلاء الأربعة ولم أر من شرط في الزوج شروط المحرم، وينبغي أنه لا فرق لأن الزوج إذا لم يكن مأموناً أو كان صبياً أو مجنوناً لم يوجد منه ما هو المقصود كما ذكرنا وعبارة المجمع أولى وهي ويشترط في حج المرأة من سفر زوج أو محرم بالغ عاقل غير مجوسي ولا فاسق مع النفقة عليه وأطلق المرأة فشمل الشابة والعجوز لإطلاق النصوص. والمرأة هي البالغة لأن الكلام فيمن يجب عليه الحج فلذا قالوا في الصبية التي لم تبلغ حد الشهوة تسافر بلا محرم فإن بلغتها لا تسافر إلا به.
And the mahram is the husband and whoever is not permitted to marry her permanently due to lineage, fosterage, or marriage affinity, and the like. So it includes the Muslim and the dhimmi, the free and the slave. But it does not include the Magian who believes in the permissibility of marrying her, nor the Muslim relative if he is not trustworthy, nor the boy who has not reached puberty, nor the insane person, because the purpose of the mahram is protecting and guarding her, and that is absent in these four. And I have not seen anyone stipulate the conditions of a mahram for the husband, but it is appropriate that there is no difference, because if the husband is not trustworthy, or is a boy, or insane, the intended purpose is not present as we mentioned. And the expression of al-Majma' is better: It is stipulated in the Hajj of a woman traveling (that she have) a husband or a mahram who is an adult, sane, not a Magian, nor a sinner, with his expenses. And he used the general term 'woman' so it includes the young and the old due to the generality of the texts. And the woman is the one who has reached puberty because the discussion is about those upon whom Hajj is obligatory. Therefore they said concerning the girl who has not reached the age of desire: she may travel without a mahram; but if she has reached it, she shall not travel except with one.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This is a definition of mahram with its conditions. The mahram is the husband or anyone permanently forbidden in marriage by blood, fosterage, or affinity. He must be adult, sane, Muslim (or dhimmi), not a Magian, and not a sinner. However, the text notes that the husband is automatically considered a mahram, but he too must be trustworthy and capable of protection. The condition applies to all women, young or old, but a prepubescent girl may travel without a mahram.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, or the husband, who must be adult, sane, trustworthy, and able to protect.
صبية (sabiyyah): A girl who has not reached the age of desire (bulugh al-shahwah), who may travel without a mahram.
فاسق (fāsiq): A sinner who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking trustworthiness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Her adult Muslim brother who is trustworthy.
B) Her husband who is a dhimmi.
C) Her cousin who is a Magian (believes marriage to her is permissible).
D) Her father who is a slave.

Key Takeaway
A mahram for travel must be an adult, sane, trustworthy individual who is permanently ineligible to marry the woman—or her husband—and must not be a Magian or a sinner; the purpose is solitary protection, not mere relation.

The Mahram Condition for Women's Hajj: Obligation or Performance?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahram as condition for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the mahram is a condition of obligation or performance for a woman's Hajj, and identify the practical consequences (thamarah) of each view.

Core Idea
Is the mahram a condition of obligation? Then no duty to secure it. A condition of performance? Then she must secure it.

The Hanafi school is internally divided on a crucial question for women's Hajj: is having a mahram a condition for the very obligation to perform Hajj (shart al-wujub), or is it a condition for valid performance (shart al-ada')? This distinction produces very different practical rulings. Let us trace the reasoning and see how the scholars justified their positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practical consequences
First, list the three legal outcomes that depend on how the mahram condition is classified: (1) obligation to make a will, (2) obligation to pay the mahram's expenses, (3) obligation to marry to obtain a mahram.
These are the thamarah al-khilaf.
2
Contrast the two views on those consequences
If the mahram is a condition of obligation, none of these are obligatory because a condition for obligation need not be acquired. If it is a condition of performance, all become obligatory because the woman must remove the obstacle to perform a fard.
This contrast is the core of the dispute.
3
Examine the authorities and their arguments
Qadikhan declared it a condition of performance; the authors of al-Bada'i' and al-Saruji declared it a condition of obligation. Note the reasoning: the one who says performance argues that Hajj admits deputyship and is linked to financial capacity; the mahram is a means to enable performance.
Both sides use Hanafi usul principles.
4
Determine the preponderant view
The author of al-Lubab leans toward the condition of performance, but the text also reports reconciliation: if the mahram demands expenses, she must pay; otherwise not.
This is not a definitive tarjih; fatwa may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في وجوب الوصية وفي وجوب نفقة المحرم وراحلته إذا أبى أن يحج معها إلا بهما وفي وجوب التزوج عليها ليحج معها إن لم تجد محرماً، فمن قال هو شرط الوجوب قال لا يجب عليها شيء من ذلك لأن شرط الوجوب لا يجب تحصيله، ولهذا لو ملك المال كان له الامتناع من القبول حتى لا يجب عليه الحج، وكذا لو أبيح له. ومن قال إنه شرط وجوب الأداء وجب جميع ورجح المحقق في أداء بأن هذه العبادة تجري فيها النيابة عند الصحة شروط وجوب مع فتح القدير أنهما العجر لا مطلقاً توسطاً دائر مع ذلك ، بين المالية المحضة والبدنية المحضة لتوسطها بينهما، والوجوب أمر فائدته فيثبت مع قدرة المال ليظهر أثره في الإحجاج والإيصاء، واعلم أن الاختلاف في وجوب الإيصاء إذا مات قبل أمن الطريق فإن مات بعد حصول الأمن فالاتفاق على الوجوب . وأشار باشتراط المحرم أو الزوج إلى أن العدة عدم في حقها شرط أيضاً بجد مع حرمة السفر عليها أي عدة كانت والعبرة لوجوبها وقت خروج أهل بلدها، وعن ابن مسعود أنه رد المعتدات من النجف بفتحتين مكان لا يعلوه الماء مستطيل فإن لزمتها العدة في السفر فسيأتي في محله إن شاء الله تعالى.
ثم اختلفوا في أن المحرم أو الزوج شرط الوجوب أو الأداء كما اختلفوا في أمن الطريق، فصح قاضيخان وغيره أنه من شرائط الأداء، وصحح صاحب البدائع والسروجي شرائط الوجوب، وصنيع المصنف - أي صاحب اللباب - يشعر بأنه من شرائط الأداء على الأرجح قوله : (وفي وجوب نفقة المحرم (الخ) صحح في السراج الوجوب وحكى في اللباب القولين بلا ترجيح لكن قدم الأول فقال : قيل نعم وقيل لا ا هـ . أي لا يلزمه ولا تجب عليها ما لم يخرج المحرم بنفقته على ما ذكره الطحاوي وهو قول أبي حفص البخاري. وفي منسك ابن أمير حاج : وهل تجب عليها نفقة المحرم والقياء براحلته؟ اختلفوا فيه وصححوا عدم الوجوب. وفي السراج الوهاج : التوفيق بين القولين أن الحرم إذا قال لا أخرج إلا بالنفقة وجب عليها وإذا خرج من غير اشتراط
And the fruit of the difference appears in the obligation of the will, and in the obligation of the expense of the mahram and his mount if he refuses to perform Hajj with her except with both of them, and in the obligation of marrying to perform Hajj with her if she does not find a mahram. One who says it is a condition of obligation says none of that is obligatory upon her because a condition of obligation does not have to be fulfilled. For this reason, if one owns wealth, he may refrain from accepting [the obligation] so that Hajj is not obligatory upon him, and likewise if it is permitted to him. And one who says it is a condition of performance makes all of it obligatory, and the verifier gave preponderance to [the view that it is a condition of] performance because this act of worship admits deputyship when valid, conditions of obligation with Fath al-Qadir that both are [conditions of] inability, not absolutely, intermediately rotating with that, between pure financial and pure physical, due to its intermediacy between them. And obligation is something whose benefit is established with capacity of wealth to appear its effect in delegating and bequeathing. Know that the difference in the obligation of the will if he dies before the safety of the road; if he dies after the occurrence of safety, then there is agreement on obligation. And he pointed to the condition of the mahram or husband that the prescription [iddah] is also a condition in her right, with the prohibition of travel upon her, whatever the iddah, and the consideration for its obligation is the time of departure of the people of her town. And from Ibn Mas'ud that he returned the women in iddah from al-Najaf (a place not covered by water, elongated); if the iddah compels her during travel, it will come in its place, Allah willing. Then they differed on whether the mahram or husband is a condition of obligation or performance, just as they differed on safety of the road. Qadikhan and others declared correct that it is among the conditions of performance, while the author of al-Bada'i' and al-Saruji declared correct [that it is among] the conditions of obligation. And the practice of the author (i.e., the author of al-Lubab) indicates that it is among the conditions of performance according to the more preponderant view. His statement: (And concerning the obligation of the expense of the mahram...) He declared correct in al-Siraj the obligation, and in al-Lubab he reported the two views without preponderance, but he gave precedence to the first and said: 'It is said yes, and it is said no.' That is, it does not obligate him, nor is it obligatory upon her, as long as the mahram does not go out at his own expense, according to what al-Tahawi mentioned, and it is the statement of Abu Hafs al-Bukhari. In the Manasik of Ibn Amir Hajj: 'Is the expense of the mahram and the provision of his mount obligatory upon her? They differed about it and declared correct the non-obligation.' In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The reconciliation between the two statements is that if the mahram says, 'I will not go out except with the expense,' then it is obligatory upon her; and if he goes out without conditioning...
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the availability of a mahram or husband for a woman is a condition for the obligation of Hajj or a condition for its performance. The author first outlines the practical consequences (thamarah) of the difference: obligation to make a will, obligation to pay the mahram's expenses, and obligation to marry to obtain a mahram. If it is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub), then none of these are obligatory because a condition of obligation need not be acquired; one may refrain until the condition is met. If it is a condition of performance (shart al-ada'), then these become obligatory because the woman must remove the obstacle. The author then notes that some scholars, like Qadikhan, consider the mahram a condition of performance, while others, like the authors of al-Bada'i' and al-Saruji, consider it a condition of obligation. The author of al-Lubab leans toward the former. The passage also discusses the ruling on expenses and the reconciliation: if the mahram demands expenses, then she must provide them; otherwise, not. This reflects the Hanafi methodology of considering the maqasid (objectives) and the nature of Hajj as a mixed act of worship (financial and physical).

Key Terms
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that must be met for the obligation to be incumbent upon a person; if not met, no obligation arises.
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada'): A condition that must be fulfilled for the valid performance of the act; the obligation exists even if the condition is absent, but performance is postponed until the condition is met.
المحرم (al-mahram): A male relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., father, brother, son, husband).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi scholar(s) declared that the mahram is a condition of performance?
A) The author of al-Bada'i'
B) Qadikhan and others
C) Al-Saruji
D) Ibn Mas'ud

Key Takeaway
The classification of the mahram as a condition of obligation or performance changes whether a woman must take proactive steps to secure it for Hajj.

Ruling on Minor or Slave Entering Ihram Before Legal Responsibility
Author explains when a minor's or slave's ihram counts for obligatory Hajj and the binding nature of ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a minor's or slave's ihram suffices for obligatory Hajj after reaching legal responsibility, and explain the condition for renewal before standing at Arafah.

Core Idea
A minor's ihram is non-binding nafl; it only suffices for fard if renewed after puberty and before wuquf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical scenario: a minor or slave enters ihram for Hajj, then reaches puberty or is freed before completing the rituals. Does that Hajj count as the obligatory Hajj (Hijjat al-Islam)? The answer hinges on the binding nature of ihram and the precise timing of renewal. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly advising families and new Muslims about their Hajj obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
Recognize that the act is entering ihram. For a minor or slave before responsibility, the ihram is valid but as a nafl (supererogatory) act, not as fard. The passage states: 'it does not suffice for his obligatory [Hajj]'.
The key principle: an act of worship initiated before legal responsibility does not automatically convert to fard when responsibility arises.
2
Locate the proof: qiyas on binding nature (luzum)
The author uses a qiyas (analogy) based on the concept of luzum (bindingness). The minor's ihram is non-binding (ghayr lazim) because he is not addressed with obligations. The slave's ihram is binding (lazim) because he is a mukallaf for nafl acts. This distinction determines whether renewal is possible.
The Hanafi position relies on the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of the person. A minor lacks full capacity; a slave has capacity for nafl.
3
Apply the condition for renewal
The passage specifies that a minor can renew his ihram after puberty and intend fard, but only before standing at Arafah (wuquf). If he renews before wuquf, it suffices for fard. If he stands at Arafah without renewal, his Hajj remains nafl and cannot be changed.
There is an internal Hanafi difference on whether 'before standing' means before the actual act of standing or before the time of standing ends. The preponderant view (mufta bihi) is before the act, following Imam al-Sarakhsi.
4
Contrast with the case of the slave
The slave who is freed after entering ihram cannot renew his intention. Because his original ihram was binding (since he was mukallaf for nafl), it remains binding after emancipation. Renewal would be invalid because the original ihram continues.
This shows that the ruling is not symmetric: the minor can renew because his ihram is non-binding; the slave cannot because his is binding.
5
Extend to the disbeliever and insane person
The passage analogizes the disbeliever and insane person to the minor. If a disbeliever or insane person enters ihram and later becomes Muslim or sane, renewing ihram before wuquf suffices for fard. However, the author notes that this does not prove that a disbeliever's Hajj judges him to have become Muslim, unlike the case of salah in congregation.
The discussion also questions how an insane person can enter ihram, suggesting his guardian would do so on his behalf, though the text requires a clear transmission (naql sarih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله فلو) احرم صبي او عبد فبلغ أو عتق فمضى لم يجز عن فرضه لأن الإحرام انعقد للنفل فلا ينقلب للفرض وهو وإن كان شرطاً عندنا لكنه شبيه بالركن من حيث إمكان اتصال الأداء به فاعتبرنا الشبه فيما نحن فيه احتياطاً. وفي إسناد الإحرام إلى الصبي دليل على صحته منه وهو محمول على ما إذا كان يعقله، فإن كان لا يعقله فأحرم عنه أبوه صار محرماً

بأرض عرفة محرم بالحج النفل، ومنهم من أفتى بصحة ذلك وقد بسطت الكلام عليها في التذكرة العفيفية في فقه الحنفية ا هـ . حجه نفلاً أداء على ملخصاً من حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قوله : (وكون وليه أحرم عنه يحتاج إلى نقل صريح) قال في النهر ظاهر أن مقتضى صحة إحرام الولي عن الصبي الذي لا يعقل صحته عن المجنون بجامع عدم العقل في كل ا.هـ. وقال المقدسي في شرحه أقول : وفي البحر العميق : لا مجنون مسلم ولا يصح منه إذا حج بنفسه ولكن يحرم عنه وليه كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى ا هـ . قلت : وفي الذخيرة قال في الأصل وكل جواب عرفته في الصبي يحرم عنه الأب فهو الجواب في حج
A minor or slave entered ihram then reached puberty or was freed and continued, it does not suffice for his obligatory [Hajj]. And the mawaqit of ihram: Dhu al-Hulayfah. (Performance?) His statement: 'So if a minor or slave entered ihram then reached puberty or was freed and continued, it does not suffice for his obligatory Hajj' because the ihram was contracted for nafl and cannot change to fard, and although it is a condition with us, it resembles a rukn in that performance can be attached to it, so we considered the resemblance in this matter as a precaution. And attributing ihram to the minor indicates its validity from him, and it is understood if he understands it; if he does not understand, then his father enters ihram on his behalf and he becomes a muhrim. So he should strip him before it [tawaf?] and clothe him in an izr and rida'. And since the minor is not addressed, his ihram is non-binding, so if he is prevented and removes his ihram, there is no dam, no penalty, no making up. And if he renews it after reaching puberty before standing [at Arafah] and intends fard, it suffices him because he can exit from it due to non-bindingness, unlike the slave who cannot exit from it due to bindingness; so if he renews it after emancipation it is not valid. And the disbeliever and the insane are like the minor; so if a disbeliever or insane person performed Hajj and then became conscious and accepted Islam, and renewed it, it suffices them. It is said: This is evidence that if a disbeliever performs Hajj, it is not judged that he has become Muslim, unlike prayer in congregation. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. But there is a discussion in two aspects: first, how can an insane person enter ihram? He cannot perform ihram himself, and that his guardian entered it for him requires clear transmission that the insane adult is like the minor in this. Second, this does not indicate that if a disbeliever performs Hajj, it is not judged that he has become Muslim, because in this [case] the rituals are ambiguous, so if that were not necessary, ... (end unclear).
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a minor or slave enters ihram for Hajj and then reaches puberty or is freed before completing the rituals. The key principle: ihram entered before legal responsibility (taklif) is a nafl (supererogatory) act, not a fard (obligatory). It cannot turn into fard merely by the change in legal status. However, if the person renews their ihram (by making a new intention) after reaching puberty/freedom and before standing at Arafah, then it can count as fard Hajj (Hijjat al-Islam). This is because the minor's ihram is non-binding (ghayr lazim) – he can exit it without penalty. In contrast, a slave's ihram is binding (lazim) because the slave is mukallaf (legally responsible) for nafl, so he cannot simply exit. Thus, if a slave is freed after entering ihram, renewing the intention does not help because the original ihram still binds him. The passage also extends the analogy to a disbeliever (kafir) and an insane person (majnun). If a disbeliever enters ihram and then becomes Muslim, and renews ihram after Islam, it counts. The text notes that this does not prove that Hajj performed as a disbeliever brings no judgment of Islam, unlike salah in congregation. There is also a discussion about the meaning of 'before standing' (qabl al-wuquf): whether it means before the act of standing at Arafah or before the time of standing ends. The author favors the former view, citing Imam al-Sarakhsi. If the minor stands at Arafah even for a moment, then his Hajj is complete (as per hadith) and cannot be changed, even if he reaches puberty later. The passage ends with a note on contemporary differences in ifta' (issuing fatwas) regarding this issue.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, entered with intention and talbiyah, involving prohibitions.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory act of worship; not obligatory but rewarded.
اللزوم (al-luzum): Binding nature; once a mukallaf enters ihram for Hajj (even nafl), it becomes binding (lazim) to complete it.
الوقوف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi 'Arafah): Standing at the plain of Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; it is the greatest pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A 12-year-old boy enters ihram for Hajj. Just before standing at Arafah, he turns 13 (puberty). What should he do for his Hajj to count as fard?
A) He must renew his ihram with a new intention for fard before standing at Arafah
B) His Hajj automatically becomes fard upon reaching puberty
C) He cannot change the intention and must perform Hajj again later
D) He must exit ihram and re-enter with a new intention after Arafah

Key Takeaway
A minor's ihram is valid as nafl but does not become fard automatically upon puberty; only explicit renewal before wuquf changes it to fard.
