Minor's Ihram and the Ruling on Kafir's Hajj
Explanation of minor's ihram non-bindingness and dispute on kafir's Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a minor's ihram is non-binding and evaluate the dispute about whether a kafir's Hajj indicates Islam.

Core Idea
A minor's ihram is non-binding; a kafir's Hajj does not prove Islam without full faith and ritual completion.

This passage tackles two interconnected rulings: the legal status of a minor's ihram and the implications of a disbeliever performing Hajj. The Hanafi position distinguishes between binding (lazim) and non-binding (ghayr lazim) states, and disputes a qiyas with congregational prayer used by some scholars to claim that Hajj indicates Islam. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for proper fiqh application in Hajj and conversion scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on the minor's ihram
Recognize that the minor's ihram is valid but non-binding because the minor is not legally addressed (ghayr mukhatab). Consequently, exiting ihram due to confinement incurs no penalty.
This is the foundational principle for the entire passage.
2
Contrast with the slave's binding ihram
Note that the slave's ihram is binding; if freed during Hajj, he cannot renew it because the original remains binding. This highlights the difference between lack of legal capacity (minor) and lack of freedom (slave).
3
Extend the analogy to the disbeliever and insane
The text states that the disbeliever and insane are like the minor: their ihram is non-binding. If a disbeliever embraces Islam or an insane person regains sanity before wuquf, renewal of ihram is required.
This sets up the dispute about whether a kafir's Hajj indicates Islam.
4
Analyze the dispute: is a kafir's Hajj evidence of conversion?
Some scholars analogize Hajj to congregational prayer, arguing that performing the act indicates Islam. The Hanafi school rejects this.
The Hanafi response is based on two objections from Fath al-Qadir.
5
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal via the two objections
(1) The insane person cannot form the intention for ihram himself, so the analogy to prayer is invalid. (2) The kafir's Hajj is incomplete (lacking iman and full rituals), so it cannot serve as a reliable indicator of conversion.
These objections uphold the Hanafi position that a kafir's Hajj does not prove Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فينبغي أن يجرده قبله ويلبسه إزاراً ورداء، ولما كان الصبي غير مخاطب كان إحرامه غير لازم ولذا لو أحصر وتحلل لا دم عليه ولا جزاء ولا قضاء، ولو جدده بعد بلوغه قبل الوقوف ونوى الفرض أجزأه لأنه يمكنه الخروج عنه لعدم اللزوم بخلاف العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عنه للزوم، فلو جدده بعد عتقه لا يصح والكافر والمجنون كالصبي، فلو حج كافر أو مجنون فأفاق وأسلم فجدد الإحرام أجزأهما قيل: وهذا دليل أن الكافر إذا حج لا يحكم بإسلامه بخلاف الصلاة بجماعة. كذا في فتح القدير وفيه بحث من وجهين : الأول كيف يتصور إحرام المجنون فإنه لا يتصور منه إحرام بنفسه وكون وليه أحرم عنه يحتاج إلى نقل صريح يفيد أن المجنون البالغ كالصبي في هذا الثاني أن هذا لا يدل على أن الكافر إذا حج لا يحكم بإسلامه لأن في هذه لأن من محرم محتملة المناسك فلو ذلك لم يجب ا هـ .
So he should remove it before that and wear an izaar and a ridaa. Since the minor is not addressed, his ihram is not binding. Hence if he is confined and releases from ihram, there is no blood sacrifice, no penalty, and no making up. And if he renews it after reaching puberty before wuquf and intends the obligatory, it suffices him because he can exit it due to non-bindingness, unlike the slave who cannot exit it due to bindingness. So if he renews it after being freed, it is not valid. The disbeliever and the insane are like the minor. So if a disbeliever or an insane person performs Hajj, then regains sanity or embraces Islam, and renews the ihram, it suffices them. It is said: This is evidence that if a disbeliever performs Hajj, he is not judged to have embraced Islam, unlike prayer in congregation. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, and it contains discussion from two aspects: First, how can the insane person's ihram be imagined? For he cannot imagine an ihram by himself, and that his guardian performs ihram on his behalf requires explicit transmission that the insane adult is like the minor in this. Second, that this does not indicate that if a disbeliever performs Hajj he is not judged to have embraced Islam, because in this case the Hajj does not exist, only the ihram, and the rituals are possible; so that is not obligatory. End.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof and inter_madhhab_dispute. The author explains that a minor's ihram is not binding because he is not legally obligated (ghayr mukhatab). Therefore, if a minor performs Hajj and is confined (ihsar), he can exit ihram without penalty. If he reaches puberty before wuquf, he should renew his ihram for the obligation to count. The slave is contrasted because his ihram is binding; if freed during Hajj, he cannot renew because the original remains binding. The kafir and insane are likened to the minor. The kafir's Hajj does not make him a Muslim, unlike some opinions. The author of Fath al-Qadir raises two objections: (1) the insane person cannot form his own intention; (2) the kafir's Hajj is incomplete without faith and all rituals. Hence, the ruling that a kafir's Hajj does not indicate Islam is defended.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty; his ihram is valid but non-binding.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention and recitation of talbiyah.
غير لازم (ghayr lazim): Not binding or irrevocable; the ihram can be exited without penalty.

D) It only counts if he performed Umrah first.

Key Takeaway
A minor's ihram is non-binding, and a kafir's Hajj does not automatically indicate conversion; renewal after achieving full legal capacity or faith before wuquf is essential.

Woman's Obligation to Marry for Hajj: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on a woman's duty to marry to secure a mahram for Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a woman must marry to perform Hajj and identify the basis for this ruling within the school.

Core Idea
A woman is not obligated to marry to perform Hajj, even if she has no mahram.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific question: if a woman is financially able but lacks a male guardian (mahram), must she marry to fulfill the Hajj obligation? The text affirms that she is not required to do so, citing earlier authorities. We will examine the ruling and the intra-Hanafi discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the exact question: Is marriage obligatory for a woman without a mahram to perform Hajj?
2
State the majority Hanafi position
The text clearly states that it is not obligatory, citing al-Lubab, al-Bada'i', Qadikhan, and a transmission from Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify the sources
Note the chain: al-Lubab -> al-Bada'i' and Qadikhan -> Ibn Shuja' from Abu Hanifa. This supports the non-obligation view.
4
Acknowledge the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars may have held a differing view, but the passage emphasizes the position of the early authorities.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that marriage is not obligatory; this is the view that should be followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي وجوب التزوج عليها الخ جزم في اللباب بأنه لا يجب عليها أن تتزوج بمن يحج بها وعزاه شارحه إلى البدائع وقاضيخان وغيرهما ثم قال : وعن ابن شجاع عن أبي حنيفة أن لا الها يجب عليها أن تتزوج زوجاً يحج بها إذا كانت موسرة ا هـ .
His statement: (And regarding the obligation of marriage upon her, etc.) It is firmly stated in al-Lubab that it is not obligatory for her to marry someone who can perform Hajj with her, and its commentator attributed it to al-Bada'i', Qadikhan, and others. Then he said: And from Ibn Shuja' from Abu Hanifa that it is not obligatory for her to marry a husband who can perform Hajj with her if she is wealthy. End.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a woman who is financially able but lacks a mahram. The majority view in the Hanafi school (from al-Lubab, al-Bada'i', Qadikhan) is that she is not obligated to marry to perform Hajj. The same is transmitted from Ibn Shuja' from Abu Hanifa. This means she may postpone Hajj until she secures a mahram through other means. The opposing view (not mentioned here) might require her to marry if possible. The relied-upon view is the one cited.

Key Terms
وجوب التزوج (wujub al-tazawwuj): The obligation of marriage to secure a mahram for Hajj.
موسرة (musirah): Wealthy; having financial ability to perform Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if she has no other means

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a woman is not obligated to marry to perform Hajj, even if she has the financial means but no mahram.

Renewal of Ihram After Puberty: Timing and Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on renewal timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the timing of a minor's ihram renewal after puberty and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of 'before wuquf'.

Core Idea
Renewal of ihram must occur before the act of wuquf; once wuquf has occurred, the Hajj is complete and cannot be converted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a nuanced issue in Hajj jurisprudence: a minor who enters ihram before puberty and then attains puberty before completing the rituals. The central question is whether he can renew his ihram to transform his voluntary Hajj into the obligatory Hajj, and crucially, the timing of that renewal. The key phrase 'before wuquf' is interpreted by Imam al-Sarakhsi as before the act of standing at Arafah, a view supported by a general hadith, while later Hanafi scholars debated whether it could be before the time of wuquf ends. We will unpack this dispute, its evidence, and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations of 'before wuquf'
The text states that 'before wuquf' can mean either before the act of standing at Arafah or before the time of wuquf (i.e., before the day of Arafah ends). Note which scholars adopted each view.
Mulla Ali followed the second interpretation; al-Sarakhsi and the author support the first.
2
Analyze al-Sarakhsi's evidence and the hadith
Al-Sarakhsi's ruling from al-Mabsut requires renewal before standing. The hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah for an hour... has completed his Hajj' is cited to support that once wuquf occurs, the Hajj is complete and cannot be altered. The general word 'whoever' includes minors.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but used for istidlal.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute and its practical outcome
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Qadi Muhammad 'Id and Shaykh 'Abdullah al-'Afif) recorded a difference in fatwa: some held that renewal after the time of wuquf has entered but before standing is invalid; others permitted it. The author notes the dispute without fully resolving it, but the majority view (mufta bihi) from the reliable sources is that renewal must be before actual wuquf.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a minor who becomes pubescent after standing cannot have his Hajj count as fard, whereas if he renews before standing, it suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو جدده بعد بلوغه قبل الوقوف الخ) كذا عبارة أغلب كتب المذهب بصيغة «قبل الوقوف» وهي يراد قبل أن يقف أو قبل فوات وقت الوقوف، وعلى الثاني مشى منلا علي في شرح وشرح النقاية، ويؤيد الأول قول الإمام السرخسي في مبسوطه في آخر باب المواقيت: ولو أن الصبي أهل بالحج قبل أن يحتلم ثم احتلم قبل أن يطوف بالبيت أو قبل أن يقف بعرفة لم يجزه عن حجة الإسلام عندنا إلا أن يجدد إحرامه قبل أن يقف بعرفة فحينئذ يجزئه عن حجة الإسلام ا هـ. وقف بعد الزوال ولو لحظة ثم بلغ ليس بله التجديد وإن بقي وقت الوقوف لتمام حجه إذ الحج بعد التمام لا يقبل النقض ولا يصح أداء حجتين في عام واحد بالإجماع. كذا ذكره القاضي محمد عيد في شرحه خلاصة الناسك على لباب المناسك المختصر من شرحه الكبير عباب المسالك عن شيخه العلامة الشيخ حسن العجيمي. وذكر مثله الشيخ عبد الله العفيف في شرح منسكه مستدلاً بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من وقف بعرفة ساعة من ليل أو نهار فقد تم حجة فمن من صيغ العموم فيشمل الصبي وقد قلنا بأن صحيح. ويمتنع حجتين نفل وفرض في سنة واحدة ثم قال : وقد وقع الاختلاف في الإفتاء في هذه المسألة في زماننا، فمن العصريين من أفتى بعدم صحة تجديد الصبي الإحرام بعد أن دخل عليه وقت الوقوف وهو بأرض عرفة محرم بالحج النفل، ومنهم من أفتى بصحة ذلك وقد بسطت الكلام عليها في التذكرة العفيفية في فقه الحنفية ا هـ . حجه نفلاً أداء على ملخصاً من حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قوله : (وكون وليه أحرم عنه يحتاج إلى نقل صريح) قال في النهر ظاهر أن مقتضى صحة إحرام الولي عن الصبي الذي لا يعقل صحته عن المجنون بجامع عدم العقل في كل ا.هـ. وقال المقدسي في شرحه أقول : وفي البحر العميق : لا مجنون مسلم ولا يصح منه إذا حج بنفسه ولكن يحرم عنه وليه كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى ا هـ . قلت : وفي الذخيرة قال في الأصل وكل جواب عرفته في الصبي يحرم عنه الأب فهو الجواب في حج المجنون | هـ. المناسك ويرمي وفي الولوالجية قبيل الإحصار وكذا الصبي يحج به أبوه، وكذا المجنون يقضي الجمار لأن إحرام الأب عنهما وهما عاجزان كإحرامهما بنفسهما ا هـ. فهذه النقول صريحة في أن المجنون كالصبي قوله: (فالحاصل أنه لا يكون مسلماً الخ) قال في النهر : جزمه بإسلامه إذا أتى بسائر الأفعال ضعيف كما مر
His statement: (And if he renews it after puberty before wuquf, etc.) Thus is the expression of most books of the school with the wording 'before wuquf'. It intends either before he stands [at Arafah] or before the time of wuquf passes. The second is followed by Mulla Ali in his commentary and the commentary of al-Nuqayah. The first is supported by the statement of Imam al-Sarakhsi in his Mabsut at the end of the chapter on Mawaqit: 'If a minor enters the state of ihram for Hajj before becoming pubescent, then becomes pubescent before circumambulating the House or before standing at Arafah, it does not suffice him for the obligatory Hajj in our view until he renews his ihram before standing at Arafah. Then it suffices him for the obligatory Hajj.' End. If he stands [at Arafah] after midday even for a moment, then becomes pubescent, he cannot renew, even if the time of wuquf remains, because his Hajj is complete, and once complete it cannot be voided, and it is not permissible to perform two Hajjs, one voluntary and one obligatory, in one year by consensus. This is as mentioned by al-Qadi Muhammad 'Id in his commentary 'Khalasat al-Nasik' on 'Lubab al-Manasik', abridged from his large commentary 'Ubab al-Masalik' from his teacher 'Allamah Shaykh Hasan al-'Ujaimi. Likewise, Shaykh 'Abdullah al-'Afif mentioned in his commentary on his own Manasik, using as proof the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH): 'Whoever stands at Arafah for an hour of the night or day has completed his Hajj.' The phrase 'whoever' is general, including the minor, and we have said that it is valid. And it is forbidden to perform two Hajjs, voluntary and obligatory, in one year. Then he said: There is a difference of opinion in fatwa on this issue in our time. Some later scholars gave a fatwa against the validity of the minor renewing ihram after the time of wuquf has entered while he is in the land of Arafah in the state of ihram for voluntary Hajj. Others gave a fatwa for its validity. I have discussed it at length in 'al-Tadhkirah al-'Afifiyyah fi Fiqh al-Hanafiyyah'. End. [..] His statement on the guardian performing ihram on his behalf requires explicit transmission. He said in al-Nahr: It is apparent that the requirement for the validity of the guardian's ihram for a minor who lacks reason is also valid for the insane, due to the shared cause of lack of reason. End. Al-Maqdisi said in his commentary: I say, in al-Bahr al-'Amiq: There is no insane Muslim, and it is not valid for him if he performs Hajj by himself, but his guardian performs ihram for him, as will come, if Allah wills. End. I say: In al-Dhakhirah, it is said in al-Asl: Every answer you know regarding the minor—the father performs ihram for him—is the answer regarding the Hajj of the insane. And in al-Walwalijiyyah, before the section on ihsar, it is said: Also the minor—his father performs Hajj with him, and also the insane—he performs the stoning because the father's ihram for both while they are incapable is like their own ihram. End. Thus these clear texts indicate that the insane is like the minor. His statement: (The conclusion is that he is not a Muslim, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: His assertion that he becomes Muslim if he performs the other actions is weak, as passed.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passages discusses the timing of renewal of ihram for a minor after puberty. The key point is whether 'before wuquf' means before the act of standing or before the time of standing ends. Mulla Ali interprets it as before the time ends, but al-Sarakhsi's statement from al-Mabsut supports the first interpretation: renewal must occur before standing (wuquf) itself. If the minor stands at Arafah even for a moment before puberty, his Hajj is complete and cannot be renewed. Later scholars differed on whether renewal after the time of wuquf has begun is valid. The author cites the hadith from 'Abdullah al-'Afif that whoever stands at Arafah for any time has completed Hajj, which includes minors. The passage then discusses the validity of a guardian performing ihram for a minor and an insane person, confirming that both are similar in that the guardian may act on their behalf.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): Standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; a pillar of Hajj.
التجديد (al-tajdid): Renewing the ihram with a new intention after puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, what is the latest time a minor can renew his ihram for his Hajj to count as obligatory?
A) Before the day of Arafah ends
B) Before he stands at Arafah (wuquf)
C) Before the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah
D) Before he completes tawaf

Key Takeaway
A minor's Hajj can only become obligatory if he renews his ihram after puberty before the actual standing at Arafah; once wuquf occurs, the Hajj is complete and cannot be converted.

The Five Mawaqit (Places of Ihram)
Enumeration and description of the five mawaqit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five mawaqit and explain the rule of assuming ihram for the afaqi.

Core Idea
An afaqi must assume ihram before crossing the miqat; the five locations are fixed by the Prophet ﷺ.

In this lesson, we examine the five designated places (mawaqit) where a pilgrim must enter the state of ihram before proceeding to Makkah. This ruling is based on the sunnah and is universally accepted across the madhabs. Understanding these locations is fundamental for anyone performing Hajj or Umrah from outside the Haram region.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Recognize that the author (al-Kanz) states the mawaqit as a ruling: it is obligatory (wajib) for the afaqi to assume ihram at these points.
The ruling is from the sunnah; crossing without ihram requires a dam (penalty).
2
List the five mawaqit
Memorize the five names: Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam. Note which regions each serves.
Dhul-Hulayfah is for Madinah; Dhat 'Irq for the east; al-Juhfah for Egypt, Sham, and Maghrib; Qarn for Najd; Yalamlam for Yemen.
3
Understand the geographical context
Note the distances given in the text (e.g., Dhul-Hulayfah is about 10 marhalas from Makkah). This helps in practical application.
Distances vary slightly between authorities but are not legally binding.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a pilgrim from a specific region, determine the correct miqat and the consequence of missing it.
The rule applies to Hajj and Umrah equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ومواقيت الإحرام ذو الحليفة وذات عرق والحجفة وقرن ويلملم لأهلها ولمن مربها وصح تقديمه عليها لا عكسه . أي الأمكنة التي لا يتجاوزها الآفاقي إلا محرما خمسة، فالميقات مشترك بين الوقت المعين والمكان المعين والمراد هنا الثاني وسيأتي الأول. وذو الحليفة - بضم الحاء المهملة وبالفاء - بينه وبين . نحو عشر مراحل أو تسع، وبينه وبين المدينة ستة أميال كما ذكره النووي، وقيل سبعة كما ذره الفياض عياض، ميقات أهل المدينة وهو أبعد المواقيت وبهذا المكان آبار تسميه العوام آبار علي قيل لأن علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه قاتل الجن في بعض تلك الآبار وهو كذب من قائله كما ذكره الحلبي في مناسكه. وذات عرق بكسر العين وسكون الراء لجميع أهل المشرق وهي بين المشرق والمغرب من مكة، قيل وبينها وبين مكة مرحلتان. والجحفة بضم الجيم وسكون الحاء المهملة واسمها في الأصل مهيعة نزل بها سيل جحف أهلها أي استأصلهم فسميت جحفة . قال النووي : بينها وبين مكة ثلاث مراحل وهي قرية بين المغرب والشمال من مكة من طريق تبوك وهي طريق أهل الشام ونواحيها اليوم وهي ميقات أهل مصر والمغرب والشأم . وقَرْن بفتح القاف وسكون الراء وهو جبل مطل على عرفات بينه وبين مكة نحو مرحلتين. وفي الصحاح إنه بفتح الراء وإن أو يساً القرني منسوب إليه ورد بأنه بسكون الراء وأن أو يسا منسوب إلى قبيلة يقال لها بنو قرن بطن من مراد وهو ميقات أهل نجد. وأما يلملم
His statement: (And the mawaqit of ihram are Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam, for their residents and for those who pass by, and it is correct to advance it to them, not the opposite.) That is, the places which one coming from a distance may not cross except in ihram; they are five. Al-Miqat is shared between the specific time and the specific place, and the meaning here is the second, and the first will come. Dhul-Hulayfah - with a damma on the ha and a fa - between it and [Makkah] about ten or nine marhalas, and between it and Madinah is six miles as mentioned by al-Nawawi, and it is said seven miles as mentioned by al-Fayyad al-'Iyad. It is the miqat of the people of Madinah, and it is the farthest of the mawaqit. At this place there are wells that the common people call 'Wells of 'Ali', it is said because 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA) fought the jinn in some of those wells, and this is a lie from its narrator, as al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik. Dhat 'Irq - with a kasra on the 'ayn and sukun on the ra - is for all the people of the east, and it lies between the east and west of Makkah. It is said that between it and Makkah is two marhalas. Al-Juhfah - with a damm on the jim and sukun on the ha - its original name is Mahya'ah; a flood came and jahafa its people, i.e., uprooted them, so it was named Juhfah. Al-Nawawi said: Between it and Makkah is three marhalas, and it is a village between the west and north of Makkah on the road to Tabuk, and it is the road of the people of Sham and its regions today, and it is the miqat of the people of Egypt, the Maghrib, and Sham. Qarn - with a fatha on the qaf and sukun on the ra - is a mountain overlooking 'Arafat, between it and Makkah about two marhalas. In al-Sihah, it is said with a fatha on the ra, and that Aws al-Qarani is attributed to it. It is refuted that it is with sukun on the ra, and that Aws is attributed to a tribe called Banu Qarn, a branch of Murad, and it is the miqat of the people of Najd. And as for Yalamlam...
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement defining the five mawaqit (places of ihram) for Hajj and Umrah. The mawaqit are Dhul-Hulayfah (for Madinah), Dhat 'Irq (for the east), al-Juhfah (for Egypt, Maghrib, and Sham), Qarn (for Najd), and Yalamlam (for Yemen). The passage explains each location's distance and etymology. It also clarifies that mawaqit can mean either the time (mawaqit al-zaman) or the place (mawaqit al-makan); here it means the places. The rule is that anyone coming from beyond these places must assume ihram before crossing them, and it is permissible to assume ihram earlier but not later.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-miqat): The fixed place (or time) for entering the state of ihram; here it means place.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person coming from outside the mawaqit, i.e., not a resident of the mawaqit or the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pilgrim from Egypt is flying to Jeddah for Hajj. Which miqat must he assume ihram at?
A) Dhul-Hulayfah
B) Dhat 'Irq
C) al-Juhfah
D) Yalamlam

Key Takeaway
An afaqi must assume ihram before crossing his designated miqat; the five mawaqit are fixed by the sunnah and universally accepted.

The Five Mawaqit of Ihram: Locations and Rulings
Commentary defining the five mawaqit of ihram with locations and hadith sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five mawaqit of ihram, identify their geographical locations, and explain the obligation to perform ihram before crossing them.

Core Idea
The five mawaqit are fixed places where a pilgrim must enter ihram; passing beyond them without ihram is prohibited.

Before reaching Makkah, pilgrims must enter a state of ihram at designated points. The Prophet ﷺ fixed five such places for different regions. This lesson explores these mawaqit, their locations, the ruling for crossing them, and the textual basis from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five mawaqit
List the five places mentioned in the matn: Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam.
Each serves a different region of the Muslim world.
2
Locate each miqat geographically
From the commentary, note the distances from Makkah and the direction. For example, Dhul-Hulayfah is about 10 stages from Makkah, near Madinah.
Know relative positions for practical application.
3
Determine who each miqat serves
Identify the regions: Dhul-Hulayfah for Madinah, Dhat 'Irq for the east, al-Juhfah for Egypt/Maghrib/Sham, Qarn for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen.
Also for anyone who passes by, even if not from that region.
4
Understand the obligation
The hadiths (in Sahihain and others) command entering ihram before these points. Hanafi: it is haram to pass without ihram; a dam is required if violated.
Shafi'i holds one must enter ihram at the first miqat encountered.
5
Note the linguistic clarification
The commentator explains that 'miqat' here means place, not time, though the word can be used for both.
This prevents confusion with the time-based mawaqit of hajj.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
وذات عرق الحجفة وقرن ويلملم لأهلها ولمن مربها وصح تقديمه عليها لا عكسه
المسألة لم يوجد الحج منه إنما وجد الإحرام فقط لأنه لو وقف بعرفة لم يكن موضوع المسألة ولم يكن للتجديد فائدة، فالحاصل أنه لا يكون مسلماً إلا بالإحرام والوقوف وشهود المناسك فلا منافاة بين الفرعين كما لا يخفى. وفي الذخيرة عن النوادر البالغ إذا جن بعد الإحرام ثم ارتكب شيئاً من محظورات الإحرام فإن فيه الكفارة فرقاً بينه وبين الصبي .
:
مكة
قوله (ومواقيت الإحرام ذو الحليفة وذات عرق والحجفة وقرن ويلملم لأهلها ولمن مربها أي الأمكنة التي لا يتجاوزها الآفاقي إلا محرما خمسة، فالميقات مشترك بين الوقت المعين والمكان المعين والمراد هنا الثاني وسيأتي الأول. وذو الحليفة - بضم الحاء المهملة وبالفاء - بينه وبين [؟] نحو عشر مراحل أو تسع، وبينه وبين المدينة ستة أميال كما ذكره النووي، وقيل سبعة كما ذره الفياض عياض، ميقات أهل المدينة وهو أبعد المواقيت وبهذا المكان آبار تسميه العوام آبار علي قيل لأن علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه قاتل الجن في بعض تلك الآبار وهو كذب من قائله كما ذكره الحلبي في مناسكه. وذات عرق بكسر العين وسكون الراء لجميع أهل المشرق وهي بين المشرق والمغرب من مكة، قيل وبينها وبين مكة مرحلتان. والجحفة بضم الجيم وسكون الحاء المهملة واسمها في الأصل مهيعة نزل بها سيل جحف أهلها أي استأصلهم فسميت جحفة . قال النووي : بينها وبين مكة ثلاث مراحل وهي قرية بين المغرب والشمال من مكة من طريق تبوك وهي طريق أهل الشام ونواحيها اليوم وهي ميقات أهل مصر والمغرب والشأم . وقَرْن بفتح القاف وسكون الراء وهو جبل مطل على عرفات بينه وبين مكة نحو مرحلتين. وفي الصحاح إنه بفتح الراء وإن أو يساً القرني منسوب إليه ورد بأنه بسكون الراء وأن أو يسا منسوب إلى قبيلة يقال لها بنو قرن بطن من مراد وهو ميقات أهل نجد. وأما يلملم
المجنون | هـ.
المناسك
ويرمي
وفي الولوالجية قبيل الإحصار وكذا الصبي يحج به أبوه، وكذا المجنون يقضي الجمار لأن إحرام الأب عنهما وهما عاجزان كإحرامهما بنفسهما ا هـ. فهذه النقول صريحة في أن المجنون كالصبي قوله: (فالحاصل أنه لا يكون مسلماً الخ) قال في النهر : جزمه بإسلامه إذا أتى بسائر الأفعال ضعيف كما مر قوله : فالميقات مشترك (الخ) قال في النهر : المواقيت جمع ميقات بمعنى الوقت المحدود استعير للمكان أعني مكان الإحرام كما استعير المكان للوقت في قوله تعالى هنالك ابتلى المؤمنون ﴾ [الأحزاب: ۳۳] قال بعض المتأخرين: ومنه قولهم ووقته البستان» وهو سهو ظاهر إذ المعنى كما في المغرب وغيره ميقاته بستان بني عامر، ولا ينافيه قول الجوهري «الميقات موضع الإحرام لأنه ليس من رأيه التفرقة بين الحقيقة والمجاز وكأنه في البحر استند إلى ظاهر ما في الاصحاح فزعم أنه مشترك بين الوقت والمكان المعين والمراد هنا الثاني، وأعرض عن كلامهم السابق وقد علمت ما هو الواقع قوله : (الحلبي) أي العلامة محمد ابن أمير حاج الحلبي تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام وشارح تحريره الأصولي وشارح منية المصلي، وهو أقدم من الحلبي صاحب
فهو ميقات أهل اليمن وهو مكان جنوبي مكة وهو جبل من جبال تهامة على مرحلتين من مكة . فهذا هو المراد بقوله «لأهلها وهذه المواقيت ما عدا ذات عرق ثابتة في الصحيحين وذات عرق في صحيح مسلم وسنن أبي داود
Book of Hajj. And Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam are for their people and for whoever passes by them, and it is valid to precede it over them, not the opposite. The issue: he has not performed hajj from it; rather he has only performed ihram, because if he stood at Arafah it would not be the subject of the issue and there would be no benefit in renewal. So the conclusion is that he is not a Muslim except with ihram, standing, and witnessing the rituals; there is no conflict between the two branches as is not hidden. And in al-Dhakhira from al-Nawadir: an adult who becomes insane after ihram then commits something from the prohibitions of ihram, then upon him is expiation, distinguishing between him and a child. (Then a colon and 'Makkah'.) He said (the author's statement): 'And the mawaqit of ihram: Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam for their people and for whoever passes by them' meaning the places that the afaqi (pilgrim from outside the miqat) must not pass beyond except in ihram; there are five. So al-miqat is shared between the specific time and the specific place; the second is intended here, and the first will come. And Dhul-Hulayfah (with dhammah on the ha' and with fa') - between it and [something] about ten or nine stages, and between it and Madinah six miles as mentioned by al-Nawawi, and it is said seven miles as mentioned by al-Fayyad 'Iyad. It is the miqat of the people of Madinah, and it is the furthest of the mawaqit. In this place there are wells that the common people call the wells of 'Ali, it is said because 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) fought the jinn in some of those wells, but this is a lie from its speaker as mentioned by al-Halabi in his Manasik. And Dhat 'Irq (with kasrah on the 'ayn and sukun on the ra') for all the people of the east, and it is between the east and the west of Makkah; it is said between it and Makkah is two stages. And al-Juhfah (with dammah on the jim and sukun on the ha') - its original name is Muhayyi'ah, a flood came that swept away its people, so it was named Juhfah. Al-Nawawi said: between it and Makkah is three stages, and it is a village between the west and north of Makkah on the road to Tabuk, which is the road of the people of Sham and its regions today, and it is the miqat of the people of Egypt, the Maghrib, and Sham. And Qarn (with fatha on the qaf and sukun on the ra') - it is a mountain overlooking Arafat, between it and Makkah about two stages. And in al-Sihah it is said that it is with fatha on the ra', and that Uways al-Qarani is attributed to it; it was refuted that it is with sukun on the ra' and that Uways is attributed to a tribe called Banu Qarn, a branch of Murad, and it is the miqat of the people of Najd. As for Yalamlam... (then inserts) the insane; the rituals; and he throws; and in al-Walwaljiyya, before ihsar, likewise the child performs hajj with his father, and likewise the insane person performs the stoning because the father's ihram for them both, while they are incapable, is like their own ihram, end quote. So these quotations are explicit that the insane person is like a child. (He said:) The conclusion is that he is not a Muslim... Al-Nahr said: His affirmation of his Islam if he performs the other actions is weak as previously. (He said:) So 'al-miqat' is shared... Al-Nahr said: 'al-mawaqit' is plural of miqat meaning the defined time; it is metaphorically used for place, meaning the place of ihram, just as place is metaphorically used for time in His statement 'there the believers were tested' [al-Ahzab 33]. Some later scholars said: from this is their statement 'and its time is the garden' but this is an obvious oversight, because the meaning, as in al-Mughrib and others, is 'its miqat is the garden of Bani 'Amir', and it is not contradicted by al-Jawhari's statement 'al-miqat is the place of ihram' because it is not his opinion to distinguish between literal and metaphorical. It is as if the author of al-Bahr relied on the apparent meaning of al-Sihah and claimed it is shared between time and the specific place, and the second is intended here, and he turned away from their previous speech, and you have known what is the reality. (He said:) Al-Halabi meaning the scholar Muhammad ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, student of the investigator Ibn al-Humam, commentator of his Usul work Tahrir and commentator of Munyat al-Musalli, and he is earlier than the Halabi who authored... Then (from next page): He is the miqat of the people of Yemen, and it is a place south of Makkah, a mountain of the mountains of Tihamah, two stages from Makkah. So this is what is meant by his statement 'for its people'. And these mawaqit, except Dhat 'Irq, are confirmed in the two Sahihs, and Dhat 'Irq is in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling and expansion probe from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by quoting the matn listing the five mawaqit (fixed places for ihram) and then provides their precise geographical locations, distances from Makkah, and for whom each is designated. The commentator also clarifies that the term 'miqat' can refer to both a time and a place, but here it means place. He identifies Dhul-Hulayfah as the miqat for Madinah (the furthest), Dhat 'Irq for the eastern region, al-Juhfah for Egypt and the Maghrib, Qarn for Najd, and Yalamlam for Yemen. He notes that the mawaqit (except Dhat 'Irq) are established in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim, while Dhat 'Irq is in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud. The passage also includes digressions: a ruling from al-Dhakhira about an adult who becomes insane after ihram and commits a prohibited act—such a person must pay expiation, unlike a child; and a later comment from al-Walwaljiyya that a child and an insane person perform hajj with the father's ihram and must perform the stoning themselves. The commentator concludes that these quotations show the insane person is like a child in these rulings. Additionally, he discusses the linguistic meaning of 'miqat' as a metaphor for place, refuting a claim about the phrase 'its time is the garden'. The primary focus remains the five mawaqit, their locations, and the obligatory ruling that one must not pass them without ihram.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): A fixed place (or time) for entering ihram. In this passage, it refers specifically to the five designated locations beyond which a pilgrim from outside the miqat must perform ihram.
آفاقي (afaqi): A pilgrim who lives outside the miqat zone and must perform ihram before crossing any of the five mawaqit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The five mawaqit are fixed places prescribed by the Prophet ﷺ; an afaqi must perform ihram before crossing any of them, and violation incurs a penalty (dam).

Ruling for a Madani: May He Delay Ihram to al-Juhfah?
Inter-madhhab dispute on a Madani's ihram timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Madani delaying ihram and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For a Madani, delaying ihram to al-Juhfah is permissible but disliked; no dam required, contrary to Shafi'i.

The miqat for Madinah is Dhul-Hulayfah, but what if a Madani wishes to delay his ihram to al-Juhfah? Is this permissible or even superior? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the Hanafi position, the intra-madhhab differences, and the contrast with Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this ruling helps pilgrims navigate competing considerations of obedience to the sunnah and practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine who is the 'Madani' (resident of Madinah) and exactly what action is being ruled upon: passing Dhul-Hulayfah without ihram to perform ihram at al-Juhfah.
The Madani has his own miqat; others passing through are treated differently.
2
Locate the Hanafi position and the conflicting view
From the passage, extract the Hanafi view that it is not obligatory to perform ihram from the first miqat, and note the opposing view from Ibn Amir Haj and the Shafi'i school.
Mulla 'Ali al-Qari states it is makruh; the text reconciles by considering circumstances.
3
Compare the proofs (dalil)
Identify the hadith evidence: the Prophet's designation of mawaqit and the practice of companions. Note the Hanafi argument that the hadith does not forbid passing the first miqat.
Shafi'i relies on the apparent implication of the hadith that each miqat is for its people and those who pass it.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'i requires a dam (sacrifice) if the first miqat is bypassed; Hanafi does not, though it considers the act makruh.
This difference affects the pilgrim's liability and the ruling if they proceed.
5
Understand the nuance about 'afdal' vs 'makruh'
The passage shows that what is 'afdal' can change based on context: if delaying helps avoid prohibitions, it may be superior; otherwise, the first miqat is recommended.
This reconciles the two narrations from Abu Hanifah.

وقوله ولمن مربها يعني من غير أهلها وقد أفاد أنه لا يجوز مجاوزة الجميع إلا محرماً فلا يجب على المدني أن يحرم من ميقاته وإن كان هو الأفضل وإنما يجب عليه أن يحرم من آخرها عندنا ويعلم منه أن الشامي إذا مر على ذي الحليفة في ذهابه لا يلزمه الإحرام منه بالطريق الأولى وإنما يجب عليه أن يحرم من الجحفة كالمصري لكن قيل أن الجحفا قد ذهبت أعلامها ولم يبق بها إلا رسوم خفية لا يكاد يعرفها إلا سكان بعض البوادي. ولهذ والله أعلم اختار الناس الإحرام من المكان المسمى برابض، وبعضهم يجعله بالغين احتياطاً لأن قبل الجحفة بنصف مرحلة أو قريب من ذلك وقد قالوا : ومن كان في بر أو بحر لا يمر بواحا هذه المواقيت المذكورة فعليه أن يحرم إذا حاذى آخرها ويعرف بالاجتهاد وعليه أن يجتهد من : الملتقى وشارح المنية أيضاً واسمه ابراهيم قوله : ( وإن كان هو الأفضل ذكر منلا علي القاري في شرح اللباب أنه يكره وفاقاً بين علمائنا خلافاً لابن أمير حاج حيث قال : هو الأفضل ا هـ. أي الأفضل تأخير المدني إحرامه إلى الجحفة. وعبارة متن اللباب والمدني إذا جاوز وقته غير محرم كره وفي لزو[؟] خلاف وصحح سقوطه ا هـ . وقال شارحه ولعله أشار إلى ما في النخبة أن من كان في طريق ميقاتان لا يجوز أن يتعدى إلى الثاني على الأصح فالدم يكون متفرعاً على القول المقابل للأصح لكز[؟] الأظهر أن يقال : وصحح عدم وجوبه لأن من في طريقه ميقاتان مخير في أن يحرم من الأول وهو الأفضل عند الجمهور خروجاً عن الخلاف فإنه متعين عند الشافعي، أو يحرم من الثاني فإنه رخصة له. وقيل: إنه أفضل بالنسبة إلى أكثر أرباب النسك فإنهم إذا أحرموا من الميقات الأول ارتكبوا كثيراً من المحظورات بعذر وبغيره قبل وصولهم إلى الميقات الثاني فيكون الأفضل في حقهم التأخير، وهذا لا ينافي ما في البدائع من جاوز ميقاتاً من هذه المواقيت من غير إحرام إلى ميقات آخر جاز إلا أن المستحب أن يحرم من الميقات الأول. كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال في غير أهل المدينة إذا مروا على المدينة فجاوزوها إلى الجحفة فلا بأس بذلك وأحب إلي أن يحرموا من ذي الحليفة لأنهم لما وصلوا إلى الميقات الأول لزمهم محافظة حرمته فيكره لهم تركها ا هـ . ومثله ذكره القدوري في شرحه وبه قال عطاء وبعض المالكية والحنابلة ووجه عدم التنافي أن حكم الاستحباب المذكور ونظراً إلى الأحوط خروجاً عن الخلاف وللمسارعة والمبادرة إلى الطاعة، وأن قوله الأفضل التأخير» بناء على فساد الزمان ومكاثرة مباشرة ،العصيان ومثله قولهم التقديم على الميقات أفضل حتى السلف : من إتمام الحج الإحرام من دويرة أهله لكنه مقيد بمن يكون مأموناً عن الوقوع في محظورات إحرامه إلا أن في قول أبي حنيفة في غير أهل المدينة إشارة إلى أن أهل المدينة ليس لهم أن يجاوزوا عن ميقاتهم المعين لهم على لسان الشرع وبه يجمع بين الروايتين المختلفتين عن أبي حنيفة، فعنه أنه لو لم يحرم من ذي الحليفة وأحرم من الجحفة أن عليه دماً وبه قال مالك والشافعي قال بعض
And his statement 'and for whoever passes by them' means whoever is not from its people, and it indicates that it is not permissible to pass beyond any of them except in ihram. So it is not obligatory for the Madani to perform ihram from his own miqat, although it is superior; rather, he must perform ihram from the last of them according to us. And it is understood from this that a Syrian, if he passes by Dhul-Hulayfah on his way, is not required to perform ihram from it, a fortiori; rather, he must perform ihram from al-Juhfah like an Egyptian. But it is said that the landmarks of al-Juhfah have disappeared, and nothing remains but faint traces that hardly anyone knows except some desert dwellers. Therefore, Allah knows best, people have chosen to perform ihram from the place called Rabidh, and some of them place it as al-Ghayn (؟) as a precaution, because it is half a stage before al-Juhfah or close to that. And they said: Whoever is on land or sea and does not pass by any of these mentioned mawaqit, then he must perform ihram when he comes opposite the last of them, and it is known by ijtihad, and he must exert himself. (From) al-Multaqa and the commentator of al-Munyah also, and his name is Ibrahim. His statement: 'And although he said it is superior' – Mulla 'Ali al-Qari mentioned in Sharh al-Lubab that it is disliked, in agreement among our scholars, contrary to Ibn Amir Haj who said it is superior. That is, it is superior for the Madani to delay his ihram to al-Juhfah. The text of al-Lubab: 'And the Madani, if he passes his time without ihram, it is disliked, and there is a difference of opinion regarding its obligation, and he corrected that it is not obligatory.' His commentator said: Perhaps he referred to what is in al-Nukhbah that a person who has two mawaqit on his way is not permitted to go beyond the second on the strongest opinion; then the blood (offering) is a consequence of the opinion opposite to the strongest. But it seems the most apparent is to say: He corrected that it is not obligatory because a person on whose route there are two mawaqit has a choice: to perform ihram from the first, which is superior according to the majority, to exit from the disagreement, for it is obligatory according to al-Shafi'i, or to perform ihram from the second, as a concession for him. And it is said: It is superior with respect to most pilgrims because if they perform ihram from the first miqat, they commit many of the prohibitions with and without excuse before reaching the second miqat; so in their case, delaying is superior. And this does not contradict what is in al-Bada'i: 'Whoever passes one of these mawaqit without ihram to another miqat, it is permissible, except that it is recommended to perform ihram from the first miqat.' Thus it is reported from Abu Hanifah that he said regarding non-Madani if they pass by Madinah and then go beyond it to al-Juhfah, there is no harm in that, but I prefer that they perform ihram from Dhul-Hulayfah, because when they reach the first miqat, the obligation to observe its sanctity is established, so it is disliked for them to leave it, end quote. And similar was mentioned by al-Quduri in his commentary, and 'Ata'' and some of the Malikis and Hanbalis said it. And the aspect of non-contradiction is that the rule of recommendation mentioned is with a view to caution to exit the disagreement and for haste and promptness to obedience, and that his statement that 'delaying is superior' is based on corruption of time and frequency of committing disobedience. Similar to their statement: 'Preceding the miqat is superior,' even the predecessors said: 'Part of completing hajj is ihram from the abode of his family,' but this is restricted to one who is safe from falling into the prohibitions of his ihram. However, in the statement of Abu Hanifah regarding non-Madani, there is an indication that the people of Madinah may not go beyond their specific miqat designated for them by the tongue of Shariah, and by this the two differing reports from Abu Hanifah are reconciled; for it is reported from him that if he did not perform ihram from Dhul-Hulayfah and performed ihram from al-Juhfah, then upon him is blood, and this is also the view of Malik and al-Shafi'i. Some...
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute from the commentary. It addresses the ruling for a Madani (a person from Madinah) regarding whether he must perform ihram from his own miqat (Dhul-Hulayfah) or may delay to al-Juhfah. The commentator explains that it is not obligatory for the Madani to perform ihram from his own miqat; rather, he should perform ihram from the last miqat (al-Juhfah) according to the Hanafi school. However, the superior action (al-afdal) is debated: some say it is to delay, others say it is disliked (makruh) to do so. Mulla 'Ali al-Qari states that it is disliked according to the Hanafis, contradicting Ibn Amir Haj who said it is superior to delay. The text cites the matn of al-Lubab: the Madani who passes his miqat without ihram is considered to have done a disliked act, and the obligation of a dam is not required according to the corrected view. The commentator discusses reports that a person with two mawaqit on his route has a choice: the first is superior to avoid disagreement (especially with Shafi'i who requires it), but the second is a concession. It is reported from Abu Hanifah that non-Madani who pass Madinah may delay to al-Juhfah without harm, but he prefers ihram from Dhul-Hulayfah due to the sanctity of the first miqat. This indicates that Madani themselves may not be permitted to pass beyond their designated miqat. Abu Hanifah is reported to have said that if one does not perform ihram from Dhul-Hulayfah and goes to al-Juhfah, a dam is required, which is also the view of Malik and al-Shafi'i. Thus, the preferred position is that ihram from the first miqat is recommended, but delaying is permissible with a valid excuse (like fearing prohibitions).

Key Terms
المدني (al-madani): A person from Madinah (or passing through Madinah) who intends hajj. The passage uses it specifically for a resident of Madinah.
أفضل (afdal): Superior or more virtuous action. In this context, it is debated whether it is superior to delay ihram to a later miqat or to perform it at the first.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked. Here, Mulla 'Ali al-Qari states that it is makruh for a Madani to pass his miqat without ihram and delay to al-Juhfah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, if a Madani passes Dhul-Hulayfah without ihram and performs ihram at al-Juhfah, what is the ruling?
A) It is obligatory to return and perform ihram at Dhul-Hulayfah, otherwise a dam is required.
B) It is permissible but disliked, and no dam is required.
C) It is invalid and the hajj is null.
D) It is superior to do so.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a Madani to delay ihram to al-Juhfah, but recommends the first miqat; no dam required, differing from Shafi'i.

Ruling on a Medinan Passing His Miqat Without Ihram
Explains the ruling for a Medinan passing his miqat without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Medinan passing his miqat without ihram, distinguish the opinions of Ibn Amir Hajj and Mulla Ali al-Qari, and apply the reconciliation of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A Medinan may delay ihram to a later miqat, but it is disliked; blood is wajib only for Madinans.

This lesson explores a nuanced issue within the Hanafi school: what happens when a person from Medina passes his designated miqat (Dhu al-Hulayfa) without entering ihram and proceeds to a later miqat like al-Juhfa? The source text reconciles conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa and presents the relied-upon position. You will learn the practical ruling and the reasoning behind the differences among later Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is: a Medinan passes Dhu al-Hulayfa without ihram and later performs ihram from al-Juhfa. The ruling is that it is permissible but disliked; blood is required for Madinans only.
This is the mufta bihi position according to the author.
2
Map the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ibn Amir Hajj considered delaying better (afdal), while Mulla Ali al-Qari considered it disliked (makruh). The author sides with the latter, but both agree on permissibility.
The dispute is about preference, not validity.
3
Reconcile the Two Narrations from Abu Hanifa
One narration requires blood if a Medinan passes Dhu al-Hulayfa without ihram; another says no blood. The reconciliation: the obligatory blood narration applies to Madinans, the concession to non-Madinans.
This is the key talil in the text.
4
Apply the Ruling to Non-Madinans
A Syrian passing Dhu al-Hulayfa is not required to perform ihram from there; he may proceed to al-Juhfa without blood, but it is recommended to perform ihram from the first miqat.
This is derived from the general principle.
5
Consider the Practical Consequence
The practical difference: a Medinan who delays owes blood (dam). A non-Medinan does not. This thamarah al-khilaf guides fatwa.
Also note the disappearance of al-Juhfa's landmarks; precautionary ihram from Rabigh is common.

داود وقوله ولمن مربها يعني من غير أهلها وقد أفاد أنه لا يجوز مجاوزة الجميع إلا محرماً فلا يجب على المدني أن يحرم من ميقاته وإن كان هو الأفضل وإنما يجب عليه أن يحرم من آخرها عندنا ويعلم منه أن الشامي إذا مر على ذي الحليفة في ذهابه لا يلزمه الإحرام منه بالطريق الأولى وإنما يجب عليه أن يحرم من الجحفة كالمصري لكن قيل أن الجحفا قد ذهبت أعلامها ولم يبق بها إلا رسوم خفية لا يكاد يعرفها إلا سكان بعض البوادي. ولهذ والله أعلم اختار الناس الإحرام من المكان المسمى برابض، وبعضهم يجعله بالغين احتياطاً لأن قبل الجحفة بنصف مرحلة أو قريب من ذلك وقد قالوا : ومن كان في بر أو بحر لا يمر بواحا هذه المواقيت المذكورة فعليه أن يحرم إذا حاذى آخرها ويعرف بالاجتهاد وعليه أن يجتهد من : الملتقى وشارح المنية أيضاً واسمه ابراهيم قوله : ( وإن كان هو الأفضل ذكر منلا علي القاري في شرح اللباب أنه يكره وفاقاً بین علمائنا خلافاً لابن أمير حاج حيث قال : هو الأفضل ا هـ. أي الأفضل تأخير المدني إحرامه إلى الجحفة. وعبارة متن اللباب والمدني إذا جاوز وقته غير محرم كره وفي لزو. خلاف وصحح سقوطه ا هـ . وقال شارحه ولعله أشار إلى ما في النخبة أن من كان في طريق ميقاتان لا يجوز أن يتعدى إلى الثاني على الأصح فالدم يكون متفرعاً على القول المقابل للأصح لكز الأظهر أن يقال : وصحح عدم وجوبه لأن من في طريقه ميقاتان مخير في أن يحرم من الأول وهو الأفضل عند الجمهور خروجاً عن الخلاف فإنه متعين عند الشافعي، أو يحرم من الثاني فإنه رخصة له. وقيل: إنه أفضل بالنسبة إلى أكثر أرباب النسك فإنهم إذا أحرموا من الميقات الأول ارتكبوا كثيراً من المحظورات بعذر وبغيره قبل وصولهم إلى الميقات الثاني فيكون الأفضل في حقهم التأخير، وهذا لا ينافي ما في البدائع من جاوز ميقاتاً من هذه المواقيت من غير إحرام إلى ميقات آخر جاز إلا أن المستحب أن يحرم من الميقات الأول. كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال في غير أهل المدينة إذا مروا على المدينة فجاوزوها إلى الجحفة فلا بأس بذلك وأحب إلي أن يحرموا من ذي الحليفة لأنهم لما وصلوا إلى الميقات الأول لزمهم محافظة حرمته فيكره لهم تركها ا هـ . ومثله ذكره القدوري في شرحه وبه قال عطاء وبعض المالكية والحنابلة ووجه عدم التنافي أن حكم الاستحباب المذكور ونظراً إلى الأحوط خروجاً عن الخلاف وللمسارعة والمبادرة إلى الطاعة، وأن قوله الأفضل التأخير» بناء على فساد الزمان ومكاثرة مباشرة ،العصيان ومثله قولهم التقديم على الميقات أفضل حتى السلف : من إتمام الحج الإحرام من دويرة أهله لكنه مقيد بمن يكون مأموناً عن الوقوع في محظورات إحرامه إلا أن في قول أبي حنيفة في غير أهل المدينة إشارة إلى أن أهل المدينة ليس لهم أن يجاوزوا عن ميقاتهم المعين لهم على لسان الشرع وبه يجمع بين الروايتين المختلفتين عن أبي حنيفة، فعنه أنه لو لم يحرم من ذي الحليفة وأحرم من الجحفة أن عليه دماً وبه قال مالك والشافعي وأحمد، وعنه ما سبق من قوله لا بأس فتحمل رواية وجوب الدم على المدنيين وعدمه على غيرهم والله أعلم ا هـ .
Book of Hajj. So it is the miqat of the people of Yemen, a place south of Mecca, a mountain of Tihama, two marhalas from Mecca. This is the intended meaning of his statement 'for its people and these miqats except Dhat Irq are confirmed in the two Sahihs, and Dhat Irq in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.' And his statement 'and for whoever passes them' means from other than its people. And he explained that it is not permissible to pass any of them except in ihram. So it is not obligatory for a Medinan to perform ihram from his miqat, although that is better; rather, he must perform ihram from the last of them according to us. And it is known from this that if a Syrian passes by Dhu al-Hulayfa on his way, he is not obliged to perform ihram from it a fortiori; rather, he must perform ihram from al-Juhfa like the Egyptian. But it is said that the landmarks of al-Juhfa have disappeared and only faint traces remain, known only to some Bedouins. Therefore, people have chosen to perform ihram from the place called Rabid, and some call it (with ghayn) as a precaution because it is half a marhala or close before al-Juhfa. And they said: Whoever is on land or sea and does not pass any of these mentioned miqats, then he must perform ihram when he is parallel to the last of them, determined by ijtihad. And he must exert ijtihad. From: al-Multaqa and Sharh al-Muniya also, its name is Ibrahim. His statement: 'And although it is better' – Mulla Ali al-Qari mentioned in Sharh al-Lubab that it is disliked, in agreement with our scholars, contrary to Ibn Amir Hajj who said it is better. i.e., it is better for the Medinan to delay his ihram to al-Juhfa. The text of al-Lubab: 'And the Medinan, if he passes his time without ihram, it is disliked, and regarding blood, there is a difference of opinion, and they corrected that it is dropped.' His commentator said: Perhaps he referred to what is in al-Nukhba: that whoever has two miqats on his route is not permitted to pass to the second according to the more sound view, so blood would be a consequence of the view opposite to the more sound. It is more apparent to say: They corrected that it is not obligatory because one who has two miqats on his route has a choice: to perform ihram from the first, which is better according to the majority to exit from disagreement, since it is determined for the Shafi'i, or to perform ihram from the second, which is a concession for him. And it is said that it is better for most pilgrims because if they perform ihram from the first miqat, they commit many prohibitions with or without excuse before reaching the second miqat, so delay is better for them. This does not contradict what is in al-Bada'i: 'Whoever passes one of these miqats without ihram to another miqat, it is permissible, but it is recommended to perform ihram from the first miqat.' This is narrated from Abu Hanifa, that he said regarding non-Madinans: If they pass by Medina and proceed to al-Juhfa, there is no harm in that, but I prefer that they perform ihram from Dhu al-Hulayfa because when they reached the first miqat, maintaining its sanctity is incumbent, so it is disliked to abandon it. Similarly, al-Quduri mentioned it in his commentary, and Ata' and some Malikis and Hanbalis agreed. The absence of contradiction is that the ruling of recommendation mentioned is based on being more cautious to exit disagreement and to hasten to obedience, and that the statement 'delay is better' is based on the corruption of time and the abundance of committing sins. Similarly, they said: 'Performing ihram before the miqat is better, and the Salaf said: Completing Hajj includes performing ihram from one's home town.' But this is restricted to one who is safe from falling into the prohibitions of his ihram. However, in Abu Hanifa's statement regarding non-Madinans, there is an indication that the people of Medina are not permitted to pass their designated miqat as specified by the Shari'ah, and with this, the two different narrations from Abu Hanifa are reconciled. For it is narrated from him that if he did not perform ihram from Dhu al-Hulayfa and performed ihram from al-Juhfa, he owes blood. This is also the view of Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad. And from him is what preceded, his statement 'no harm.' So the narration of obligation of blood is applied to the Madinans, and its non-obligation to others. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling for a Medinan who passes his designated miqat (Dhu al-Hulayfa) without ihram and proceeds to a later miqat (al-Juhfa). The author begins by stating the general principle that each region has its own miqat, and it is not permissible to pass any miqat except in a state of ihram. However, for a Medinan, it is not obligatory to perform ihram from his own miqat; rather, he may delay and perform ihram from the last miqat he passes, i.e., al-Juhfa. This is the Hanafi position, as opposed to the Shafi'i who require ihram from the first miqat. The better practice is to perform ihram from the first miqat, but delay is allowed. The author then discusses the difference of opinion: Ibn Amir Hajj considers delay as better, while Mulla Ali al-Qari considers it disliked (makruh). The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that delaying is makruh but does not necessitate blood except for the Madinan himself. The author reconciles two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one requiring blood for passing Dhu al-Hulayfa, and another excusing blood. The reconciliation is that the narration requiring blood applies specifically to Madinans, while the one excusing applies to others. Thus, for a non-Medinan, it is permissible to delay without blood, but it is still recommended to perform ihram from the first miqat.

Key Terms
المدني (al-Madani): A person from Medina, whose miqat is Dhu al-Hulayfa.
ميقات (miqat): Designated place for entering ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
الجحفة (al-Juhfa): The miqat for people of Sham and Egypt, located near Rabigh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled Hanafi position, a Medinan who passes Dhu al-Hulayfa without ihram and performs ihram from al-Juhfa must:
A) Offer a blood sacrifice (dam).
B) Repeat his Hajj because it is invalid.
C) Do nothing; it is perfectly acceptable.
D) Perform a sajdah sahw.

Key Takeaway
A Medinan may delay ihram to a later miqat, but it is disliked and blood is wajib; for non-Madinans, delay is permissible without blood.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Muhadha as Criterion When No Miqat is Passed
Explains that those not passing any miqat perform ihram when parallel to the last miqat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule for ihram when a pilgrim does not pass any miqat, and apply the muhadha criterion to distinguish between those who pass a miqat and those who do not.

Core Idea
Muhadha applies only when no miqat is passed; passing a miqat takes precedence.

This lesson tackles a common scenario: a pilgrim who does not pass any of the five known miqats. The Hanafi school requires such a person to perform ihram when he becomes parallel (muhadh) to the last miqat. A Shafi'i scholar objected that this would change the practice of the Egyptians and Syrians. We will unpack the Hanafi response and see why the ruling remains unchanged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
A pilgrim may either pass a miqat directly or not pass any miqat. The ruling differs for each.
Passing a miqat means physically entering its boundary.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for those not passing a miqat
Such a pilgrim must perform ihram when he is parallel (muhadh) to the last miqat, which is Qarn al-Manazil.
Muhadha is determined by ijtihad based on geography.
3
Recognize the Shafi'i objection
A Shafi'i scholar argued that according to Hanafi logic, Egyptians and Syrians should also use muhadha to Qarn, but they use al-Juhfa.
This objection challenges the consistency of the Hanafi ruling.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: First, Egyptians and Syrians actually pass al-Juhfa, so they do not rely on muhadha. Second, muhadha is approximate, and Qarn's muhadha is distant due to mountains.
Passing a miqat takes precedence over muhadha.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The established practice of Egyptians performing ihram at al-Juhfa remains valid, and the rule for others not passing any miqat is to use muhadha to the last miqat.
No change to common practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإلا فاخر المواقيت الخ) أي وإلا نقل بأن المراد بالمحاذاة المحاذاة القريبة يلزم عليه أن لا يجب على الشامي كالمصري الإحرام من الجحفة له يجوز بل مجاوزتها والإحرام بعدها حين يحاذي قرن المنازل لأنه آخر المواقيت باعتبار المحاذاة فينافي ما مر من وجوب الإحرم من الجحفة . وقوله «ذكر لي الخ» بيان لذلك مع زيادة قوله : (ذكر لي بعض أهل العلم من الشافعية) يعني به الشيخ شهاب الدين ابن حجر شارح المنهاج والشمائل وغيرهما، وكان من أجلائهم وقد أدركته في كذا في النهر. ثم قال وأقول في الجواب الثاني ما لا يخفى لأن من لا يمر على المواقيت يحرم إذا حاذى آخرها قربت المحاذاة أو بعدت قوله : ( عند عدم المرور على المواقيت) أخذ التقييد به فإذا لم يكن بحيث يحاذي فعلى مرحلتين إلى مكة. ولعل مرادهم بالمحاذاة المحاذاة القريبة من الميقات إلا فآخر المواقيت باعتبار المحاذاة قرن المنازل . ذكر لي بعض أهل العلم من الشافعية المقيمين بمكة في الحجة الرابعة للعبد الضعيف أن المحاذاة قرن المنازل ذكر لي بعض أهل العلم الشافعية المقيمين بمكة في الحجة الرابعة للعبد الضعيف أن المحاذاة حاصلة في هذا الميقات من فينبغي على مذهب الحنفية أن لا يلزم الإحرام من رابع بل من خليص القرية المعروفة فإنه حينئذ يكون محاذياً لآخر المواقيت وهو قرن فأجبته بجوابين : الأول أن إحرام المصري والشامي لم يكن بالمحاذاة وإنما هو بالمرور على الجحفة وإن لم تكن معروفة وإحرامهم قبلها احتياطاً، والمحاذاة إنما تعتبر عند عدم المرور على المواقيت الثاني أن مرادهم المحاذاة القريبة ومحاذاة القريبة ومحاذاة المارين لقرن بعيدة لأن بينهم وبينه بعض جبال والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال.
His statement: 'And otherwise, the farthest of the miqats etc.' i.e., if it is transmitted that what is meant by muhadha is approximate muhadha, then it would follow that it is not obligatory for the Syrian like the Egyptian to perform ihram from al-Juhfa; rather, he may pass it and perform ihram after it when he is parallel to Qarn al-Manazil, because it is the farthest miqat in terms of muhadha. This would contradict what has passed about the obligation of ihram from al-Juhfa. His statement: 'It was mentioned to me etc.' is an explanation of that with an addition. His statement: 'A scholar from the Shafi'iyyah mentioned to me' meaning by that Shaykh Shihab al-Din Ibn Hajar, the commentator on al-Minhaj and al-Shama'il and others, and he was from their great ones, and I met him in such-and-such in al-Nahr. Then he said: And I say in the second answer what is not hidden, because one who does not pass the miqats performs ihram when he is parallel to the last of them, whether the muhadha is close or far. His statement: 'in the case of not passing the miqats' he took the restriction from it. Then: 'If he is not in a position to be parallel, then he does so at two marhalas from Mecca.' Perhaps their intention with muhadha is approximate muhadha from the miqat, except that the farthest miqat in terms of muhadha is Qarn al-Manazil. A shaykh from the Shafi'iyyah residing in Mecca related to me in the fourth Hajj of the weak servant that the muhadha of Qarn al-Manazil, he said: A shaykh from the Shafi'iyyah residing in Mecca related to me in the fourth Hajj of the weak servant that muhadha is present at this miqat, so according to the Hanafi school, one should not be required to perform ihram from Rabid but from Khulays, the known village, because then he would be parallel to the last miqat, which is Qarn. So I answered him with two answers: first, that the ihram of the Egyptian and Syrian is not by muhadha but by passing al-Juhfa, even if it is not known, and their ihram before it is precautionary; muhadha is only considered when not passing the miqats. Second, that their intention is approximate muhadha, and the muhadha of those passing by Qarn is distant because there are mountains between them. And Allah knows the true reality.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a person who does not pass any of the known miqats. The Hanafi position is that such a person must perform ihram when he is parallel (muhadh) to the last miqat. The author explains that 'the last miqat' in terms of muhadha is Qarn al-Manazil. A Shafi'i scholar suggested that if a person is not passing by al-Juhfa, the Hanafi view would lead to performing ihram from Khulays rather than from Rabid because Khulays is parallel to Qarn. The author refutes this with two points: first, Egyptians and Syrians perform ihram from al-Juhfa because they pass by it, not by muhadha; their ihram before al-Juhfa is precautionary. Second, the muhadha intended is approximate, and the muhadha for those passing by Qarn is distant due to intervening mountains. Thus, the established practice remains valid.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhādha): Being parallel to a miqat; used as a criterion for those not passing the miqat directly.
قرن المنازل (Qarn al-Manāzil): The miqat for people of Najd, considered the farthest miqat in terms of muhadha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the criterion for determining ihram location for a person who does not pass any of the five miqats?
A) He must travel to the nearest miqat.
B) He must perform ihram when parallel to the last miqat.
C) He may enter Mecca without ihram.
D) He must perform ihram at the closest miqat from his location.

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, muhadha is a valid criterion only for those not passing any miqat; passing a miqat takes precedence.
